рдЗрджрд╛рдиреАрдВ рдпрд╛рджреГрд╢рдВ рдирд╛рдо рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдВ рддрдиреН рдирд┐рдпрдордпрддрд┐ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реВрдкрддреЛ рд╜рд░реНрдерддрд╢реН рдЪ ред

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

One should perform the тАШnaming,тАЩ тАШN─Бmadheya,тАЩ of the child on the tenth or the twelfth day.

No significance is meant to be attached to the sense of the causative affix in тАШK─Бrayet,тАЩ should have it done.тАЩ For the Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtra simply saysтАФтАШOn the tenth day the father should take up the child and perform his namingтАЩ (without the causal form).

The term тАШN─БmadheyaтАЩ means simply тАШn─Бma,тАЩ тАШnameтАЩ; and it is that word by which a person is called during life.

In as much as the section has started with the mentiou of the тАШJ─Бtakarma,тАЩ as to be done тАШbefore the cutting of the umbilical cord,тАЩ it follows that the тАШtenthтАЩ and тАШtwelfthтАЩ (of the Text) refer to the day as counted from the day of birth; and they do not refer to the lunar dates.

On this point some people have held that the mention of the тАШtenth dayтАЩ is only meant to indicate the тАШpassing of the days of impurityтАЩ; the past-participle epithet тАШat─лt─Бy─Бm,тАЩ тАШhaving passed,тАЩ being understood. So that the meaning is that, тАШfor the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa the Naming should be done after the lapse of the tenth day, for the Kс╣гatriya after the lapse of the twelfth day, and for the Vai┼Ыya after the lapse of the fifteenth day.тАЩ

This explanation, however, is not right. For there being no ground for taking the words in the indirect figurative sense suggested, the ceremony could very well be performed during the period of impurity, just like the тАШBirth-rite.тАЩ If the feeding of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зas were enjoined (as a necessary accompaniment of the с╣Ъte), then there might be some justification for the suggested figurative interpretation.

If the тАШtenthтАЩ or the тАШtwelfthтАЩ day happen to fulfil the conditions mentioned in the second line of the verse, then the ceremony should be done on those days. Otherwise it should be performed on some other auspicious lunar date.

The тАШauspicious lunar datesтАЩ are the, the fifth (day of the lunar month), and so forth.

тАШPuс╣Зya,тАЩ тАШauspicious,тАЩ means commended. The ninth, fourteenth and such other days (of the lunar month),тАФwhich are commonly called тАШRikt─Б,тАЩтАФare тАШnot commended,тАЩ тАШinauspicious.тАЩ

тАШMuh┼лrta,тАЩ тАШmoment,тАЩ stands for what is called тАШlagnaтАЩ (the point of time indicated by the тАШcontact with the Horizon,тАЩ i.e., the тАШrising,тАЩ of a particular Zodiacal Sign), Aquarius, and the rest. тАШAt a moment that is auspicious,тАЩтАФi.e., which is not possessed by any evil planet, which is looked upon by Jupiter and Venus. Such тАШauspiciousnessтАЩ of the moment can be ascertained with the help of the science of Astrology.

тАШUnder a propitious lunar asterism,тАЩтАФthe тАШare those beginning with ┼Ъraviс╣гс╣нh─Б; and that day on which these happen to be тАШpropitious.тАЩ The тАШpropitiousnessтАЩ of the Lunar Asterism consists in its being free from the contact of тАШmalignantтАЩ and тАШevilтАЩ planets, as also from the condition of тАШVyat─лp─БtaтАЩ (a malignant aspect of the Sun and the Moon).

The particle тАШV─БтАЩ in the Text has a collective sense (meaning тАШandтАЩ); hence the meaning is that тАШthe ceremony should he performed on an auspicious day, and at an auspicious moment, and under a faultless lunar asterism.тАЩ The due combination of all these conditions can be ascertained with the help of the Science of Astrology.

The final upshot of the whole comes to this:тАФThe ceremony should never be performed before the tenth or twelfth day,тАФand after these days it may be performed only at the auspicious moment on that day which is found to be under a propitious lunar asterism.тАЩтАФ(30)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

тАШDa┼Ыamy─Бm dv─Бda┼Ыy─БmтАЩтАФтАШThe tenth of twelfth day of the monthтАЩтАФMedh─Бtithi, who also notes and rejects the explanationтАФтАШafter the lapse of the tenth or twelfth dayтАФi.e., тАШon the lapsing of the period of impurityтАЩтАФwhich is accepted by Kull┼лka.

This verse is quoted in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 233) where it notes the latter explanation and says that it has been rejected by Medh─Бtithi and Apar─Бrka. It is curious that having the work of Medh─Бtithi before him, the author of V─лramitrodaya did not note his explanation that the ceremony is to be performed on the 10th or 12th day (tithi) of the month.

The verse is quoted in Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 855) also, where however no explanation is givenтАФand in Nirс╣Зayasindhu (p. 371), where it is added that what is meant is that the naming of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa should be done on the expiry of the tenth day, of the Kс╣гatriya on the expiry of the twelfth day, of the Vai┼Ыya on the expiry of the sixteenth day and of the Shudra on the expiry of the twenty-first day;тАФand the second half of the verse lays down substitutes.

This verse is quoted in Saс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (p. 24), which adds that тАШda┼Ыamy─БmтАЩ has been taken as тАШda┼Ыamy─Бm a├▒t─БyamтАЩ, тАШafter the lapse of the tenth dayтАЩ,тАФthat no significance attaches to the causal affix in тАШk─БrayetтАЩ;тАФin Saс╣Гsk─Бс╣Ыaratnam─Бl─Б (p. 850), which adds that the causal affix in тАШk─БrayetтАЩ has the reflexive sense;тАФin Nс╣Ыsiс╣Гhapras─Бda (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 34a);тАФand in Sс╣Ыmticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 52), which explains meaning as тАШon the tenth day from the day of the birth, the father should do the namingтАЩ, it being the fatherтАЩs business to do this.

Viс╣гс╣Зu-Smс╣Ыti, 27.5.тАФтАШThe naming should be done after the lapse of the period of impurity.тАЩ

Y─Бj├▒avalkya, 1.12.тАФтАШThe naming on the eleventh day.тАЩ ─А┼Ыval─Бyana (Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtr─Б, 1.4).тАФтАШThey should give him a name.тАЩ

P─Бraskara (Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtr─Б, 1.17.11).тАФтАШOn the tenth day, the father should take him up, and after having fed the Br─Бhmaс╣Зas, should perform the naming ceremony.тАЩ

Gobhila (Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtr─Б, 2.7.7).тАФтАШOn the expiry of ten days, or hundred days, or a year, after birth, the Naming.тАЩ

Jyotirva┼Ыiс╣гс╣нha (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 231).тАФтАШThe naming of the boy should be done either on the day of birth, or on the twelfth day, or in special cases, on the tenth day.тАЩ

Mahe┼Ыvara (Ibid).тАФтАШThe J─Бtakarma and the naming of the boy should he done either by the father or brothers at the time of birth; or on the twelfth day from birth, or on the first day.тАЩ

[The naming on the day of birth refers to the imparting of a secret name, which is done along with the J─Бtakarma; see above.]

Viс╣гс╣Зu-pur─Бс╣Зa (Ibid).тАФтАШThe father should do the naming on the tenth day.тАЩ

Vy─Бsa (Ibid).тАФтАШSome wise men hold that the naming is to be done on the tenth day; others mention the twelfth day; and yet others hold that it should be done after the lapse of one full month.тАЩ

N─Бrada (Do.)тАФтАШFrom the birth, on the tenth day, or the twelfth day, is performed the naming of Br─Бhmaс╣Зas; of the other two castes, it is on the expiry of the period of impurity;тАФso also for ┼Ъ┼лdras; hut some people hold that the naming of the ┼Ъ┼лdra should be done on the thirty-first day.тАЩ

┼Ъaс╣Еkha (Do.)тАФтАШThe naming has been prescribed as to be done on the lapse of the period of impurity.тАЩ

Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нha (Do.)тАФтАШThe naming is prescribed as to be done on the tenth or the twelfth dav.тАЩ

Bс╣Ыhaspati (Do.)тАФтАШThe naming should he done, for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, on the tenth or tho twelfth day; for the Kс╣гatriya on the thirteenth day; for the Vai┼Ыya on the sixteenth day; and for the ┼Ъ┼лdra either on the nineteenth (v. l. twentieth) or the thirty-second (v. l. twenty-second) day.тАЩ

Mah─Бbh─Бrata (Do.)тАФтАШThe naming of the twice-born castes should be done on the twelfth, the sixteenth, the twentieth and the twenty-second day respectively; for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa it may be done on the tenth also.тАЩ

Bhaviс╣гyapur─Бс╣Зa (Do.)тАФтАШOn the expiry of the twelfth night, or, according to others, on the expiry of one month, or, according to others, on the eighteenth day.тАЩ

[Thus we find that the choice lies among the following daysтАФthe day of birth, tenth, eleventh, twelfth, thirteenth, sixteenth, eighteenth, nineteenth, twenty-second, thirty-first, hundred and first and the end of a year.]

As regards the тАШpuс╣Зya tithi, muh┼лrta and nakс╣гatraтАЩ the reader is referred to the V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, pp. 234-237.

  • рдПрд╡рдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░ рджреНрд░рд╖реНрдЯрд╡реНрдпрдореН ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪрд╛рдиреНрд╡рд┐рддрд╛рджрд┐рд╢рдмреНрджрдкреНрд░рдпреЛрдЧреЛ рдмрд▓рд╛рдиреНрд╡рд┐рддрдВ рдзрдирд╕рдВрдпреБрдХреНрддрдореН рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЗрддрд░рдерд╛ рдПрд╡рдореН рдПрд╡рд╛рд╡рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрджреН “рдмрд▓рдирд╛рдорд╛рдирд┐ рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рддреН” рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╕реНрд╡рд▓реНрдкрддреНрд╡рд╛рджреН рдмрд▓рд╛рджреНрдпрд░реНрдерд╡рд╛рдЪрд┐рдирд╛рдореН35 рдЖрдирдиреНрддреНрдпрд╛рдЪреН рдЪ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рд╡реНрдпрдХреНрддреАрдирд╛рдВ рджреБрд░рд╡рдзрд╛рдиреЗ рднреЗрджреЗ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░реЛрдЪреНрдЫреЗрдж рдПрд╡ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН ред

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The Author now proceeds to determine the form of the name to be given to the child.

тАШMaс╣Еgalyam,тАЩ тАШauspicious,тАЩ means тАШmaс╣Еgal─Бya hitam,тАЩ or тАШmaс╣Еgal─Бya s─Бdhu,тАЩ тАШconducive to welfare.тАЩ The тАШwelfareтАЩ meant here is that which consists in the fulfilment of something desirable, in the shape of longevity, wealth and such other things as lead to physical and mental pleasure. And a term can be said to be тАШconducive,тАЩтАФтАШhitaтАЩ or тАШs─Бdhu,тАЩтАФto this welfare, only when it connotes it; and it is in this sense that we have the Nominal Affix (тАШyat,тАЩ in тАШmaс╣ЕgalyamтАЩ). Further, by being тАШconduciveтАЩ it is not meant that it should always express the actual fulfilment of a desirable thing; but that it may also express the desirable thing itself.

This connotation of the desirable thing may be either (a) by means of compounds, such as тАШ─Бyuс╕еsiddhiтАЩ (accomplishment, of longevity), тАШdhanasiddhiтАЩ (acquisition of wealth), тАШputral─БhhaтАЩ (obtaining of a son), and so forth,тАФor (b) by a nominal affix connoting тАШconducivenessтАЩ тАШeffectiveness,тАЩ or тАШpurpose.тАЩ But the Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtra has prohibited the use of a name ending in a Nominal affixтАФтАШOne should fix a name ending with a Verbal, not one with a nominal affixтАЩтАФsays P─Бraskara. And as for compounds also, there is a combination of the denotations of two words; so that there is a chance of the name consisting of many letters; the lext is going to lay down certain appendages to the actual names, such as тАШthe name of Br─Бhmaс╣Зa should end in ┼Ъarman, and so forthтАЩ (Manu, 2.32); so that if the name consists of three or four letters, along with the appendage тАШ┼Ыarman,тАЩ it would oome to consist of five or six letters; and this would go against the rule that тАШthe name should consist of two or four letters.тАЩ (Baudh─Бyana and ─Аpastamba). From all this it follows that such words should he employed as names as are connotative of things that are desired by most people,тАФe.g., son, cattle, landed property, daughter, wealth and so forth; and these should end with the term тАШ**┼Ыarman.тАЩ Thus it is that such names become possible as тАШGo-┼Ыarman.тАЩ тАШDhana-┼Ыarman,тАЩ тАШHiraс╣Зya-┼Ыarman,тАЩ тАШKaly─Бс╣Зa-┼Ыarman,тАЩ тАШMaс╣Еgala-┼Ыarman,тАЩ and so on.

Or, the term тАШmaс╣ЕgalaтАЩ may be taken as standing for тАШDharma,тАЩ тАШMeritтАЩ; and тАШmaс╣ЕgalyaтАЩ in that case would mean that which is conducive to merit (meritorious).

тАЬWhat is it that is conducive to merit?тАЭ

All those words that constitute the names of Deities; e.g., тАШIndra,тАЩ тАШAgni,тАЩ тАШV─Бy┼лтАЩ; also the names of sagesтАФe.g., тАШVasiс╣гс╣нha,тАЩ тАШVi┼Ыv─Бmiс╣нra,тАЩ тАШMedh─БtithiтАЩ; these latter also are тАШconducive to meritтАЩ; as is clearly indicated by such directions asтАФ(a) тАШone should make offerings to the sages,тАЩ (b) тАШone should meditate upon the men of pious deeds,тАЩ тАШone who desires prosperity should, on rising in the morning, repeat the names of Deities, sages and of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зas of pious deeds.тАЩ

The epithet тАШmangalya,тАЩ тАШauspiciousтАЩ (meritorious) serves to preclude all тАШinauspiciousтАЩ names, such as тАШYama,тАЩ тАШMс╣ЫtyuтАЩ and the like; and also those that are meaninglessтАФsuch, as тАШс╕МitthaтАЩ and the like.

тАШThat of the Kс╣гatriya connected with power,тАЩтАФi.e., expressive of power. The тАШanvayaтАЩ (expressed by тАШanvitaтАЩ in the compound тАШbal─БnvitaтАЩ means connection; and the only connection that a word can have with a thing is the relation, of being connotative of it.тАФтАШPowerтАЩ is strength; and the word, that connotes this should be used as the name for the Kс╣гatriya,e.g., тАШ┼Ъatruntapa,тАЩ тАШDuryodhana,тАЩ тАШPraj─Бp─Бla.тАЩ The several kinds of names have been mentioned (in the text), as indicative of the several castes.

Similarly, тАШthat of the Vai┼Ыya Associated with wealth.тАЩ It is not meant that only synonyms of тАШdhanaтАЩ should be used,тАФsuch as тАШDhanaтАЩ тАШVitta,тАЩ тАШSv─Бpateya,тАЩтАФbut that any word that may be in any way connotative of wealth should be used. Or, what is meant is that either such words as тАШdhanaтАЩ (тАШwealthтАЩ) and the like should be used, or such as signify connection with wealth; such as тАШDhanakarman,тАЩ тАШMah─Бdhana,тАЩ тАШGoman,тАЩ тАШDh─Бnyag?aha.тАЩ

Throughout this verse, such is the meaningтАФof the term тАШconnected with powerтАЩ and тАШassociated with wealth.тАЩ If this were not what is meant, the text would have said simply тАШthe names of power should be used.тАЩ And in that case, since the words actually denotative of power would be very few in number, while the number of individuals to be named would be endless,тАФall usage (based oh names) would come to an end.

тАШThat of the ┼Ъ┼лdra contemptible,тАЩтАФsuch as тАШKс╣Ыpaс╣Зaka,тАЩ тАШD─лna,тАЩ тАШ┼Ъavaraka,тАЩ and so forth.тАФ(31)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in Gad─Бdharapaddhati (K─Бlas─Бra, p. 217);тАФin Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 53) to the effect that the names of the four castes should consist of words expressive respectively, of welfare, strength, wealth and deprecation;тАФin Nс╣Ыsiс╣Гhapras─Бda (Saс╣Гsk─Бra p. 346);тАФand in Saс╣Гsk─Бra-may┼лkha (p. 25).

BurnellтАФтАШThis is now obsolete. The names of the different castes are now usually epithets or titles of some favourite deity. The caste is known only by the suffixed title.тАЩ

This verse has been quoted in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Б ra, p. 242), where we have the following explanations: тАШmaс╣ЕgalyamтАЩ means expressive of auspiciousness; e.g., the name тАШLakс╣гm─лdharaтАЩ;тАФтАШBal─БnvitamтАЩ means expressive of bravery, e.g., the name тАШYudhiс╣гс╣нhira;тАЩтАФтАШdhanasamyuktamтАЩ, means containing terms expressive of wealth; e.g., the name тАШMah─БdhanaтАЩ;тАФтАШjugupsitamтАЩ means containing a term denoting depreciation; e.g., the name тАШNarad─БsaтАЩ.

Madanap─Бrij─Бta also quotes this verse (on p. 357), where it is explained to mean that тАШthe names should be expressive of auspiciousness and the restтАЩ

Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 441) quotes it as also the four typical names asтАФтАШ┼Ъr─л ┼Ъarm─БтАЩ тАШVikramap─БloтАЩ, M─Бс╣Зikya┼Ыreс╣гс╣нhi and H─лnad─Бsa;тАФit is quoted in Apar─Бrka (p. 27) as laying down rules regarding the first part of the name.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

┼Ъaс╣Еkha (Smс╣Ыti, 2.3).тАФтАШThe name of all castes should consist of an even number of letters; an auspicious one for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, one endowed with strength for the Kс╣гatriya.тАЩ

Viс╣гс╣Зu (Smс╣Ыti, 1.27.6-9).тАФтАШThe Br─Бhmaс╣ЗaтАЩs name should be expressive of auspiciousnessтАФthe Kс╣гatriyaтАЩs expressive of strength,тАФthe Vai┼ЫyaтАЩs expressive of wealth,тАФthe ┼Ъ┼лdraтАЩs expressive of depreciation.тАЩ

V─лramitrodaya (┼Ъaс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 237).тАФNames are of four kinds;

  1. connected with family-deity,
  2. connected with month,
  3. connected with asterism,
  4. and temporal.

(a) Says ┼Ъaс╣Еkha.тАФтАШThe father should fix a name connected with the family-deity,тАЩ i.e., a name consisting of words expressive of the Deity.

(b) G─Бrgya.тАФтАШThe father should impart to the hoy the name of the month and the name of the preceptor. The months have been declared to have the following names:тАФ

  1. M─Бrga┼Ы─лrс╣гaтАФKс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa,
  2. Pauс╣гaтАФAnanta,
  3. M─БghaтАФAchyuta,
  4. Ph─БlgunaтАФChakr─л,
  5. CaitraтАФVaikuс╣Зс╣нha,
  6. Vai┼Ы─Бkha,тАФJan─Бrdana,
  7. Jyaiс╣гс╣нha,тАФUpendra,
  8. ─Ас╣г─Бс╕НhaтАФYaj├▒apuruс╣гa.

  10. Bh─БdraтАФHari,
  11. ─А┼ЫvinaтАФYog─л┼Ыa,
  12. K─БrttikaтАФPuс╣Зс╕Нar─лk─Бkс╣гa.тАЩ

(c) ┼Ъaс╣Еkha-Likhita.тАФтАШEither the father or some other senior member of the family should fix a name connected with the asterism.тАЩ This name has been held to be the one to be used when the person bearing the name accosts a superior.

Says Baudh─БyanaтАФтАШThis name in accordance with the asterism is the secret one, which is known only to the father and the mother and which the boy is to use in accosting.тАЩ

Also ─А┼Ыval─БyanaтАФтАШThe accosting name should be known only to the father and the mother; as it is under this name that the boy is initiated.тАЩ

Also ┼Ъaunaka, тАШThat name under which he is to be initiated, and by which he will do the accosting of the teacher,тАФshould also be fixed at the time of the naming ceremony. This accostive name should be pronounced by the father very silently, so that others may not know it. This initiative name the parents should bear in mind.тАЩ

Like the names attached to the months the names attached to the asterisms are as follows:тАФ

  1. Agni (Kс╣Ыttik─Б),
  2. Praj─Бpati (Rohiс╣З─л),
  3. Soma (Mс╣Ыga┼Ыiras),
  4. Rudra (─Аrdr─Б),
  5. Diti (Punarvas┼л),
  6. Bс╣Ыhaspati (Puс╣гv─Б),
  7. Sarpa (A┼Ыleс╣г─Б),
  8. Pitс╣Ы (Magh─Б),
  9. Bhaga (Purvaphalgun─л),
  10. Aryam─Б (Uttaraphalgun─л),
  11. Savitс╣Ы (Hast─Б),
  12. Tvaс╣гtс╣Ы (Chitr─Б),
  13. ─Аyuс╣г (Sv─Бt─л),
  14. Indra-Agni (Vi┼Ы─Бkh─Б),
  15. Mitra (Anur─Бdh─Б),
  16. Indra (Jyeс╣гс╣нh─Б),
  17. Nirс╣Ыti (M┼лl─Б),
  18. Apas (P┼лrv─Бс╣г─Бс╕Нh─Б),
  19. Vi┼Ыvedevas (Uttar─Бс╣г─Бс╕Нh─Б),
  20. Viс╣гс╣Зu (┼Ъravaс╣З─Б),
  21. Vasu (Dhaniс╣гс╣нh─Б),
  22. Varuс╣Зa (┼Ъatabhiс╣гa),
  23. Ajaikap─Бt (P┼лrvabh─Бdra),
  24. Ahirbudhnya (Uttarabh─Бdra),
  25. P┼лс╣гan (Revat─л),
  26. A┼Ыvins (A┼Ыvin─л),
  27. Yama (Bharaс╣З─л).

But according to Baudh─Бyana, the тАЬname connected with the asterismтАЭ is in accordance with the names of the asterisms themselvesтАФsuch as тАШRohiс╣З─л,тАЩ тАШBharaс╣З─л,тАЩ and the rest; and not in accordance with the name of the deity attached to each asterism. According to the astrologers however each asterism has four letters assigned to it (such as ch┼л-che-cho-la, assigned to A┼Ыvin─л, and so forth, and тАЬthe name connected with the asterism of A┼Ыvin─л,тАЭ would be the name whose first letter consists of one of these four letters).

(d) The тАШtemporal nameтАЩ has been described by Bс╣Ыhaspati as тАШconducive to all kinds of business.тАЩ It is this name that has been laid down by ─А┼Ыval─Бyana as having for its first letter one of the ghoс╣гa-letters, in its middle one of the antastha letters; ending with the visarga, containing either two or four vowels; and in male names the number of letters should always be even.

But Baijav─БpaтАФтАШThe father fixes the name, which consists of either two or three or four letters, or of unlimited number of letters.тАЩ

Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нhaтАФтАШThe name should consist of either two or four vowels, but those ending in l or r should be avoided.тАЩ

The Mah─Бbh─Бс╣гyaтАФтАШThe first letter of the name should be ghoс╣гa-vat, the middle one of the antastha letters, it should not be similar to the names of the ancestors, or of the enemy; it should be one formed with a verbal affix, not with a nominal affix.тАЩ

─А┼Ыval─БyanaтАФтАШThat name is best which consists of either four or two letters, which is in consonance with that of the grandfatherтАЩ (this last includes also the gods).

Kapila-Saс╣Гhit─БтАФтАШOn the eleventh day, in due form, the name should be given, which is in consonance with the family-custom, and resembles the name of the gods or of the parents.тАЩ

Baijav─Бpa (Apar─Бrka, p. 27).тАФтАШThe father gives a name either of one letter or two letters or three letters or four letters, or of letters without limit; it should be one formed with a verbal, never with a nominal, affix.тАЩ

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

[What appears to be the meaning is that] the actual term (тАШ┼Ыarman,тАЩ etc.) should form part of the name,тАФand that the two terms (mentioned in the preceding and the present verse) should appear in the order stated, the тАШauspiciousтАЩ term coming at the beginning and the term тАШ┼ЫarmanтАЩ at the end (of the name),тАФas illustrated above (тАШGo-┼Ыarman,тАЩ тАШDhana-┼ЫarmanтАЩ and so forth).

But this would not be possible in regard to the names of the Kс╣гatriya and the rest; because the term тАШrakс╣г─Б.тАЩ (тАШsecurity,тАЩ which is mentioned in connection with the Kс╣гatriya) is of the feminine gender, and as such could not be co-ordinated with the names of males. Hence in view of conformity, and in view also of actual practice, and also in view of the two verses being syntactically distinct, we should take them as complementary to each other; the sense being that the тАШauspicious nameтАЩ (mentioned in the preceding verse) should he тАШexpressive of ┼Ыarman, PeaceтАЩтАФthis term standing for refuge, shelter, happiness. It is only if we take the term тАШ┼ЫarmanтАЩ of the text as standing for what is developed by it, that we have the possibility of names ending in тАШsv─Бm┼л,тАЩ тАШdatta,тАЩ тАШbh┼лti,тАЩ and the rest; the name тАШIndrasv─Бm─лтАЩ meaning тАШhe who has Indra for his shelterтАЩ; тАШIndra-dattaтАЩ also signifies the fact of Indra being the shelter.

Similarly with all the rest (the names of the Kс╣гatriya, etc.)

тАЬWhat does this argument meanтАФthat, in view of the two verses being syntactically distinct, we should take them as complementary to each other? Por the same reason, why are not the two sentences тАШone should sacrifice with Vr─лhiтАЩ and тАШone should sacrifice with YavaтАЩ taken as complementary (and not as optional alternatives, as they have been taken)?тАЭ

What we have said is only what is indicated (by the words of the Text). The Text being the work of a human writer, if he had intended the statements to be optional alternatives, he should, for the sake of brevity, have said тАШthe name should be either auspicious or expressive of peaceтАЩ; when we have two distinct syntactical constructions, there are two verbs, and this becomes too prolix (and the prolixity cannot be justified except by taking the two as complementary). [All this reason ng, based upon intention and propriety of speech, cannot apply to the case of Vedic sentences, where there is no author.]

тАШRakс╣г─Б,тАЩ is тАШprotection,тАЩ тАШpreservation.тАЩ

тАШPuс╣гс╣нiтАЩ is тАШprosperityтАЩ as well as тАШsecurity.тАЩ Such names as тАШGovс╣ЫddhaтАЩ тАШDhanagupta.тАЩ

тАШPreс╣гyaтАЩ is тАШsubmissiveтАЩ; such names as тАШBr─Бhmaс╣Зa-d─Бsa,тАЩ and тАШDevad─Бsa,тАЩ which means (respectively) тАШsubmissive to, dependent upon, the Br─Бhmaс╣ЗaтАЩ and тАШsubmissive to and dependent upon a deity.тАЩтАФ(32)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 243) also; and in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra. p. 55) as laying down the subsidiary titles of the four caste-names;тАФalso in Vidh─Бnap─Бrij─Бta (p. 309);тАФand in Nirс╣Зayasindhu (p. 178).

Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdс╕еava (─Аc─Бra, p. 441) quoting the verse explains it to mean that тАШ┼ЫarmanтАЩ must be the suffixed word to the Br─Бhmaс╣ЗaтАЩs name.

N─Бrayaс╣Зa and R─Бghav─Бnanda opine that the name of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa must always contain the word тАШ┼ЫarmanтАЩ itself. But Medh─Бtithi and several others hold that the name should connote what is connoted by the term тАШ┼Ыarman.тАЩ

The present day practice, however, follows the former explanationтАФтАШ┼ЫarmanтАЩ.being regarded now as the suffixed title to every Br─Бhmaс╣ЗaтАЩs name.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

P─Бraskara-Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtr─Б, 1. 17.4.тАФтАШ┼Ъarma for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, Varma for the Kс╣гatriya, Gupta for the Vai┼Ыya.тАЩ

Yama-Smс╣Ыti (Do.).тАФтАШ┼Ъarma and Deva for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, R─Бj─Б for the Kс╣гatriya, Gupta and Datta for the Vai┼Ыya and D─Бsa for the ┼Ъ┼лdra.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

Inasmuch as significance has been attached to the mention of the тАШmaleтАЩ child (in verse 29), what has been said in the preceding verses is not applicable to women; and the present verse is going to lay down rules regarding the names of women.

тАШEasily pronouncibleтАЩ;тАФthat which can be easily pronounced; the name of women should be such as can be uttered, with ease, even by women and children. It is mostly women and children that have got to deal with women; and the womanтАЩs organ of speech being not very efficient, she cannot pronounce each and every Sanskrit word; hence the Text lays stress upon this pronouncibility in the case of feminine names. This however docs not mean that the masculine names may be unpronouncible. As examples of тАШpronouncibleтАЩ names wo have, тАШMaс╣Еgala-dev─л,тАЩ тАШCh─Бrudati,тАЩ тАШSuvadan─Б,тАЩ etc., and as counter-examples (i.e., of unpronouncible names), тАШ┼Ъarmiс╣гс╣нh─Б,тАЩ тАШSu┼Ыliс╣гс╣н─Бс╣Еg─л,тАЩ and the like.

тАШNot harsh,тАЩтАФi.e., not denoting any thing harsh; names denoting harsh things are such as тАШс╕М─Бkin─лтАЩ (Sorceress), тАШParuс╣г─БтАЩ (Rough) and so forth.

тАШOf plain meaning,тАЩтАФwhose moaning does not need to be explained before it is comprehended; which, as soon as it is heard, couveys its meaning to the learned and the unlearned alike. As examples of names with meanings not plain, we have, (a) тАШK─Бmaniс╕Нh─БтАЩ and (b) тАШK─Бriс╣гagandh─лтАЩ; the meaning of these terms is not comprehended until the following explanations have been provided:тАФ(a) тАШwho is, as if it were, the very receptacle of love, she in whom all love is contained,тАЩ and (b) тАШK─Бr─лс╣гagandh─лтАЩ is the тАШdaughter of Kariс╣гagandhi.тАЩ

тАШHeart-captivating,тАЩтАФthat which pleases the mind; e.g., тАШ┼Ъreyas─лтАЩ; while of the contrary kind we have the name тАШK─Бl─Бkс╣г─л.тАЩ

тАШAuspicious,тАЩтАФsuch as тАШ┼Ъarmavat─лтАЩ; of the contrary kind is the name тАШAbh─Бg─Б,тАЩ тАШM andabh─Бg─Б.тАЩ тАШEnding in a long vowel,тАЩтАФthat which has a long vowel at the end. Contrary to this is the name тАШ┼Ъarat.тАЩ

тАШ─А┼Ы─лrv─БdaтАЩ is that which denotes benediction; тАШabhidh─БnaтАЩ is term; and when the two are compounded in tho dh─Бraya form, we get the meaning тАШbenedictory termтАЩ; and the name that contains such a term is called тАШ─Б┼Ы─лrv─Бd─Бbhidh─Бnavat,тАЩ тАШcontaining a benedictory term.тАЩ Examples of such namesтАФтАШSaputr─Б,тАЩ тАШBahuputr─Б,тАЩ тАШKulav─Бhik─БтАЩ; these are benedictory names; of the contrary kind are such names as, тАШApra┼Ыast─Б,тАЩ тАШAlakс╣гaс╣З─Б.тАЩ

тАЬWhat is the difference between тАШauspiciousтАЩ and тАШbenedictoryтАЩ?тАЭ

None whatsoever. The second epithet has been added only for the purpose of filling up the metre.тАФ(33)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 441), which cites the typical female name тАШ┼Ъr─лd─Бs─л.тАЩ

This is quoted also in Smс╣Ыtitattva (p. 631).

V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 243) quotes the verse, and having explained the words, cites as examplesтАФтАШYa┼Ыod─БтАЩ (easily pronouncible) тАШKulaghn─лтАЩ (harsh)тАФтАШIndir─БтАЩ (not of plain meaning)тАФтАШKamah─лy─БтАЩ (heart-captivating)тАФтАШSubhadr─БтАЩ (auspicious)тАФand тАШSaubh─Бgyavat─лтАЩ (containing a benedictory term).

Vidh─Бnap─Бrij─Бta (p. 310) simply quotes the verse;тАФand Apar─Бrka (p. 27) quotes it as laying down rules regarding the first part of female names.

This is quoted in Smс╣Ыti candrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 55), which adds the following notesтАФтАШsukhodyam,тАЩ easily pronouncible,тАФтАШmaс╣ЕgalyamтАЩ denoting auspiciousness;тАФтАШd─лrghavarс╣Зa, the long ─л. or ─Б.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

Laghu┼Ы─Бt─Бtapa, 35.тАФтАШThe girl should not be named after a river or an asterism or a tree; nor should she have a terrifying name.тАЩ

─А┼Ыval─Бyana-Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtra, 1.15.9.тАФтАШThe names of girls should consist of an odd number of letters.тАЩ

┼Ъaunaka (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 213).тАФтАШThe name of males should contain even, and of females odd, number of letters.тАЩ

Baijav─Бpa (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 243).тАФтАШThe name of the woman should consist of three letters and should end in the long ─л.тАЩ

─А┼Ыval─Бyana (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 243).тАФтАШThe name of males should contain an even number of letters, and of females odd number of letters.тАЩ

B├╝hler

033 The names of women should be easy to pronounce, not imply anything dreadful, possess a plain meaning, be pleasing and auspicious, end in long vowels, and contain a word of benediction.

In the fourth month should be performed the ceremony of the childтАЩs тАШEgressтАЩ from the room; and in the sixth month the ceremony of тАШFeedingтАЩ; or, whatever might be regarded as auspicious in the family.тАФ(34)

рдореЗрдзрд╛рддрд┐рдерд┐рдГ

рдЬрдиреНрдордЪрддреБрд░реНрдердорд╛рд╕реЗ рдЧреГрд╣рд╛рджреН рдмрд╣рд┐рд░реН рдирд┐рд╖реНрдХреНрд░рдордгрдореН рдЖрджрд┐рддреНрдпрджрд░реНрд╢рдирдВ рд╢рд┐рд╢реЛрд░реН рдмрд╛рд▓рд╕реНрдп рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдореН ред рддреНрд░реАрдиреН рдорд╛рд╕рд╛рдиреН рдЧрд░реНрднрдЧреГрд╣ рдПрд╡ рд╡рд╛рд╕рдпреЗрддреН ред рд╢рд┐рд╢реБрдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгрдВ рд╢реВрджреНрд░рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдкрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердореН ред рдПрд╡рдВ рд╖рд╖реНрдареЗ рдорд╛рд╢реНрдпреН рдЕрдкреНрдпреН рдЕрдиреНрдирдкреНрд░рд╛рд╢рдирдореН ред рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдорд╛рд╕рд╛рдиреН рдХреНрд╖реАрд░рд╛рд╣рд╛рд░ рдПрд╡ ред рдпрджреН рд╡рд╛ рдХреБрд▓реЗ рджрд╛рд░рдХрд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрд░реЗрдпрд╕реНрдпрдВ рдордЩреНрдЧрд▓реНрдпрдВ рдкреВрддрдирд╛ рд╢рдХреБрдирд┐рдХреИрдХрд╡реГрдХреНрд╖реЛрдкрд╣рд╛рд░рд╛рджрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдореН ред рдХрд╛рд▓рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖реЗ рд╡рд╛ рддрддреН рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдореН ред рдЕрдпрдВ рдЪ рд╕рдВрд╕реНрдХрд╛рд░рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ ред рддреЗрди рдирд╛рдордзреЗрдпрдореН рдЙрдХреНрддрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╡реНрдпрддрд┐рд░реЗрдХреЗрдгрд╛рдкрд┐ рдпрдерд╛рдХреБрд▓рдзрд░реНрдордВ рд▓рднреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдореА рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╢рд░реНрдорд╛ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рднреВрдорд┐рдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдШреЛрд╖ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд░рд╛рдд рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдгреБрдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рджреЗрд╡ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдЬреНрдпреЛрддрд┐рдГ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░рдпрд╢рд╛ рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ рдХреБрд▓рднреЗрджреЗрдиреЛрдкрдкрдиреНрдирдВ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рее реи.рейрек рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШIn the fourth monthтАЩтАФfrom birthтАФтАШshould be performed the ceremony of the childтАЩs egressтАЩтАФbeing taken out of the room and shown the sun. This implies that for three months the child should he kept in the lying-in room itself.

The common name тАШchildтАЩ is used, with a view to include the ┼Ы┼лdra also.

Similarly тАШin the sixth month,тАЩ the ceremony of First Feeding on grains. For five months the child should he kept purely on milk.

тАШOr, whatever might be regarded as auspiciousтАЩтАФconducive to welfareтАФтАШin the familyтАЩ of the child; such well-known rites, for instance, as making offerings to P┼лс╣нan─Б, to ┼Ъakunika, to certain trees, etc., etc. This may he done at specified times.

This last clause is meant to apply to all ceremonies; so that the naming also may he done according to family custom, even though it be not in strict conformity with the rules laid down above. Hence with different families, such names become possible asтАФтАШIndrasv─Бm─л,тАЩ тАШIndra┼ЫarmanтАЩ тАШIndrabh┼лti,тАЩ тАШIndrar─Бta,тАЩ Indraviс╣гс╣Зu,тАЩ тАШIndradeva,тАЩ тАШIndrajyotiс╣г,тАЩ тАШIndraya┼Ыaс╣г,тАЩ and so forth.тАФ(34)

тАШYadveс╣гс╣нam maс╣Еgalam kuleтАЩтАФMedh─Бtithi, along with Govindar─Бja and Kull┼лka, takes this as applicable to all the sacraments.тАФтАШKulaтАЩ is family, not tribe.

The first half of the verse is quoted in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 442), and the second half in Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 360) and in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 267), which latter remarks that this option regarding family-custom applies only to the sacrament of the First Feeding. The verse is quoted in

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШC┼лс╕Н─БтАЩ is the tuft of hair on the crown of the beadтАЩ; and the ceremony for the purpose of this is called тАШ**C┼лс╕Н─Бkarman,тАЩ тАШTonsureтАЩ; this name тАШTonsureтАЩ is given to that ceremony which consists in the cutting of the hair in such a manner as to leave well-arranged tufts of hair on certain parts of the head.

This may be done тАШin the first year or the thirdтАЩ;тАФthis option being due to considerations of the good and evil aspects of planets.

тАШIn view of the injunctions of the VedaтАЩ:тАФthis is merely explanatory: the fact of the entire contents of the work being based upon the Veda having been already stated before. Or, the term may he taken here as not necessarily standing for the injunctive texts, but including the Mantras also; and as a matter of fact, we have the mantra, тАШyatkс╣гureс╣Зa m─Бrjayet, etc.,тАЩ (P─Бraskara-gс╣Ыhyas┼лtra, 2.1.1), which is indicative of the Tonsure-ceremony, in the same manner as the Mantra тАШy─Б├▒jan─Б pratinandanti, etc.,тАЩ (P─Бraskara,тАФ3.2.2) indicates the Aс╣гс╣нak─Б-rites. So that what the phrase means is that the ceremony should be performed with mantras. As to the particular details (regarding the mantras, etc.), these are learnt from the Gс╣Ыyhas┼лtra.

From this it follows that this sacrament is not to he done for the ┼Ъ┼лdra; which is also clear from the mention of the тАШtwice-born.тАЩ As for the shaving of hair without any restriction as to time, this is done for special purposes, and may he done for the ┼Ъ┼лdra also: this is not interdicted.тАФ(35)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

тАШDharmataс╕етАЩтАФтАШaccording to LawтАЩ (N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa and Nandana);тАФтАШfor the sake of spiritual meritтАЩ (Kull┼лka).

This verse has been quoted in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 605) for the purpose of showing that even a boy who has not cut his teeth can be тАШone who has had Ids Tonsure performed.тАЩ

It is quoted in Smс╣Ыti-tattva (p. 653)тАФwhich points out that the time most suited for the ceremony is the third, not the first year and it bases this on the distinct declaration by ┼Ъaс╣Еkha thatтАФтАШfor the rite of Tonsure, the third year is what has been accepted by all the Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtras.тАЩ It also quotes it on p. 922, with a view to show that the time for the ceremony is not fixed, there being an option as to its being done in the first, third, or even the fifth year.

It is quoted in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 296), where it is explained that the presence of the particle тАШv─Б,тАЩ тАШorтАЩ, implies that the rite may be performed in the second year also; this latter is also sanctioned by a text from Yama.

Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 34) also quotes it without adding any explanatory notes.тАФIt is quoted in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 58);тАФin Hem─Бdri (Pari┼Ыeс╣гa, p. 742);тАФin Saс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (pp. 29 and 128), which quotes Medh─Бtithi to the effect that the term тАШdvij─Бt─лn─БmтАЩ indicates that this rite is not to be performed for the Shudra.;тАФin Nс╣Ыsiс╣Гhapras─Бda (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 36c); and in Gad─Бdharapaddhati (K─Бlas─Бra, p. 219).

Medh─Бtithi has described this ceremony as that тАШwhich consists in the cutting of the hair in such a manner as to leave well-arranged tufts of hair on certain parts of the head.тАЩ

Further details have heen supplied in Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 361), which quotes Lok─Бkс╣гi (called Laug─Бkс╣гi in Smс╣Ыtitattva, p. 653) describing the тАШ**C┼лс╕Н─БтАЩas тАШa line of hair, towards the right among the Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нhas, on both sides among the Airis and K─Б┼Ыyapas, and in five places among the ─Ас╣Еgirasas; some people keep a single line; others only the top-tuft, shaped like the leaf of the banyan treeтАФand adds that the exact form is to be determined by the Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtra, of the man concerned.

[The upshot of the whole is that Tonsure may he performed during any of the following yearsтАФ1st, 3rd, 5th, 7th, 10th, 11th,тАФor on the Upanayana-day;тАФor according to the custom prevailing in the family.]

┼Ъaс╣Еkha (Do.).тАФтАШTonsure during the third or the fifth vear.тАЩ

┼Ъaunaka (Do.).тАФтАШTonsure during the third year, or according to the family-custom.тАЩ

Lok─Бkс╣гi (Do.).тАФтАШFor those belonging to the Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нha Gotra, the tuft is towards the right, for those of Atri or K─Б┼Ы-yapa, on both sides; for those of Bhс╣Ыgu, it should be all shaven; for those of Aс╣Еgiras, there are five tufts; others have the tuft in the form of a semi-circle.тАЩ

┼Ъaс╣Еkha-Likhita (Apar─Бrka, p. 29).тАФтАШTonsure during the third or the fifth year.тАЩ

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

Counting from the year that one spends in the motherтАЩs womb, when the child reaches the eighth year;тАФthe term тАШgarbhaтАЩ stands for the year spent in the womb; this indication being due to the presence of the term тАШyear,тАЩ тАШabdaтАЩ; certainly the тАШyearтАЩ could never be the тАШeighthтАЩ from тАШgarbha,тАЩ if this latter were taken in its direct sense;тАФin this year one should perform the Initiation of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa.

The term тАШaupan─БyanamтАЩ stands for тАШupamyanam,тАЩ the тАШaс╣ЗтАЩ affix having the reflexive sense; and the lengthening of the vowel in the latter term (тАШnayanamтАЩ) being in accordance with (P─Бс╣Зini 6.3.198); or the lengthening of the vowels of both terms (тАШupaтАЩ and тАШnayanamтАЩ) may be regarded as a Vedic anomaly.

тАШUpanayana,тАЩ тАШInitiation,тАЩ is the name of a sacrament described in the Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtras and well-known to Vedic scholars, its other name is тАШMau├▒j─л-bandha,тАЩ тАШGirdle-Investiture.тАЩ That ceremony in which the child is taken over toтАФmade over toтАФ(upan─лyate)тАФthe teacher, for the purposes of teachingтАФand not for any such other purpose as the building of a Avail, or the making of a matтАФis what is called тАШUpanayana.тАЩ It is the name of a particular sacramental rite.

тАШOf the King in the eleventh year from conceptionтАЩ;тАФfor the Kс╣гatс╣нriya the ceremony should be performed in the eleventh year тАШfrom conception,тАЩтАФi.e., тАШbeginning from conception,тАЩ or тАШafter conception.тАЩ

The term тАШkingтАЩ тАШr─БjanтАЩ (in тАШr─Бj├▒aс╕етАЩ) should he taken as standing for the Kс╣гatriya caste; and does not necessarily mean one who is a duly anointed king; firstly because such is the sense in which the word is generally used in books; secondly because in the present context it occurs along with the terms тАШBr─Бhmaс╣ЗaтАЩ and the rest (which are all denotative of castes); and thirdly because we find the term тАШKс╣гatriyaтАЩ used in the rules that follow regarding the details of the ceremony; e.g., it is raid that тАШthe girdle of the Kс╣гatriya should consist of the bow-stringтАЩ (below, Verse 12). It is true that the term тАШkingтАЩ is sometimes used in the sense of the тАШrulersтАЩ of тАШcountries,тАЩ and as such applied to Vai┼Ыyas and other castes also; but such usage is purely figurative and indirect. And the figurative meaning of a word can be accepted only when the original direct meaning is found inapplicable. That the term тАШkingтАЩ in the text stands for the Kс╣гatriya is shown by the following words of the author of the Gс╣Ыhya-sutraтАФтАШOne should initiate the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa in the eighth year, the Kс╣гatriya in the eleventh and the Vai┼Ыya in the twefth.тАЩ It is on this understanding that the revered P─Бс╣Зini derives the word тАШr─БjyaтАЩ (тАШKingshipтАЩ) from the word тАШr─БjanтАЩ (King), explaining it as тАШthe function the King,тАЩ and hence used in the ordinary sense of тАШlord of countryтАЩ [ i.e., the тАШfunction of ruling a countryтАЩ really belongs to the Kс╣гatriya caste, and when persons of other castes arc called тАШKingтАЩ their title is based upon their doing тАШthe work of the KingтАЩ].

Of the Vai┼Ыya, the ceremony should be performed in the twelfth year from conception.тАФ(86)

This verse is quoted in Hem─Бdri (Pari┼Ыeс╣гa, p. 745);тАФin Gad─Бdharapaddhati (K─Бlas─Бra, p. 220), which explains that тАЬUpanayana is to be derived as тАШNayanam evan─БyanamтАЩ and then the prefix тАШUpaтАЩ added;тАФin Saс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (p. 32);тАФand in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 68), which adds that in the case of the Kс╣гatriya and the Vai┼Ыya also the years are to be counted from the one spent in the womb.

It has been quoted in Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 17); and in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 446).

V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 344) explains the reason for the eighth, eleventh and twelfth years being regarded as the best for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, the Kс╣гatriya and the Vai┼Ыya respectively. The G─Бyatr─л mantra is sacred for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa and its foot contains eight syllables; the Triс╣гtup for the Kс╣гatriya contains a foot of eleven syllables, and the Jagati for the Vai┼Ыya has a foot of twelve syllables.

036 In the eighth year after conception, one should perform the initiation (upanayana) of a Brahmana, in the eleventh after conception (that) of a Kshatriya, but in the twelfth that of a Vaisya.

For the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa desirous of Brahmic glory, it should be done in the fifth year; for the тАШKingтАЩ desirous of power, in the sixth; and for the Vai┼Ыya desirous of business, in the eighth.тАФ(37)

  • рдмрд▓рдВ рд╕рд╛рдорд░реНрдереНрдпрдореН рдЖрднреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░рдВ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордВ рдЪ ред рдЙрддреНрд╕рд╛рд╣рд╢рдХреНрддрд┐рд░реН рдорд╣рд╛рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрддрд╛ рдЪреЗрддреНрдпреН рдПрддрджреН45 рдЖрднреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░рдореН, рдмрд╛рд╣реНрдпрдВ рдЪ рд╣рд╕реНрддреНрдпрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдердкрджрд╛рддрд┐рдХреЛрд╢рд╕рдВрдкрддреН ред рддрджреН рдЙрдХреНрддрдореН- “рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдЩреНрдЧрд╛рднреНрдпреБрдЪреНрдЪрдпрдВ рд╕рд╛рдВрдпреМрдЧрд┐рдХрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдирд╛рдореН” (рдирд┐рд░реН рез.реи) рдЗрддрд┐ ред

  • рдИрд╣рд╛ рдЪреЗрд╖реНрдЯрд╛ ред рдмрд╣реБрдирд╛ рдзрдиреЗрди рдХреГрд╖рд┐рд╡рд╛рдгрд┐рдЬреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╣рд╛рд░рдГ ред

  • рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░ рдЧрд░реНрднрд╛рджрд┐рд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛ рдЪ46 рд╡рд░реНрд╖рд╛рдгрд╛рдореН, рдЧрд░реНрднрд╛рджреН рдЗрддрд┐ рд╣реНрдпреН рдЕрдиреБрд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ рее реи.рейрен рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

What belongs to the father is here attributed to the child; the desireтАФтАШMay my sou attain Brahmic glory!тАЩтАФresides in the father; and this desire being attributed to the child, the latter is spoken of as тАШdesirous of Brahmic glory.тАЩ The child itself is too youug to have the said desire.

тАЬIn that case the action done by one person would have its result accruing to a totally different person; and this would involve the absurdity of a man acquiring what he has not earned. And the assertion that the result accrues to the child without his desiring it is one that is contrary to all reason and scriptural authority.тАЭ

There is no force in the objection. The case in question is analogous to that of the ┼Ъyena sacrifice: the ┼Ъyena is performed by a man seekiug to encompass death, and this death falls upon the person against whom the performance is aimed (and not on the performer himself). It might be argued thatтАФтАЬin this case the result actually accrues to the person seekiug for it; it is the sacrificer who desires the death of his enemy; and it is he who obtains this result; so that the result of the act does not accrue to a person that did not perform it.тАЭтАФBut in the present case also, the result, in the shape of тАШhaving a child with the particular qualification,тАЩ accrues to the performer of the Initiation (the father); just as the good health of the child brings pleasure to the father, so also the Brahmic glory of the son would be a source of pleasure to the father; so that the result here also would accrue to the performer, who had sought for it. Further, it is only from the construction of the actual words used that we can ascertain the meaning of the scriptural texts; and in the present context, the only construction found possible is that the father should perform the ceremony with the desire of a certain result to accrue to his son; and there are no grounds for abandoning this natural construction of the words.

This same explanation applies also to the case of the benefits of the after-death rites accruing to the father (even though performed by the son); as in that case also the performer is the son, and the result is the satisfaction of the father. Further, we have the textтАФтАШThou art my very self called the. nonтАЩтАФwhich shows that when the after-death rites are performed by the son, it is the father himself (iс╣З the shape of the son) that makes the offerings to himself; specially as it was with a view to this alone that the father begot the son.

Then again, in the Sarvasv─Бra sacrifice (which is performed by one who wishes to bring about his own death and translation to heaven),тАФeven after the sacrificer himself has died, the subsequent details have got to he performed: and in this performance also the same sacrificer is regarded as the тАШperformer,тАЩ in view of the direction that he has given fo the Br─Бhmaс╣ЗasтАФтАШO br─Бhmaс╣Зas, please complete this sacrifice,тАЩтАФas also of the sacrificial gifts and appointments made by him; by virtue of which the said sacrificer is regarded as the actual instigator or employer of the officiating priests. In the same manner, in the case in question also, in as much as the son was begotten for the purpose of performing the funeral rites, these rites, though performed (by the son) for the sake of the father, are regarded as performed by the father himself.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

Medh─Бtithi (p. 90, 1. 15)тАФтАШSarvasv─БreтАЩтАФSee M─лm─Бс╣Гs─Б S┼лtra 10.2.56-57. At the Sarvasv─Бra sacrifice the sacrificer recites the ─Аrbhaya hymn just before he enters the fire for self-immolation,

This verse is quoted in Apar─Бrka (p. 27) as laying down the time for the performance of the Upanayaс╣Зa with special ends in view.

It is quoted in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 446), which quotes ─Аpastamba as connecting The seventh year with тАШBr─Бhmic glory,тАЩ the eighth with тАШlongevity,тАЩ the ninth with тАШsplendour,тАЩ the tenth with тАШfoodтАЩ, the eleventh with тАШefficiency of organs,тАЩ and the twelfth with тАШcattleтАЩ.

Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 17) quotes it mentioning the said assertions.

It is quoted in Hem─Бdri (Pari┼Ыeс╣гa, p. 748);тАФin Saс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (p. 12), as mentioning special results to be achieved;тАФin Nс╣Ыsiс╣Гhapras─Бda (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 41 b); and in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 68).

V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 345) quotes it as describing the K─Бmya options.

Nirс╣Зayasindhu (p. 184) quotes it without comment.

Gautama-Dharmas┼лtra, 1.7-8.тАФтАШWhen special results are desired, during the ninth or the fifth year.тАЩ

─Аpastamba-Dharmas┼лtra, 1.21-26.тАФтАШDuring the seventh year, if Br─Бhmic glory is desired for the boy; during the eighth year, if longevity is desired; during the ninth year, if brilliance is desired; during the tenth year, if possession of much food is desired; during the eleventh year, if efficiency of sense-organs is desired; during the twelfth year, if possession of cattle is desired.тАЩ

U┼Ыanas (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 315).тАФтАШThe Upanayana of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa should be done during the fifth year from birth, of the Kс╣гatriya during the sixth, and of the Vai┼Ыya during the seventh year,тАФif strength is desired.тАЩ

Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нha (V─лra-Saс╣Гskara, p. 345).тАФтАШFor the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa if Br─Бhmic glory is desired, his Upanayana should be performed during the eighth year (either from conception or from birth); if food is desired, during the ninth year; if intelligence is desired, during the tenth year: if possession of jewels is desired, during the eleventh year; if bodily stoutness is desired, during the twelfth year.тАЩ

Aс╣Еgiras (Do., p. 346).тАФтАШFor the Kс╣гatriya desiring prosperity or strength, it should be performed during the sixth or the twelfth year, respectively; for the Vai┼Ыya desiring success in agriculture or longevity, it should be performed during the eighth or fourth year, respectively.тАЩ

Baudh─Бyana (Do., p. 346).тАФтАШDuring the seventh year, if Br─Бhmic glory is desired; during the eighth, if longevity is desired; during the ninth, if brilliance is desired; during the tenth, if food is desired; during the eleventh, if efficient sense-organs are desired; during the twelfth, if cattle is desired; during the thirteenth, if intelligence is desired; during the fourteenth, if stoutness is desired; during the fifteenth, if the birth of a brotherтАЩs son is desired; and during the sixteenth, if all desirable things are desired.тАЩ

B├╝hler

037 (The initiation) of a Brahmana who desires proficiency in sacred learning should take place in the fifth (year after conception), (that) of a Kshatriya who wishes to become powerful in the sixth, (and that) of a Vaisya who longs for (success in his) business in the eighth.

For the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa the S─Бvitr─л does not lapse till the sixteenth year; for the Kс╣гatriya till the twenty-second year; and for the Vai┼Ыya till the twenty-fourth year.тАФ(38)

рдПрд╡рдВ рддрд╛рд╡рдиреН рдореБрдЦреНрдпрдХрд╛рдореНрдпрд╛рд╡реН рдЙрдкрдирдпрдирдХрд╛рд▓рд╛рд╡реН рдЙрдХреНрддреМ ред рдЗрджрд╛рдиреАрдВ рдкрд┐рддреБрд░реН рдЕрднрд╛рд╡реЗ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ рд╡рд╛ рдХрдердВрдЪрд┐рджреН рдЕрдиреБрдкрдиреАрддреЗ рдорд╛рдгрд╡рдХреЗ рдХрд╛рд▓рд╛рддрд┐рдкрддреНрддрд╛рд╡реН рдЕрдиреБрдкрдиреЗрдпрддрд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд╛, рд╕рддреНрдпреН рдЕрдкрд┐ рдХрд╛рд▓рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЩреНрдЧрддреНрд╡реЗ рддрджрднрд╛рд╡реЗ рд╜рдзрд┐рдХрд╛рд░рдирд┐рд╡реГрддреНрддреЗрдГ,47 рдпрдерд╛ рд╕рд╛рдпрдВрдкреНрд░рд╛рддрдГрдХрд╛рд▓рд╛рддрд┐рдкрддреНрддрд╛рд╡реН рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рд╣реЛрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдХрд░рдгреЗ ред рдЕрддреЛ рд╡рд┐рд╣рд┐рддрдХрд╛рд▓рд╡реНрдпрддрд┐рд░реЗрдХреЗрдг рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкреНрд░рд╕рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердореН рдЗрджрдореН рдЖрд░рднреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдпрд╛рд╡рддреН рд╖реН┼Нрдбрд╢рдВ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рдВ рдЧрд░реНрднрд╛рджреН рдЖрд░рднреНрдп рддрд╛рд╡рджреН рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрд╕реНрдпреЛрдкрдирдпрдирд░реНрд╣рддрд╛ рди рдирд┐рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ ред рд╕рд╛рд╡рд┐рддреНрд░реАрд╢рдмреНрджреЗрди рддрджрдиреБрд╡рдЪрдирд╕рд╛рдзрдирдореН рдЙрдкрдирдпрдирд╛рдЦреНрдпрдВ рдХрд░реНрдо рд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрддреЗ ред рдирд╛рддрд┐рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ рдирд╛рддрд┐рдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддрдХрд╛рд▓рдВ рднрд╡рддреАрддреНрдпреН рдЕрд░реНрдердГ ред

  • рдПрд╡рдореН рдЖ рджреНрд╡рд╛рд╡рд┐рдВрд╢рд╛рддреН рдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рдмрдиреНрдзреЛрдГ рдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рд┐рдпрдЬрд╛рддреАрдпрд╕реНрдпреЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрд░реНрдердГ ред рдмрдиреНрдзреБрд╢рдмреНрджреЛ рд╜рдпрдВ рдХреНрд╡рдЪрд┐рддреН рдХреБрддреНрд╕рд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ ред рдпрддреН рд╕реНрд╡рдВ рдХрдердВ рд╡реЗрддреНрд╕48 рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордмрдиреНрдз49 рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рддрд┐рд╡рдЪрдирдГ рдпрдерд╛,

  • рд▓рд┐рдЩреНрдЧрджрд░реНрд╢рдирдВ рдЪреЛрджрд╛рд╣рд░рдиреНрддрд┐ ред “рдЧрд╛рдпрддреНрд░реНрдпрд╛ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдореН рдЙрдкрдирдпреАрдд, рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрднрд╛ рд░рд╛рдЬрдиреНрдпрдореН, рдЬрдЧрддреНрдпрд╛ рд╡реИрд╢реНрдпрдореН” рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдПрддреЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдЪ рдЫрдВрджрд╕рд╛рдореН рдЗрдпрддрд╛ рдХрд╛рд▓реЗрди рджреНрд╡реМ рдкрд╛рджреМ рдкреВрд░реНрдпреЗрддреЗ ред рддрд╛рд╡рдиреНрддрдВ рдХрд╛рд▓рдВ рдмрд▓рд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рди рддреНрдпрдЬрдиреНрддрд┐ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рд╢реНрд░рдпрднреВрддрд╛рдиреН рд╡рд░реНрдгрд╛рдиреН ред рддреГрддреАрдпреЗ рддреБ рдкрд╛рджреЗ рд╜рдкрдХреНрд░рд╛рдиреНрддреЗ рдЧрддрд░рд╕рд╛рдиреНрдпреН рдЕрддрд┐рд╡рдпрд╛рдВрд╕рд┐ рдиреНрдпреВрдирд╕рд╛рдорд░реНрдереНрдпрд╛рдирд┐ рднрд╡рдиреНрддрд┐ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрд┐рдореН рдЙрдкрдпрд╛рдиреНрддрд┐ ред рдпрдерд╛ “рдкрдЮреНрдЪрд╢рддрд╛ рд╕реНрдерд╡рд┐рд░реЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпрдГ” рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЕрддрд╢реН рдЪ рдиреИрддреЗрди рд╡рдпрдореН рдЙрдкрд╛рд╕рд┐рддрд╛рдиреАрддрд┐ рддреНрдпрдЬрдиреНрддрд┐ рддрдВ рд╡рд░реНрдгрдореН ред рддрддреЛ “рди рдЧрд╛рдпрддреНрд░реЛ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгреЛ, рди рддреНрд░реИрд╖реНрдЯреБрднреЛ рд░рд╛рдЬрдиреНрдпреЛ, рди рдЬрд╛рдЧрддреЛ рд╡реИрд╢реНрдпрдГ” рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛ рдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛ рдЛрдЪрдГ рд╕рд╛ рд╕рд╡рд┐рддреНрд░реАрдГ; рд╕рд╛ рдЪ рдЧрд╛рдпрддреНрд░реА рджреНрд░рд╖реНрдЯрд╡реНрдпрд╛ рдкреНрд░рджрд░реНрд╢рд┐рддрд╛, рдЧреГрд╣реНрдпрд╛рдЪреН рдЪ ред рдПрд╡рдВ рдХреНрд╖рддреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╕реНрдп рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реНрдЯреБрдкреН рд╕рд╛рд╡рд┐рддреНрд░реА “рдЖрдХреГрд╖реНрдгреЗрди” (рд░реНрд╡реН рез.рейрел.реи) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рд╡реИрд╢реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдЬрдЧрддреА “рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛ рд░реВрдкрд╛рдгрд┐” (рд░реНрд╡реН рел.реорез.реи) рдЗрддрд┐ рее реи.рейрео рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

For the Initiatory Rite, the principal as well as the optional time have been prescribed. From this it would seem that if, on account of the death of the father, or by reason of illness and such other causes, the boy remains uninitiated and the prescribed time has gone by,тАФhe becomes unfit, for initiation; this idea being countenanced by the faot that, even though the prescribed time is a secondary factor in the rite, yet on the lapse of that time, the performerтАЩs title to the performance ceases; just as we find in the case of omission of the Agnihotra -offerings after the prescribed morning and evening have gone by. It is with a view to this that the present verse propounds an exception to the general rule, and lays down the necessity of performing the rite even after the passing off of the prescribed time.

Till the end of the sixteenth year after conception, the Br─Бhmaс╣ЗaтАЩs title to the Initiatory Bite does not cease. The term тАШS─Бvitr─лтАЩ in the text stands for the тАШRite of Initiation,тАЩ which is the means whereby the teaching of the is accomplished. тАШDoes not lapse,тАЩ i.e., does not become out of date.

Similarly тАШfor the Kс╣гatriya till the twenty-second year,тАЩтАФi.e., for the person belonging to the Kс╣гatriya caste. Tho term тАШbandhuтАЩ is used (a) sometimes in a deprecatory sense; e.g., in such passages asтАФтАШhow doth thou know this. O Brahma-bandhu! (wretched Br─Бhmaс╣Зa)?тАЩ;тАФ(b) sometimes it is used in the sense of тАШfamilyтАЩ; e.g., in the passageтАФтАШthe possession of a number of villages, the presence of a large following, extensive family-connections (), and alliances,тАФthese are not to be trifled with even by Indra himself; what to say of persons possessing only parts of the earth!тАЩ;тАФ(c) in some cases it also means тАШsubstanceтАЩ; e.g., in P─Бс╣Зiс╣ЗiтАЩs Sutra (5.4.9)тАФтАШa word ending with the term j─Бс╣нi takes the affix ca, when it denotes bandhu (i.e., a substance belonging to a particular class).тАЩ In the present context the first two meanings of the term тАШbandhuтАЩ being inapplicable, we take it in the third sense.

The nominal affix (с╕Нaс╣н) in the term тАШdv─Бviс╣Г┼Ыaс╕етАЩ means that which completes the number twenty-two, i.e., the twenty-second.

тАШFor the Vai┼Ыya till the twenty-fourth yearтАЩ.тАФHere also though the presence of the тАШс╕Нaс╣нтАЩ-affix implying completion was necessary, yet it has not been used in view of metrical contingencies; but the sense is there all the same. That this must be so is proved by the fact that the number тАШtwenty-four,тАЩ which denotes the entire lot of twenty-four years, could never form the limit of anything; while tine тАШtwenty-fourth year’ which is one part of the тАШtwenty-four,тАЩ can very well form the limit.

People explain the particle тАШ─БтАЩ as denoting inclusion.

In support of what is said in this verse people cite the Vedic textтАФтАШThe Br─Бhmaс╣Зa should be initiated with the G─Бyatr─л, the Kс╣гatriya with the and the Vai┼Ыya with the Jagat─лтАЩ [the G─Бyatr─л metre containing 24, three times eight, the Tс╣Ыс╣гtup 33, three times eleven, and the Jagat─л, 48, four times twelve, syllables]; the ages spoken of in the text (16, 22 and 24) suffice to complete two quarters of each of the three metres; up till then the metres retain their force and do с╣Зot abandon the castes that form their receptacles; when however the third quarter has passed, they lose their essence, become aged and having their force reduced, they disappaer, just as the man becomes old at 50 (which represents two quarters of his life of 100 years). It is for this reason that the said metres abandon their respective castes, when they find that they have not been studied by them; and it is thus that (after the said ages) the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa ceases to be тАШrelated to the G─Бyatr─л,тАЩ the Kс╣гatriya ceases to be тАШrelated to the Triс╣гс╣нupтАЩ and the Vai┼Ыya ceases to be тАШrelated to the Jagat─л.тАЩ

тАШS─Бvitr─лтАЩтАФis the name of that verse which has for its deity; and that such a verse is the G─Бyatr─л has been shown above, on the strength of the Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtras.

For the Kс╣гatriya, the тАШS─Бvitr─лтАЩ is the verse тАШ─Аkс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зena, etc.тАЩ (с╣Ъgveda, 1.35-2; V─Бjasaneya, 33.43), which is in the Triс╣гс╣нup metre; and for the Vai┼Ыya, it is the verse тАШVi┼Ыv─Б r┼лp─Бс╣Зi, etc.тАЩ с╣Ъgveda, 5.81.2; V─Бjasaneya, 12.3).тАФ(38)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

Burnell, in applying the name тАШvr─БtyaтАЩ to тАШAryans not Br─Бhmanised,тАЩ should have quoted his authorities.

Kull┼лka notes that some people have taken the particle тАШ─Б,тАЩ тАШtill,тАЩ in the sense of тАШuntil the beginning ofтАЩ.

This verse has been quoted in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 342), where it is pointed out that the тАШsixteenthтАЩ and other years mentioned here should be counted тАШfrom conception,тАЩ as in the case of the eighth and others in verse 36. It points out that this verse lays down the many secondary occasions for the performance of the ceremony.

This same work on p. 344, refers to the passage in Medh─Бtithi, where a Vedic text is quoted, which connects. the G─Бyatr─л Triс╣гс╣нup and Jagati metres with the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, the Kс╣гatriya and the Vai┼Ыya respectively; and as under 36, so here also, it explains that the limits fixed in this verse too are determined by the number of syllables in a foot of each of the three metres mentioned. A foot of the g─Бyatr─л has eight syllables; so till the bс╣Зy is sixteen years old, the G─Бyatr─л retains more than a third of its force; and it is only when the boy has passed his sixteenth year (corresponding to the sixteen syllables of the two feet of the G─Бyatr─л) that the force of the mantra becomes weakened. Similarly twenty two years correspond to the twenty-two syllables of the two feet of the Triс╣гс╣нup, sacred for the Kс╣гatriya, and twenty four years correspond to the twenty four syllables of the first two feet of the Jagati metre, sacred for the Vai┼Ыya.

It is quoted in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 446); and in Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 36) as the outside age-limit for Upanayana;тАФin Hem─Бdri (Pari┼Ыeс╣гa, p. 751), which adds that тАШ─БтАЩ here denotes limit;тАФin Nс╣Ыsiс╣Гhapras─Бda (Saс╣Гsk─Бra. p. 41b);тАФand in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 72), as Laying down the secondary times for the initiation.

Vidh─Бnap─Бrij─Бta, (p. 471) has quoted the verse as laying down the secondary occasion for Upanayana;тАФso also Nirс╣Зayasindhu (p. 184).

**(Verse 38-39)

Viс╣гс╣Зu, 1.27.26.тАФ(Exactly the same words as in Manu.)

Gautama-Dharmas┼лtra, 1.14.16.тАФтАШFor the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, the S─Бvitr─л does not lapse till the sixteenth year; for the Kс╣гatriya, till the twenty-second year; for the Vai┼Ыya till two years longer.тАЩ

Baudh─Бyana-Dharmas┼лtra, 1.2.13.тАФтАШThere is no lapse for these till the sixteenth, the twentv-second and the twenty-fourth year, respectively.тАЩ

─Аpastamba-Dharmas┼лtra, 1.1.27.тАФтАШTill the sixteenth year there is no lapse for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa; till the twenty-second, for the Kс╣гatriya; and till the twenty-fourth, for the Vai┼Ыya; till then they would be fit for keeping the observances that we are going to describe.тАЩ

Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нha-Smс╣Ыti, 11.51.53.тАФтАШFor the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, the time does not lapse till the sixteenth year; for the Kс╣гatriya, till the twenty-second year; for the Vai┼Ыya, till the twenty-fourth year.тАЩ

─А┼Ыval─Бyana-Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtra, 1.19.5-6.тАФтАШFor the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, the time does not lapse till the sixteenth year; for the Kс╣гatriya, till the twenty-second year; for the Vai┼Ыya, till the twenty-fourth year; after this, they become lapsed from the S─Бvitr─л.тАЩ

P─Бraskara Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtra, 2.5.36-38.тАФтАШFor the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, the time does not become lapsed till the sixteenth year; for the Kс╣гatriya, till the twenty-second and for the Vai┼Ыya till the twenty-fourth year.тАЩ

Paiс╣нh─лnasi (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 3-12).тАФтАШThe twelfth, the sixteenth and the twentieth years are the times not deprecated.тАЩ

Y─Бj├▒avalkya (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 342).тАФтАШThe time for Upanayana extends up to the sixteenth, the twenty-second and the twenty-fourth year, for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, the Kс╣гatriya and the Vai┼Ыya, respectively.

Y─Бj├▒avalkya 1.38 (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 347).тАФтАШAfter these years all the three become fallen, excluded from all religious rites; and become apostates, deprived of the S─Бvitr─л, until they perform the Vr─Бtyastoma.тАЩ

Vy─Бsa (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 343).тАФтАШSixteen years, twenty-two years and twenty-four years constitute the time for Upanayana.тАЩ

┼Ъaс╣Еkha (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 343).тАФтАШSixteen years have been prescribed for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, twenty-two years for the Kс╣гatriya and twenty-four years for the Vai┼Ыya.тАЩ

Yama (V─лramitrodaya-Saihsk─Бra, p. 343).тАФтАШHe who has dropped the S─Бvitr─л for fifteen years, should keep the observance after having shaven his head along with the ┼Ъikh─Б.тАЩ

Yama (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 347).тАФтАШThe apostates, fallen from S─Бvitr─л, should be studiously shunned.тАЩ

─А┼Ыval─Бyana-Smс╣Ыti (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 343).тАФтАШSixteenth is the limit for Br─Бhmaс╣Зas for securing the status of the twice-born; twenty-second for Kс╣гatriyas; and twenty-fourth for Vai┼Ыyas.тАЩ

─А┼Ыval─Бyana-Smс╣Ыti (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 347).тАФтАШAfter this, not having acquired the status of the twice-born, they fall and become apostates, excluded from Vedic rites.тАЩ

Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нha (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 345).тАФThe Br─Бhmaс╣Зa who has passed his sixteenth year, should not have his Upanayana performed; the Kс╣гatriya after the twentieth year: and the Vai┼Ыya after the twenty-fifth year.тАЩ

┼Ъaс╣Еkha (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 347).тАФ(Has the same def├мni-tion of the тАШApostateтАЩ as Y─Бj├▒avalkya.)

038 The (time for the) Savitri (initiation) of a Brahmana does not pass until the completion of the sixteenth year (after conception), of a Kshatriya until the completion of the twenty-second, and of a Vaisya until the completion of the twenty-fourth.

рдЙрдХреНрддрдореН “рдЖрд░реНрдпреИрд░реН рдирд┐рдиреНрджрд┐рддрдГ” рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдХрд╛ рдкреБрдирд░реН рдПрд╖рд╛рдВ рдирд┐рдиреНрджреЗрддреНрдпреН рдЖрд╣ ред

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШBeyondтАЩтАФafterтАФthe said time, тАШall these threeтАЩ castesтАФthe Br─Бhmaс╣Зa and the rest;тАФтАШat the proper timeтАЩтАФat the exact time prescribed for each caste, or even at the secondary period permitted;тАФтАШnot having received the sacramentтАЩтАФnot having their Upanayana- ceremony performed;тАФтАШexcluded from S─Бvitr─лтАЩтАФbecome fallen off from Initiation; and also тАШcome to he known as Vr─БtyasтАЩтАФтАШdespised,тАЩ looked down upon, тАШby all good menтАЩ by respectable and cultured people.

This verse is intended to explain the signification of the well known name тАШVr─БtyaтАЩ That they become excluded from Initiation has already been implied in the preceding verse.

It has been said that they тАШare despised by good menтАЩ; the next verse explains the nature of contempt in which they are held.тАФ(39)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava, (─Аc─Бra, p. 446), and in Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 36), where it is explained that on the expiry of the limit mentioned in verse 38, the boy becomes a тАШVr─Бtya,тАЩ тАШapostateтАЩ, and can be invested only after having become sanctified by the performance of the Vr─Бtyastoma rite.

Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 36) goes on to add that the dumb and the insane, as never fit for the sacraments, are not to be regarded as тАШapostatesтАЩ by reason of the omission of the sacraments; so that in the event of their having children these latter do not lose their Br─Бhmaс╣Зa-hood or their right to the sacraments.

V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 347) quotes this verse as from Manu and Yama both.

  • рдХрд┐рдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрдирд┐рд╖реЗрдзрдГ ред рдиреЗрддреНрдпреН рдЖрд╣- рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдпреМрдирд╛рдВрд╢реН рдЪ ред рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдо рд╡реЗрджрдГ ред рддрдиреНрдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддрд╛рдГ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд╛ рдпрд╛рдЬрдирд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдкрдирдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдЧреНрд░рд╣рд╛рдГ52 ред рди рддреЗ рдпрд╛рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдГ рди рдпрд╛рдЬрдХрд╛рдГ рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдГ ред рдПрд╡рдВ рдирд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдпрд╛ рдиреИрддреЗрднреНрдпреЛ рд╜рдзреНрдпреЗрддрд╡реНрдпрдореН ред рд╡реЗрджрд╛рд░реНрдердВ рд╡рд┐рджреБрд╖рдГ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдЧреНрд░рд╣рд╛рдзрд┐рдХрд╛рд░рд╛рджреН рдПрд╖реЛ рд╜рдкрд┐ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдорд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзреЛ рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рдпреМрдирдГ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрдГ рдХрдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛ рджрд╛рдирд╛рджрд╛рдиреЗ ред рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгрдВ рдкреНрд░рджрд░реНрд╢рдирд╛рд░реНрдердореН ред рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдЪреН рдЪ рджреЛрд╖рджрд░реНрд╢рдирд╛рджреН рд╡реНрд░рд╛рддреНрдпрддрд╛рдкрд░рд┐рд╣рд╛рд░рд╛рд░реНрдереЗ рдкрд┐рддреБрд░реН рдЕрднрд╛рд╡реЗ рд╜рдкрд┐ рд╡реНрдпреБрддреНрдкрдиреНрдирдмреБрджреНрдзрд┐рдирд╛ рдорд╛рдгрд╡рдХреЗрдирд╛рдкреНрдпреН рдЖрддреНрдордирд╛рддреНрдореЛрдкрдирд╛рдпрдпрд┐рддрд╡реНрдп рдЗрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рддреАрдпрддреЗ ред рдХрд╛рдореНрдпреЛ рд╣реНрдпреН рдЕрдпрдореН рдЖрдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рдзрд┐рдГ ред рддрддреНрд░рд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпрддреНрд╡рдореН рдЕрдХрд╛рдордпрдорд╛рдиреЛ рдпрджрд┐ рдХрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рдиреН рди рдкрд░реНрд╡рд░реНрддрддреЗ рддрджрд╛ рдорд╛рдгрд╡рдХреЗрди рдкреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдердпрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпреЛ рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛53 ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪ рд╢реНрд░реБрддрд┐рдГ- “рд╕рддреНрдпрдХрд╛рдореЛ рдЬрд╛рдмрд╛рд▓рдГ рд╣рд╛рд░рд┐рджреНрд░реБрдорддрдВ54 рдЧреМрддрдордореН рдЗрдпрд╛рдп рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд░реНрдпрдВ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рд╡рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдорд┐” (рдЫреБ рек.рек.рей) рдЗрддрд┐, рд╕реНрд╡рдпрдореН рдЖрдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпрдореН рдЕрднреНрдпрд░реНрдерд┐рддрд╡рд╛рдиреН рдЙрдкрдирдпрдирд╛рд░реНрдердореН рее реи.рекреж рее
рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШWith theseтАЩтАФVr─Бtyas;тАФтАШuntil purifiedтАЩтАФby expiatory rites;тАФтАШduly,тАЩ i.e., according to rules laid down in the scriptures laying down expiatory rites; e.g., тАШmaking them undergo three Kс╣Ыcchras, etc., etc.;тАЩтАФтАШeven in times of distressтАЩтАФi.e., under no circumstances however distressful;тАФтАШshould not establish,тАЩ enter into, тАШrelationshipтАЩ with them.

The question arising as to whether or not this prohibits all kinds of relationship, the text supplies the answer in the negativeтАФтАШspiritual or uterine .тАЩ

The term тАШbr─Бhma,тАЩ тАШspirit,тАЩ here stands for the Veda; and it is relationships through the Veda that are prohibited; such relationships as officiating at sacrifices, teaching and accepting gifts; the meaning being that one should neither officiate at their sacrificial performances, nor appoint them to officiate at sacrifices, they should not be taught, nor should one read with them. Since it is only one who knows the meaning of the Veda that is entitled to accept gifts, the accepting of gifts also becomes a тАШVedicтАЩ or тАШspiritualтАЩ relationship.

тАШUterine relationship,тАЩтАФthe giving and taking of daughters in marriage.

The specification of the тАШBr─Бhmaс╣ЗaтАЩ is intended to be illustrative only.

The sense of all this is that, in view of the disqualification here described, the boy whose father is no more should, if he is intelligent, try to avoid the disqualification, by presenting himself (at the proper time) for Initiation. To this end we have the ┼ЪrutiтАФтАЬSatyak─Бma J─Бb─Бla went to Gautama H─Бridrumata and saidтАФтАШI shall, sir, live with you as a religious studentтАЭ; where the boy himself requested the teacher to inflate him. The initiating of boys is however entirely optional; so that if the teacher should be found unwilling to take up the initiation, be should be appealed to by the boy by means of presents, etc.тАФ(40)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in Pr─Бya┼Ыcittaviveka (p. 144);тАФand in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 73), which explains тАШbrahma-sambandhaтАЩ as тАШteaching and so forth,тАЩ and тАШap┼лtaiс╕етАЩ as those who have not performed the prescribed expiatory rites.

It is quoted in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 446);тАФand also in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 349), which explains the term тАШap┼лtaiс╕етАЩ as тАШthose who have not performed the prescribed expiatory rites;тАЩ and the тАШrelationshipsтАЩ referred are explained as standing for Initiation, Reading, Teaching, Sacrificing and Receiving gifts.

This verse is quoted in Apar─Бrka (p. 68) in support of the view that dealings are permitted with such men as may have performed the expiatory rites laid down for the omission of the sacraments;тАФit adds that this is made clear by the epithet тАШAp┼лtaiс╕етАЩ.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

─Аpastamba-Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtra, 1.1.33; 1.2.6.тАФтАШWith these (apostates) one should avoid association, dining and marriage; in the event of their being desirous of expiating (the omission and the consequent apostacy), they should keep, for twelve years, the observances relating to Vedic studies, and then undergo the Upanayana, and be sprinkled with water with P─Бvam─Бn─л and other mantras.тАЩ

Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нha-Smс╣Ыti, 11.55.тАФтАШThey should not perform their Upanayana, nor teach them, nor sacrifice for them, nor marry them.тАЩ

─А┼Ыval─Бyana-Gс╣Ыhyas├╝tra, 1.19.7.тАФтАШThey should not perform their Upanayana, nor teach them, nor sacrifice for them, nor have any dealings with them.тАЩ [The V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 349, explains тАШdealingsтАЩ to mean тАШmarriage-connection.тАЩ]

P─Бraskara - Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtra, 2.5.40.тАФ[Exactly the same as above.]

Gobhila-Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtra, 2.10.6.тАФтАШThey should not perform their Upanayana, nor teach them, nor sacrifice for them, nor have marriage-relations with them.тАЩ

Baudh─Бyana-Smс╣Ыti (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 348).тАФтАШThere are no rites for the apostate until he passes through the Upanayana; so long as he is not born in the Veda, he remains like a ┼Ъ┼лdra.тАЩ

─А┼Ыval─Бyana-Smrti (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 349).тАФтАШNo dealingsтАФeither Vedic (tutorial), or marital or commercial,тАФshould he ever held with them by any cultured person who is true to his dharma.тАЩ

B├╝hler

040 With such men, if they have not been purified according to the rule, let no Brahmana ever, even in times of distress, form a connexion either through the Veda or by marriage.
