  • рдирдиреБ рдЪрд╛рдиреНрддрд░реЗрдгрд╛рдкрд┐ рд╡рдЪрдирдВ рд▓реЛрдХрдд рдПрд╡реИрддрддреН рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрдореН “рдЪреВрд░реНрдгрд┐рддрд╛рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрддрджрдЧреНрдзрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рдЬреНрд░рд╛рдирд┐рд▓рд╣реБрддрд╛рд╢рдиреИрдГ” (рдореНрднреН рен.ремрем.резрео) рдЗрддрд┐ рдпрдерд╛рдХреНрд░рдордВ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрддреНрддрд┐рдГ, рдЪреВрд░реНрдгрд┐рддрд╛ рд╡рдЬреНрд░реЗрдгрд╛рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрддрд╛рдГ рдЕрдирд┐рд▓реЗрди рджрдЧреНрдзрд╛ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдиреЗрддрд┐ ред рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рднрд╡реЗрджреН рдПрддрджреН рдПрд╡рдВ рдпрджрд┐ рднреЗрджреЗрди рдирд┐рд░реНрджреЗрд╢рдГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН рд╕рдорд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛рддреНрд╡рдВ рдЪ ред рдЗрд╣ рддреБ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд╛рд░рд┐рдг рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдПрдХрд╢рдмреНрджреЛрдкрд╛рджрд╛рдирд╛рдиреН рди рдХреНрд░рдореЛ рд╜рд╡рдЧрдореНрдпрддреЗ ред рддреНрд░рдпрд╢реН рдЪ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд╛рд░рд┐рдгрдГ ред рд╖рдбреН рдЕрдиреБрджреЗрд╢рд┐рдирдГ рддреНрд░реАрдгрд┐ рдЪрд░реНрдорд╛рдгрд┐ рддреНрд░реАрдгрд┐55 рд╡рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐ ред рдЖрдиреБрдкреВрд░реНрд╡реНрдпрдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгреЗ56 рддреБ рд╕рддрд┐ рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдиреНрддрд░реЛрдкрд╛рддреНрддрдГ рдХреНрд░рдо рдЖрд╢реНрд░реАрдпрддреЗ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪ рдЪрд░реНрдорднрд┐рдГ рд╕рдВрдмрдзреНрдп рдкреБрдирд░реН рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд╛рд░рд┐рдкрджрдореН рдЖрд╡рд░реНрддреНрдп рд╡рд╛рд╕реЛрднрд┐рдГ рд╕рдВрдмрдзреНрдпрддреЗ ред рддрддрдГ рд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛рд╕рд╛рдореНрдпрд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд┐рдГ ред рдИрджреГрд╢ рдПрд╡ рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпреЗ рднрдЧрд╡рддрд╛ рдкрд╛рдгрд┐рдирд┐рдирд╛ рдпрддреНрдирдГ рдХреГрддрдГ “рдпрдерд╛рд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрдореН рдЕрдиреБрджреЗрд╢рдГ рд╕рдорд╛рдирд╛рдореН” рдЗрддрд┐ (рдкрд╛рдгреН рез.рей.резреж) рее реи.рекрез рее
рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

Though the term тАШKс╣Ыс╣гna,тАЩ тАШblack,тАЩ is applied to everything that may be endowed with the quality of blackness,тАФas we find in the expressions тАШthe black cow,тАЩ тАШthe black blanket,тАЩ and so forth,тАФyet, in the present context, it is clearly recognised as standing for the тАШblack deerтАЩ; firstly because of its occurring along with the тАШskin of the Ruru deer,тАЩ and secondly because of the directions contained in other Smс╣Ыtis (which clearly mention the black deer).

тАШRuruтАЩтАФis a particular species of the deer.

тАШBastaтАЩтАФis the goat.

In all the three words (тАШk─Бrс╣гс╣ЗaтАЩтАФтАШrauravaтАЩтАФтАШv─БstaтАЩ) the nominal affix (aс╣З) denotes either formation or constitution (i.e., either тАШformed out ofтАЩ or тАШconsisting ofтАЩ).

тАШShould wearтАЩ;тАФthe Br─Бhmaс╣Зa should cover his body with the skin of the black antelope, the Kс╣гatriya with the skin of the Ruru deer and the Vai┼Ыya with the skin of the goat.

And also cloth made of ┼Ыaс╣Зa (hemp), kс╣гum─Б (flax), and ┼лrс╣З─Б (wool).

The particle тАШcaтАЩ (тАШand alsoтАЩ) has the cumulative force.

The cloth made of hemp and the rest are not to be used as upper garments; and the skins are to be used as upper garments; as such is the proper course. For Kaup─лna (loin-slip) and wrapping, the cloth is to be used.

тАШRespectingтАЩ each of the three castes is not related to all the clothing that is mentioned; nor are they to be connected in the reverse order; in fact the first Brahmac─Бr─л is connected with the first skin and first cloth, the second with the second and so forth, as we have shown.

An objection is raisedтАФтАЬEven without the express mention (of the respective order), it would be understood through usage; for instance, such expressions as тАШshattered, scattered an d burnt by thunder, wind and fireтАЩ are always understood to mean тАШshattered by thunder,тАЩ тАШscattered by the windтАЩ and тАШburnt by fireтАЩ (even though respectivity is not expressly mentioned).тАЭ

Answer.тАФThis could be so understood if the three Brahma-charts bad been mentioned separately, and if the number (of Brahmac─Бris and the clothings) were the same. In the present instance, however, we have the single term тАШBrahmac─Бris,тАЩ and the three Brahmac─Бris are not specifically named in any order. Further, the number of Brahmac─Бris is three, while that of the correlatives is sixтАФthree skins and three cloths. When however the text expressly mentions тАШrespectivity,тАЩ the order of the Br─Бhmac─Бris is deduced from that in which they are found to be spoken of in other texts. And after the тАШthree BrahmacharisтАЩ have been construed with the three skins, they are again repeated and construed with the cloths. And in.this manner the compatibility of numbers is maintained. It is primarily with reference to such cases that the revered P─Бс╣Зini has taken the trouble of laying down that тАШwhen an equal number of things are mentioned they are to be taken in their respective order.тАЩ (1.3.10).тАФ(41)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

тАШRuruтАЩтАФhas been described by R─Бghav─Бnanda as тАШtiger.тАЩ

Medh─Бtithi (p. 92,1. 11)тАФтАШSmс╣ЫtyantaraтАФThis refers to Baudh─Бyana, Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtra, 2. 5. 16.

This verse is quoted in Apar─Бrka (p.тАЮ 57) as laying down that the skin of the Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зamс╣Ыga, Ruru and Ch─Бga should be worn as the тАШupper garment,тАЩ respectively, by the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, the Kс╣гatriya and the Vai┼Ыya,

This verse is quoted in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 446), where it is explained that the skins mentioned are to be used as the upper garment, and the hempen and other cloths as the lower garment

Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 20) quotes the second half as prescribing the cloths to be used by the three castes respectively;тАФand the first half (on p. 22) as laying down the skins.

The second half is quoted in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Б ra, p. 411) and the first half also (p. 413).

The verse is quoted in Saс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (p. 36), which adds that the skins of the Black Antelope, the Ruru deer and the goat are to be used as the upper garment:тАФin Nс╣Ыsiс╣Гhapras─Бda (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 430);тАФand in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 75).

Burnell is again inaccurate in saying that cotton and silk (with the well to do) are alone used now for outer garments.тАЭ

Medh─Бtithi rightly remarks that the triplication cannot apply to the Kс╣гatriyaтАЩs girdle; as on triplication the bowstring would cease to be a тАШbowstring. Govindar─Бja agrees with him. So also Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 20) and V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra; p. 432), R─Бghav─Бnanda explains that as the bow-string itself is a triplicated cord, no further triplication would be necessary.

The тАШMu├▒jaтАЩ grass, in Northern India called muс╣Гja, is, as Burnell notes, the Saccarum Sara of the botanists.

Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 20) explains that the Mu├▒ja has тАШtejan─лтАЩ as its other name; and a foot-note adds that it is what is called murag─Б.

This verge is quoted in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 447);тАФalso in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 432), which explains тАШtrivс╣ЫtтАЩ not as twisted three-fold, but as тАШgoing round the waist three timesтАЩ;тАФin Nirс╣Зayasindhu (p. 189);тАФin

Apar─Бrka (p. 58); in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 70), which explains тАШtrivс╣ЫtтАЩ as threefold;тАФin Saс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (p. 37), which quotes Medh─Бtithi to the effect that since bowstrings are made sometimes of leather, the author has added the epithet тАШMaurv─лтАЩ, тАШMurv─Б grassтАЩ; in Saс╣Гsk─Бraratnam─Бl─Б (p. 192), which reproduces the above remark of Medh─Бtithi, as also his further remark that the string is to be removed from the bow and then tied round the waist: it adds the following notes: the тАШSam─БтАЩ, not uneven, thin in one place and thick in another; it should be of uniform thickness all through;тАФthe three-fold twist applies to the hempen cord and not to the bow-string, which would cease to be a bowstring when so twisted;тАФit is quoted also in Nс╣Ыsiс╣Гhapras─Бda (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 43 b).

─Аpastamba-Dharmas┼лtra, 1.3.1-9.тАФтАШFor the Kс╣гatriya, dyed in Ma├▒jiс╣гс╣нh─Б; for the Vai┼Ыya, dyed in Haridr─Б; for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, the skin of the white or black deer; for the Kс╣гatriya, the skin of the spotted deer; for the Vai┼Ыya, the skin of the goat; the sheep-skin for all castes; as also the woolen cloth; if the student is desirous of Br─Бhmic glory, he should wear the skins alone; if desirous of Kс╣гattric glory, he should wear the cloths alone; if desirous of both kinds of glory, he should wear both.тАЩ

Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нha-Smс╣Ыti, 11.47.тАФтАШFor the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, the upper garment consists of the skin of the black deer; for the Kс╣гatriya, of the skin of the spotted deer; for the Vai┼Ыya, of the skin of the cow or of the goat.тАЩ [V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 413, reads for тАШGavyam,тАЩ тАШ─Бvyam,тАЩ which means тАШof sheep.тАЩ ]

Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нha-Smс╣Ыti, 11.49.тАФтАШFor the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, the doth new and white; for the Kс╣гatriya, dyed in Ma├▒jiс╣гс╣нh─Б; for the Vai┼Ыya, dyed in Haridr─Б, or silken; for all, woven cloth, undyed; the new white cotton cloth, as also the hempen.тАЩ

Viс╣гс╣Зu-Smс╣Ыti, 27.19-20.тАФтАШThe upper garment should he of cotton, hemp and wool; and the skins of the deer, the tiger and the goat.тАЩ

─А┼Ыval─Бyana-Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtra, 1.19.7.тАФтАШThe hoy should be adorned and having his head shaven according to family-custom, clothed in new cloth or in skin; the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa in the skin of the black deer, the Kс╣гatriya in that of the spotted deer, and the Vai┼Ыya in that of the goat.тАЩ [The тАШahata,тАЩ тАШnew,тАЩ cloth has been thus defined by Pracetas:тАФтАШslightly washed, fresh-white, with ends intact, never worn beforeтАЩтАФVira-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 411.]

[The idea is that the lower garment should consist of cloth and the upper garment of skin.]

рд╢рдгрддрдиреНрддреБрд╡рд┐рдХрд╛рд░рдГ рд╢рдгрддрд╛рдиреНрддрд╡реА ред рдЫрд╛рдиреНрджрд╕рддреНрд╡рд╛рджреН рдЙрддреНрддрд░рдкрджрд╡реГрджреНрдзрд┐рдГ ред рдЕрде рд╡рд╛ рдХреЗрд╡рд▓рд╛рддреН рддрдиреНрддреБрд╢рдмреНрджрд╛рддреН рддрджреНрдзрд┐рддреЗ рдХреГрддреЗ рддрджрдиреНрддрд╕реНрдп рд╢рдгреИрдГ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрдГ- рд╢рдгрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рддрд╛рдиреНрддрд╡реАрддрд┐ ред рдкреНрд░рдХреГрддреЗрд░реН[^резреореи] рд╡рд┐рдХрд╛рд░рдГ рд╢рдгрддрд╛рдиреНрддрд╡реА рдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрд┐рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд┐рддрдпрд╛ рд╡реНрдпрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрддреЗ ред “рдЧрд╡реНрдпрдВ рдШреГрддрдореН” “рджреЗрд╡рджрддреНрддрд╕реНрдп рдкреМрддреНрд░рдГ” рдЗрддрд┐ ред рддрдиреНрддреБрдГ рд╕реВрддреНрд░рдВ рд╢рдгрдореМрдЮреНрдЬреАрд╡рддреН рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрд╛ ред рдЧреГрд╣реНрдпрдХрд╛рд░реИрд░реН рд╡реИрд╢реНрдпрдореЗрдЦрд▓рд╛рдпрд╛рдГ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реГрддреНрддрд╛рджрд┐рдзрд░реНрдордГ рд╕реБрд╕реНрдкрд╖реНрдЯ рдПрд╡реЛрдХреНрддрдГ рее реи.рекреи рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The mu├▒ja is a particular kind of grass; the cord made of that grass is called тАШMau├▒j─л.тАЩ This cord should form the тАШgirdle,тАЩ hraid, waist-band. тАШThreefoldтАЩтАФtriple-corded;тАФтАШof even thicknessтАЩтАФnot such as is thin in one part and thinner in another; but such as is even throughout;тАФтАШsoft and smooth,тАЩ of soft texture, well-rubbed.

тАШFor the Kс╣гatriya the bow-stringтАЩ;тАФthe string of the bow. The bow-string is made sometimes of leathern thong, sometimes of grass or of fibres of hemp or flax; hence the text specifies it as that тАШmade of murv─Б grassтАЩ; this string should be taken down from the bow and made into the waist-band.

Even though the qualifications of triplicity and the rest apply literally to all kinds of тАШgirdle,тАЩ and not only to that of mu├▒ja grass, yet they cannot be applied to the тАШbow-string,тАЩ as with such qualifications it would entirely lose its character of тАШbow-string.тАЩ

тАШMade of hempen fibresтАЩ;тАФthe lengthening of the vowel in the second number of the compound is an archaism. Or, we may take the term тАШt─Бntav─лтАЩ by itself formed with the nominal affix added to the term тАШtantuтАЩ only, and then compound the term тАШt─Бntav─лтАЩ with the term тАШ┼Ыaс╣ЗaтАЩ; since the тАШt─Бntav─л,тАЩ the fibre, is a product of the тАШ┼Ыaс╣Зa,тАЩ hemp, it is naturally spoken of as related to its source (the hemp) [hence the compound ┼Ыaс╣З─Бn─Бm t─Бntav─лтАФтАШ┼Ыaс╣Зat─Бntav─лтАЩ; as we find in such expressions as тАШthe cowтАЩs butter,тАЩ тАШDeva-dattaтАЩs grand sonтАЩ and so forth]. This hempen cord should be made like that of the Mu├▒ja cord; as the author of the Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtras have clearly laid down that the Vai┼ЫyaтАЩs girdle should have the qualities of triplicity and the rest.тАФ(42)

  • рддреЗрди рдореБрдЮреНрдЬрд╛рднрд╛рд╡реЗ рдХреМрд╢реА ред рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛ рдЕрднрд╛рд╡реЗ рд╜рд╢реНрдордиреНрддрдХреЗрди ред рд╢рд╛рдгрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдмрд▓реНрд╡рдЬреИрдГред рддреГрдгреМрд╖рдзрд┐рд╡рдЪрдирд╛рддреН рдХреБрд╢рд╛рджрдпрдГ ред рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдирд┐рдзрд┐рдирд┐рдпрдорд╢реН рдЪрд╛рдпрдореН ред рдХреБрд╢рд╛рджреНрдпрднрд╛рд╡реЗ рд╜рдкреНрдпреН рдЕрдиреНрдпрдиреН рдореБрдЮреНрдЬрд╛рджрд┐рд╕рджреГрд╢рдореН рдЙрдкрд╛рджреЗрдпрдореН ред

  • рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реГрддреНрддрд╛ рдЧреНрд░рдиреНрдерд┐рдиреИрдХреЗрди ред рдирд╛рдпрдВ рдЧреНрд░рдиреНрдерд┐рд╕рдВрдЦреНрдпрд╛рднреЗрджреЛ рд╡рд░реНрдгрднреЗрджреЗрди ред рдЕрдкрд┐ рддреБ рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпреЗрдХрдВ рд╡рд┐рдХрд▓реНрдкрдГ ред рдХреБрд╢рд╛рджрд┐рдореЗрдЦрд▓рд╛рд╕реНрд╡реН рдЕрдкреНрдпреН рдЕрдпрдВ рдЧреНрд░рдиреНрдерд┐рднреЗрджреЛ рдзрд░реНрдорднреЗрджрд╢реН рдЪреЛрджреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдГ рд╕реНрдореГрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░рд╕рдорд╛рдЪрд╛рд░рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдирд┐рддреНрдпрддреНрд╡реЗ рд╜рдкрд┐ рджреНрд░рд╖реНрдЯрд╡реНрдпрдГ рее реи.рекрей рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

Writers declare that the phrase тАШand the restтАЩ is understood, the sense being тАШin the event of Mu├▒ja and the rest being not available.тАЩ And the reason for this is that it is only thus that the plural number тАШshould be made,тАЩ becomes more appropriate; specially as the diversity of the girdle has been clearly prescribed in accordance with the diversity of castes. If the girdle spoken of in the present verse were meant for that of any one caste only, then the plural number could be justified only by taking it as referring to the girdle worn by the endless individual members of that one caste; and further, it would be necessary in this case to alter the singular number in тАШviprasyaтАЩ (of the preceding verse) into the plural number (to bring it into conformity with the present verse); and lastly, in this case all the three alternatives herein mentioned would have to be taken as pertaining to the one girdle (of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa only). And no such multiplicity of option should be allowed so long as there is any other way of taking the text.

Thus then the sense of the present verse is as followsтАФ(a) if Mu├▒ja is not available, the girdle should be made of Ku┼Ыa; if the bow-string is not available, it should be made of Ashmantaka; and (c) if the hempen fibre is not available it should be made of Balvaja.

The terms тАШku┼Ыa,тАЩ etc., denote grasses and herbs.

This verse is meant to restrict the choice of substitutes; so that in the absence of ku┼Ыa, etc., one would not be justified in using any other similar substances.

Triplicated by one knot. The various numbers (of knots) are not meant to be restricted to the three castes respectively; they are intended to be optional alternatives for every one of them. This difference in the number of knots in the girdle made of ku┼Ыa, etc., as well as the other details laid down in connection with it are to be regarded as regular injunctions, even though the customs laid down in other Smс╣Ыtis are not necessarily binding.тАФ(43)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 447),тАФand also in Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 20), which latter agrees with Medh─Бtithi in taking the Ku┼Ыa-A┼Ыm─Бntaka-Balvaja as pertaining to the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, the Kс╣гatriya and the Vai┼Ыya respectively.

V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 433) explains that the term тАШMu├▒jaтАЩ in the present verse stands for all its variants mentioned in the preceding verse, and proceeds to quote the view that what is meant is thatтАФ(a) for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa in the absence of Mu├▒ja, Ku┼Ыa should be used,тАФ(b) for the K┼Ыatriya in the absence of Murv─Б, A┼Ыm─Бntaka, and (c) for the Vai┼Ыya in the absence of ┼Ъaс╣Зa, Balvaja; but dissents from it, stating it as its own opinion, that all the three substitutes mentioned are meant for each of the primary substances enjoined before. It cites another view, according to which, since the present verse mentions the Mu├▒ja only, the meaning must be that the three substitutes are meant for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa only; so that for the Kс╣гatriya and the Vai┼Ыya, if the substance primarily prescribed under the preceding verse be not available, they should make use of some other suitable material resembling the primary. But this view also is not approved as being in conflict with the text of Yama, which says thatтАФтАЬin the absence, of these i.e. the three, Mu├▒ja, Murv─Б and ┼Ъaс╣Зa, the girdle should be made of Ku┼Ыa, A┼Ыm─Бntaka and Balvaja.тАЭ

The second half of the verse is quoted in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra) on page 432, where it adds that the options mentioned do not depend entirely on the wish of the wearer,тАФthe number of knots being, in fact, determined by the number of Pravaras of the Gotra to which the boy belongs.

Nirс╣Зayasindhu (p. 189) also quotes this verse;тАФand Apar─Бrka (p. 58), which explains that the knots are to be made in accordance with oneтАЩs тАШGotra-с╣Ыс╣гisтАЩ;тАФalso Saс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (p. 37), which quotes Kull┼лkaтАЩs explanation;тАФin Saс╣Гsk─Бraratnam─Бl─Б (p. 193) as setting forth substitutes for the girdle-zone; it adds the following notes:тАФThe term тАШ─БdiтАЩ is understood here, the construction being тАШMu├▒j─Бdyabh─БveтАЩ, тАШin the absence of Mu├▒ja and other substancesтАЩ; the number of knots is to be the same as that of the wearerтАЩs Pravara;тАФin Nс╣Ыsiс╣Гhapras─Бda (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 43b);тАФand in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 80), which adds the note that тАШtrivс╣ЫtтАЩ means тАШthreefoldтАЩ; and that тАШMu├▒jaтАЩ here stands for the Murv─Б and other substances specified in the preceding verse.

P─Бraskara-Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtra, 2.5.24.тАФтАШIn the absence of Mu├▒ja, it should consist of Ku┼Ыa, Ashman taka and Balvaja.тАЩ

Yama (V─лramitrodaya-Sarhsk─Бra, p. 433).тАФтАШIn the absence of these (Mu├▒ja, Murv─Б and Hemp), it should consist of Ku┼Ыa, Ashmantaka and Balvaja; and girdles should be made threefold with either one or three knots.тАЩ

The Sacrificial Thread worn over the shoulder,тАФwhich is triple and twisted upwards,тАФshould be hade op cotton for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, of hempen fibres for the Kс╣гatriya, and op woolen fibres for the Vai┼Ыya.тАФ(44)

  • рдКрд░реНрдзреНрд╡рд╡реГрддреНрддрдореН рдКрд░реНрдзреНрд╡рд╛рдВ рджрд┐рд╢рдВ рджрд┐рд╢рдВ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╡рд░реНрддреНрдпрддреЗ рд╡реЗрд╖реНрдЯреНрдпрддреЗ ред рддреНрд░рд┐рд╡реГрддреН рддреНрд░рд┐рдЧреБрдгрдореН ред рдХрд░реНрддрдирд┐рдХрд╛рднреНрдпреЛ рд▓рдмреНрдзрд╕реВрддреНрд░рднрд╛рд╡рд╕реНрдп рддреНрд░рд┐рдЧреБрдгреАрдХреГрддрд╕реНрдпреЗрджрдореН рдКрд░реНрдзреНрд╡рдирд┐рд╡рд░реНрддрдирдВ57 рд╡рд┐рдзреАрдпрддреЗ ред рд╕рдВрд╣рддреНрдп рддрдиреНрддреБрддреНрд░рдпрдореН рдКрд░реНрдзреНрд╡рд╡реЗрд╖реНрдЯрдиреЗрди рд░рдЬреНрдЬреНрд╡рд╛рдХрд╛рд░рдВ рдХреГрддреНрд╡рд╛ рддреЗрдиреЛрдкрд╡реАрддрдВ рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рддреН ред рд╕рд╛ рдЪ рд░рдЬреНрдЬреБрд░реН рдПрдХреИрд╡ рдзрд╛рд░рдпрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрд╛, рддрд┐рд╕реНрд░рдГ рдкрдЮреНрдЪ рд╕рдкреНрдд рд╡рд╛ ред рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрд╛рджреН рдзрд┐ рддрджреН рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЛрдкрд╡реАрддрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдВ58 рд▓рднрддреЗ ред рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд╛рд░реНрдереЛ рд╜рдпрдореН рдЙрджреНрдпрддреЗ рдЗрддрд┐ рднрдХреНрддреНрдпреЛрдкрдЪрд░реНрдпрддреЗ ред рддрддреНрд░реЗрд╖реНрдЯрд┐рдкрд╢реБрд╕реЛрдорд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдпрдЬреНрдЮрд░реВрдкрддрдпреИрдХрддреНрд╡рд╛рджреН рдПрдХрддрдиреНрддреБрдХрдВ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрддреЗ ред рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рддреНрд░рдпрд╕рд╛рдзреНрдпрддреНрд╡рд╛рджреН рдЕрд╣реАрдиреИрдХрд╛рд╣рд╕рддреНрд░рднреЗрджрд╛рджреН рд╡рд╛ рддреНрд░рд┐рддрдиреНрддреБрдХрдореН ред рд╕реЛрдорд╕рдВрд╕реНрдерд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕рдкреНрддрд╕рдЩреНрдЦреНрдпрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рд╕рдкреНрдд рд╡рд╛ рддрдиреНрддрд╡рдГ ред “рддреНрд░реАрдгрд┐ рд╕рд╡рдирд╛рдирд┐ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╕рдВрдзреНрдпреЗрди” рдЗрддрд┐ рдкрдЮреНрдЪ ред рд╕реВрддреНрд░рд╛рднрд╛рд╡реЗ59 рдкрдЯрд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛рдкрд┐ рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдореН ред рд╕реНрдореГрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░ рдПрд╡рдореН рдЙрдХреНрддрдореН ред
  • рдЕрд╡рд┐рдГ рдореЗрд╖рд╕реН рддрд╕реНрдп рд╕реВрддреНрд░рдВ рддреЗрди рдХреГрддрдВ рдЖрд╡рд┐рдХрд╕реВрддреНрд░рд┐рдХрдореН ред рдЕрдзреНрдпрд╛рддреНрдорд╛рджрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рдЯреН рдардЮреН рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдГ ред “рдЕрд╡рд┐рдХрд╕реВрддреНрд░рд┐рдХрдореН” рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд╛ рдкрдард┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдореН ред рддрддреНрд░ рдЪ рдорддреНрд╡рд░реНрдереАрдпреЗрди рдардирд╛ рд░реВрдкрд╕рд┐рджреНрдзрд┐рдГ рее реи.рекрек рее
рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The term тАШupav─лtaтАЩ stands for the peculiar manner in which cloth is worn; as will be explained later in Verse 63; as such, it is only a quality; and since this quality cannot be made of cotton, the quality is taken as standing for the thing to which the quality belongs; the meaning being that the thing that is to be worn in the particular way should be made of cotton; the term тАШupav─лtamтАЩ being regarded as formed with the тАШachтАЩ affix, according to P─Бс╣Зini 5.2.127, тАШupav─лtamтАЩ being equivalent to тАШupav─лtavat.тАЩ

тАШTwisted upwardsтАЩтАФi.e., turned round, coiled upwards.

тАШTripleтАЩтАФconsisting of three yarns.

This тАШtwisting upwardsтАЩ is laid down for that article which, on coming out of the spinning wheel, has acquired the properties of the тАШyarnтАЩ and has then been folded three times. That is to say, three yarns should be brought together and by upward twisting made into a cord, and then used as the тАШsacred thread.тАЩ Of this cord, either only one or three or five or seven should be worn. It comes to be known as the тАШsacrificial threadтАЩ by reason of its being connected with sacrificial performances; in as much as it is worn for the purposes of sacrificial performances, it is so called figuratively.

Now, of the three kinds of sacrifice, the Iс╣гс╣нi, the Pa┼Ыu and the Soma sacrifices, it may be worn single at all these, when they are all looked upon as тАШsacrificesтАЩ in general (and hence, uniform); or it may be worn three-fold, when they are looked upon either as performed with the help of three fires, or as being divided into the three classes of тАШAh─лna,тАЩ

тАШEk─БhaтАЩ and тАШSatraтАЩ; or again, it may be worn seven-fold, in view of the number of stages in the Soma sacrifice being seven; or lastly, it may be worn five-fold, in view of there being three тАШSavanasтАЩ (extractions of Soma-juice) and two тАШSandhy─БsтАЩ (twilights).

[In the absence of Cotton], the тАШThreadтАЩ may be made of silk and other fibres also; such is the direction given ill other Smс╣Ыtis.

тАШAviтАЩ is sheep; the yarn made of wool is тАШwoolen fibreтАЩ; the term тАШ─Бrik?s┼лtrikamтАЩ being formed with the тАШс╣нha├▒тАЩ affix, according to the V─Бrtika on Paс╣Зini 4.3.60. Or, we may read тАШavikas┼лtrikamтАЩ this word being formed with the тАШс╣нhanтАЩ affix having the sense of the possessive.тАФ(14)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in Smс╣Ыtichandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 80), Which says that тАШtrivс╣ЫtтАЩ means тАШmade of nine yarnsтАЩ;тАФand in Nity─Бch─Бraprad─лpa (p. 31).

It is quoted in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 448); in Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 21),тАФand in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 414);тАФalso in Nirс╣Зayasindhu (p. 190);тАФin Apar─Бrka (p. 58);тАФin Nс╣Ыsiс╣Гhapras─Бda (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 43a);тАФin Saс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (p. 38), which has the following notes:тАФтАШ┼лrdhvavс╣ЫtamтАЩ and тАШtrivс╣ЫtтАЩ are to be construed with тАШ┼Ыaс╣Зas┼лtramayamтАЩ; also,тАФтАШ─БvikamтАЩ means тАШof sheep- wool.тАЩ

тАШUrdhvavс╣ЫtamтАЩтАФThis is thus defined by тАШSaс╣Еgrah─Бk─Бra.тАЩ a writer quoted in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava and Madanap─Бrij─БtaтАФтАШThat which is twisted threefold by the right hand moving upwardтАЩтАФi.e. twisted towards the right.

тАШTrivс╣ЫtтАЩтАФhas been explained in V─лramitrodaya as standing for тАШconsisting of nine threadsтАЩ; and thus on the basis of a ┼Ъruti text which defines тАШTrivс╣ЫtтАЩ as nine. The same explanation is given in Apar─Бrka also;тАФso also Smс╣Ыtikaumud─л (p. 6.)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

Even though the text uses the Copulative Compound (which implies that two staves have to be carried), yet, in as much as in connection with the detailed qualifications of the staff laid down in the text, we find the singular number used,тАФe.g., in the next verse, and in Verse 18 below,тАФit is understood that only one staff is to be carried; specially as in the Gс╣Ыhya-s┼лtra we readтАФтАШthe Br─Бhmaс╣ЗaтАЩs staffтАЩ is of Bilva or Pal─Б┼ЫaтАЩ; and the Gautama-s┼лtra speaks of the carrying of one staff only. In the present context all that is done is to lay down the mere possibility of the staff; the expression тАШshould have stavesтАЩ meaning that the said staves are fit for Brahmac─Бr─лs. As regards the question as to the act during which the staff is to be held, we shall have the answer in Verse 48 below; so that the staff being only an auxiliary to that act, the singular number used in that verse must be regarded as significant. For these reasons the

Dual number used in the present verse must be taken merely as referring to all possible staves; just like the plural number in the assertionтАФтАШif God were to give rain many persons would take to cultivation.тАЩ

тАШBilva,тАЩ тАШPal─Б┼Ыa,тАЩ тАШVaс╣нa,тАЩ тАШKhadiraтАЩ P─лluтАЩ and тАШbaraтАЩ are names of particular species of trees.

тАШBailvaтАЩ means тАШmade of BilvaтАЩ; and so with the rest.

The naming of the woods is meant to be merely illustrative; as the general rule is that тАШstaves made of sacred woods are fit for all castesтАЩ (Gautama 1.1.24).

These staves the Brahmac─Бr─лs тАШshould haveтАЩ during the act to be described below (in 48);тАФтАШby lawтАЩтАФi.e., in accordance with scriptural injunctions.тАФ(45)

045 A Brahmana shall (carry), according to the sacred law, a staff of Bilva or Palasa; a Kshatriya, of Vata or Khadira; (and) a Vaisya, of Pilu or Udumbara.

рдореЗрдзрд╛рддрд┐рдерд┐рдГ

рдЖрдХрд╛рд░рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рд╡рдЪрдиреЛ рджрдгреНрдбрд╢рдмреНрджрдГ ред рджреАрд░реНрдШрдВ рдХрд╛рд╖реНрдардВ61 рд╕рдВрдорд┐рддрд╛рдпрд╛рдордВ рджрдгреНрдб рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдХрд┐рдпрддреН рддрд╕реНрдп рджреИрд░реНрдШреНрдпрдореН рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрдкреЗрдХреНрд╖рд╛рдпрд╛рдореН рдЖрд╣ ред рдХреЗрд╢рд╛рдиреНрддрдВ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддрд┐ рдХреЗрд╢рд╛рдиреНрддрдЧреЛ рдореВрд░реНрджреНрдзрдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгрдГ ред рдкрд╛рджрд╛рдЧреНрд░рд╛рджреН рдЖрд░рднреНрдп рдореВрд░реНрджреНрдзрд╛рд╡рдзрд┐рдГ рдХреЗрд╢рд╛рдиреНрддрдЧрдГ ред рдХреЗрд╢рд╛ рд╡рд╛рдиреНрддреЛ рд╜рд╕реНрдпреЗрддрд┐ рдХреЗрд╢рд╛рдиреНрддрдХрдГ ред рд╕рдорд╛рд╕рд╛рдиреНрддрдГ рдХрдХрд╛рд░рдГ ред рдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгрддрдГ рдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгреЗрдирд╛рдиреЗрди рдпреБрдХреНрддреЛ рджрдгреНрдбрдГ рдХрд╛рд░реНрдпрдГ рдХрд╛рд░рдпрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдГ рдмреНрд░рд╛рд╣реНрдордгрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЪрд╛рд░реНрдпреЗрдг ред рд▓рд▓рд╛рдЯрд╕рдВрдорд┐рддрдГ рд▓рд▓рд╛рдЯрд╛рдиреНрддрдореН рдЗрддрдГ рд▓рд▓рд╛рдЯрдиреНрддрдкреНрд░рдорд╛рдгрдГ ред рд▓рд▓рд╛рдЯрдорд╛рддреНрд░реЗ рдЪрддреБрд░рдЩреНрдЧреБрд▓реЗрди рдореАрдпрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рджрдгреНрдбрд╢рдмреНрджрд╡рд╛рдЪреНрдпрддреНрд╡рд╛рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рджреН рдПрд╡рдВ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдпрддреЗ- рдкрд╛рджрд╛рдЧреНрд░рд╛рджреН рдЖрд░рднреНрдп рдпрд╛рд╡рд▓реН рд▓рд▓рд╛рдЯрд╛рдиреНрддрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрдГ ред рдПрд╡рдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢реЛ рд╡реИрд╢реНрдпрд╕реНрдп рдирд╛рд╕рд╛рдиреНрддрдЧ рдЗрддрд┐ рее реи.рекрем рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The term тАШstaffтАЩ denotes the particular shape (of the wood carried);тАФa long piece of wood of a well-defined size is called тАШstaff.тАЩ

The question arising as to what its length should be, the Text answers it. That which reaches up to the end of the hair is called тАШKe┼Ы─Бntika,тАЩ i.e., reaching up to the head; i.e., in size it should reach from the tip of the foot up to the head. Or, the compound тАШKe┼Ы─Бnta.тАЩ may be expounded as тАШthat of which the hair forms the end,тАЩ the ka coming in as an additional affix at the end of the compound.

тАШIn size,тАЩтАФthe staffтАФтАШshould be madeтАЩ of the said size,тАФтАШfor the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa,тАЩтАФi.e., by the Teacher.

тАШReaching to the foreheadтАЩтАФi.e., of the size reaching up to the forehead. The тАШforeheadтАЩ itself is only four inches in width; and as a piece of wood of that size could never be spoken of as тАШstaff,тАЩ we have to explain the term тАШlal─Бс╣нasamnitaс╕етАЩ (which, as it stands, means тАШof the size of the foreheadтАЩ) as meaning тАШthat which reaches from the tip of the foot up to the forehead.тАЩ

Similarly for the Vai┼Ыya, it should reach up to the tip of the nose.тАФ(46)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in Smс╣Ыtitattva (p. 930), which adds that in the event of the specified wood not being available any one of the woods recommended for the three castes may be used for any one of these three;тАФin Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 22);тАФin V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 436), which last explains тАШKe┼Ы─Бntikaс╕етАЩ as тАШM┼лrdh─Бpram─Бс╣Зaс╕етАЩ;тАФin Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 448);тАФin Apar─Бrka (p. 57);тАФin Nс╣Ыsiс╣Гhapras─Бda (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p.43b);тАФand in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 78), which explains тАШKe┼Ы─Бntikaс╕етАЩ as reaching up to the head.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

Gautama-Dharmas┼лtra, 1.27.тАФтАШThey are of the size reaching up to the head, the forehead and the nose-tip.тАЩ

Baudh─Бyana-Dharmas┼лtra.тАФтАШThe staves are of a sacrificial wood, reaching up to the head, the forehead and the nose-с╣нip.тАЩ

Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нha-Smс╣Ыti, 11.46.тАФтАШFor the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, it should reach up to the hair; for the Kс╣гatriya, up to the forehead; for the Vai┼Ыya, up to tho nose.тАЩ

─А┼Ыval─Бyana-Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtra, 19.13.тАФтАШFor the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa, reaching up to the hair; for the Kс╣гatriya, reaching up to the forehead; for the Vai┼Ыya, reaching up to с╣нhe Breath (Nose-tip).тАЩ

P─Бraskara-Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtra (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 436).тАФтАШThe staff of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa should reach to his hair; of the Kс╣гatriya, to his forehead; of the Vai┼Ыya, to the Breath.тАЩ

Vy─Бsa (Do.).тАФтАШReaching up to the head, the forehead and the nose-tip.тАЩ

┼Ъaс╣Еkha (Do., p. 437).тАФтАШThey have been described as ranging between the Hair and the Forehead.тАЩ

Viс╣гс╣Зu (V─лra-Saс╣Гskara, p. 437).тАФтАШThey should reach the Hair, the Forehead and the Nose.тАЩ

┼Ъaс╣Еkha-Likhita (Do.).тАФтАШThey should reach the Hair, the Forehead and the Mouth.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШStraightтАЩтАФnot crooked.

тАШAllтАЩтАФrefers to those mentioned above; all those mentioned being equally the things under consideration.

тАШUnimpairedтАЩтАФwithout holes.

тАШHandsome lookingтАЩ;тАФwhose appearance is pleasing. That is, of pure colour and without thorns.

тАШNot frighteningтАЩ;тАФthey should not be used to frighten anyone, dog or man; тАШto menтАЩ being only indicative (of animals in general).

тАШWith barkтАЩтАФuncut, unpeeled.

тАШUnspoilt by fire,тАЩтАФnot affected by fire either of lightning or of the forest.тАФ(47)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

  • рдкреНрд░рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрдВ рдкрд░реАрддреНрдп рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреЛ рдЧрддреНрд╡реНрдЖрдЧреНрдирд┐рдореН ред рдЪрд░реЗрддреН рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рддреН ред **рднреИрдХреНрд╖рдореН ред **рднрд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдгрд╛рдореН рд╕рдореВрд╣реЛ рднреИрдХреНрд╖рдореН ред рддрдЪреН рдЪрд░реЗрджреН рдпрд╛рдЪреЗрдд ред рдпрдерд╛рд╡рд┐рдзреАрддрд┐ рд╡рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрдорд╛рдгрд╡рд┐рдзреНрдпрдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ ред рднрд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛рд╢рдмреНрджреЗрди рд╕реНрд╡рд▓реНрдкрдкрд░рд┐рдорд╛рдгрдВ рднрдХреНрддрд╛рджреНрдпреН рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ рее реи.рекрео рее

After the skins have been put on, the tying of the girdle should be done; and after having tied the girdle, the Initiation should be performed; the staff is taken up after the тАШsacred threadтАЩ ceremony has been performed. After the staff has been taken up, the Sun should be worshipped; i.e., one should stand facing the sun and worship Him with those Mantras of which the sun is the presiding deity; what are the particular Mantras to be employed can be ascertained from the Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtras; as also the other details of procedure.

The present verse describes only what is common to all persons.

тАШHaving walked round the fire to his right,тАЩтАФhaving passed all round it.

тАШGharetтАЩтАФ(lit.) should accomplish;тАФтАШalmsтАЩ is a collective term, stauding for collection of fool;тАФthis he тАШshould beg.тАЩ

тАШAccording to prescribed ruleтАЩтАФrefers to the rules going to be laid down below. The term тАШbhikс╣г┼лтАЩ (food) stands for small quantities of cooked rice, etc.тАФ(18)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 451), where it is explained that the Sun is to be worshiped as the sum total of the connotation of the G─Бyatr─л-mantra;тАФand that one is to realise that he is one with that deity. According to this authority the тАШpar─лty─БgnimтАЩmeans, not that the boy is to тАШwalk round the fireтАЩ (as explained by Kull┼лka and Medh─Бtithi), but that he should tend the fire; and it proceeds to point out that the тАШtending of the fireтАЩ is to be done according to what has been laid down by Manu himself under 2. 186.

It is difficult to see how this writer would construe the adverb тАШpradakс╣гiс╣Зam.тАЩ

This verse is quoted in Smс╣Ыtitattva (p. 935) in support of the view that the particle тАШathaтАЩ in the Gс╣Ыhya-s┼лtra: тАШaiha bhaikс╣гya├▒caratiтАЩ stands for the Upasth─Бna of the Sun and тАШpradakс╣гiс╣ЗaтАЩ of the Fire;тАФin Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 32); the latter explaining тАШ─лpsitamтАЩ by тАШas prescribed for each individual, and not any otherтАЩ, adds that the Sun is to be worshipped with mantras sacred to that deity. It accepts Medh─БtithiтАЩs explanation of the phrase тАШparity─БgnimтАЩ; and points out that the three acts mentioned here all form part of the procedure of тАШbegging.тАЩ

It is quoted also in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 481), according to which also, тАШ─лpsitamтАЩ means тАШwhat is prescribed for each particular casteтАЩ;тАФand the phrase тАШbh─Бskaram upasth─БyaтАЩ (though it quotes the latter term as тАШabhi-v─БdyaтАЩ) as тАШfacing the sunтАЩ (which is the explanation, it adds, suggested by Kalpataru);тАФand тАШYath─БvidhiтАЩ as тАШaccording to the rule laid down in the next verse.тАЩ It adds that all the three acts are subsidiary to the act of begging.

It is quoted in Apar─Бrka (p. 60);тАФin Saс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (p. 60);тАФin Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 108), which explains тАШYath─БvidhiтАЩ as тАШaccording to the ordinancesтАФand in V─лramitrodaya (Vy─Бvah─Бra, p. 124 a).

  • рдЙрдкрдиреАрдд рдЗрддрд┐ рднреВрддрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдирд┐рд░реНрджреЗрд╢рд╛рджреН рдЖрдиреНрд╡рд╣рд┐рдХреЗ рд╜рдкрд┐ рд╡реГрддреНрддреНрдпрд░реНрдереЗ рднреИрдХреНрд╖реНрдпрдЪрд░рдгреЗ рд╜рдпрдореН рдПрд╡ рд╡рд┐рдзрд┐рд░реН рдЗрддрд┐ рджрд░реНрд╢рдпрддрд┐ ред “рдПрд╖ рдкреНрд░реЛрдХреНрддреЛ рд╣рд┐ рджреНрд╡рд┐рдЬрд╛рддреАрдирд╛рдореН рдФрдкрдирд╛рдпрдирд┐рдХрдГ” (рдореНрдзреН реи.ремрео) рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдкрдирдпрдирдкреНрд░рдХрд░рдгрдореН рдЙрдкрд╕рдВрд╣рд░рдиреНрдиреН рдЙрдкрдирдпрдирд╛рдЩреНрдЧрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдкрд┐ рднреИрдХреНрд╖реНрдпрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдпрдореН рдПрд╡ рд╡рд┐рдзрд┐рд░реН рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЖрд╣ ред рдЕрдиреНрдпрдерд╛рдХрд░рдгрд╛рджреН рдЙрдкрдирдпрдирд╛рдЩреНрдЧрдореН рдПрд╡реИрддрддреН рд╕реНрдпрд╛рджреН рдпрджрд┐ рд╡рд╛ рднреВрддрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрд╕рд╛рдорд░реНрдереНрдпрд╛рддреН66 рдкреНрд░рдХрд░рдгрдВ рдмрд╛рдзрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рд╡реГрддреНрддреНрдпрд░реНрде рдПрд╡ рднреИрдХреНрд╖реНрдпреЗ ред рдЙрдкрдиреАрдпрдорд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рддрджрдЩреНрдЧрдВ рдпрджреНрднреИрдХреНрд╖рдВ рдпрдЪреН рдЪрд╛рд╣рд░реН рдЕрд╣рд░реН рд╡реГрддреНрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердВ рддрддреНрд░ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рддреНрд░рд╛рдпрдВ рдзрд░реНрдордГ рее реи.рекреп рее
рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The word тАШbhaikс╣гamтАЩ here stands for the words with which the request for alms is preferred; as it is only the words that can have тАШbhavatтАЩ as the тАШbeginningтАЩ; the food itself could not have any such beginning.

In as much as it is laid down that ladies are the first to be begged from first, and in the request made it is the person begged from that is addressed, it is the feminine vocative form of the term тАШbhavatтАЩ that should be used.

All that the present text does is to lay down the order of the words to he used, there being some transcendental purpose served by the order. The actual words used should beтАФтАШbhavati bhikс╣г─Бm dehi,тАЩ тАШO Lady, give me food.тАЩ

Question,тАФтАЬ Wherefore could there be any possibility of

Sanskrit words being used, since they are addressed to women, and they do not understand Sanskrit

Answer.тАФThe Initiatory ceremony, being compulsory, is of an eternal character; and it is in connection with this ceremony that the use of the words is laid down. The vernaculars (corrupt languages) are not eternal; so that there could be no connection between these and an eternal ceremony. Then again, just as when educated people hear corrupt forms of words used, they are reminded, by the resemblance, of the corresponding correct forms and thereby come to comprehend the meaning;тАФfor instance, the (incorrect) word тАШ?─БтАЩ leads to the inference (remembrance of) of the (correct) word тАШgo’ through similarity, according to the theory that тАШthe incorrect word is expressive only by inference, and the meaning is comprehended from the inferred correct wordтАЩ; in the same manner when correct words are addressed to women, they remember, through similarity, the corresponding incorrect words whoso meaning they know, and thus they come to comprehend the; meaning of the words used. Further, the expression in question is a short, one consisting of three words only, and these being well-known words, they would be easily comprehensible by ladies also.

Similarly the Kс╣гatriya should use words of which the тАШbhavatтАЩ forms the middle; the actual form being тАШbhikс╣г─Бm bhavati dehi,тАЩ тАШGive me, O Lady, food.тАЩ So the Vai┼Ыya should use words of which тАШbhavatтАЩ forms the end. The word тАШbhavaduttaramтАЩ means тАШthat of which bhavat forms the endтАЩ;тАФthe compound thus standing for the sentence (give me food, O LadyтАЩ).

тАШHaving undergone InitiationтАЩ;тАФthe past-participial ending implies that the rule laid down here is to be observed also in connection with the begging for food for daily living (even after the first day of the initiation); and further, what is said in verse 68 belowтАФтАШsuch is the procedure of initiation for the twice-bornтАЩтАФis a summing up of the whole section on тАШInitiationтАЩ; and hence shows that the rule laid down in the present verse applies also to that begging for alms whicс╕е forms part of the ceremony of Initiation. If we do not take it thus, then what is laid down here would only he taken either as a part of the Initiation-rites (as shown by the context), or as applying to the ordinary begging for food;тАФin this latter case the implication of the context would be rejected and stress would be laid only upon the sense of the past-participial ending (тАШhaving undergone InitiationтАЩ) As a matter of fact, what is here prescribed is applicable to that тАШbegging for foodтАЩ which forms part of the Initiatory Rites, as also to that which is done for the purposes of livelihood.тАФ(49)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in Smс╣Ыtitattva (p. 936); in Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 32), which latter adds, the following notes:тАФ

In the phrase тАШbhaikс╣гam charetтАЩ the verb indicates begging, as is shown by the objective term тАШbhaikс╣гamтАЩ; it is in view of this that the expression to be used in the begging isтАФтАШbhikс╣г─Бm dehiтАЩ (тАШgive almsтАЩ);тАФand as the words have to be addressed with proper respect, the term тАШbhavatтАЩ with the vocative ending (тАШMadamтАЩ or тАШSirтАЩ) has to be added at the beginning, middle or end, according to the caste of the begging boy;тАФthen, inasmuch as in the house, it is, as a rule, the women-folk that give alms, it follows that the feminine-(vocative) form of the term тАШbhavatтАЩ should be used;тАФthus then the precise form of the expression comes to be thisтАФ(a) The Br─Бhamaс╣Зa boy should say тАШbhavati bhikс╣г─Бm dehiтАЩ, (b) the Kс╣гatriya, тАШbhikс╣г─Бm bhavati dehi,тАЩ and (c) the Vai┼Ыya, тАШbhikс╣г─Бm dehi bhavatiтАЩ. There is no such hard and fast rule as that тАШalms should be begged from women only.тАЩ

V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 481) also quotes the verse, and supplies the formula as noted in Madanap─Бrij─Бta;тАФSaс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (p. 60) quotes it, and lays down the formula for the three castes asтАФ(a) тАШbhavati bhikс╣г─Бm dad─БtuтАЩ, (b) тАШbhikс╣г─Бm bhavat─л dad─Бtu,тАЩ and (c) тАШbhikс╣г─Бm dad─Бtu bhavatiтАФSmс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 108), which mentions the formula as given in Madanap─Бrij─Бta;тАФand also V─лramitrodaya (Vy─Бvah─Бra, p. 124).

Burnell remarks that тАШthis begging of alms is now obsolete But so far as the formality is concerned, it is still gone through at the close of the Upanayaс╣Зa ceremony.

This verse is quoted in Apar─Бrka (p. 59) as laying down the rule relating to that alms-begging which is done as part of the Upanayaс╣Зa-ceremony.

It is quoted in Smс╣Ыtitittva (p. 936), which adds that these ladies are to be approached only if they happen to be on the spot, and the boy is not to go to their houses;тАФin Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 34), which latter quotes it only with a view to explain that there is no inconsistency between this injunction and the later prohibition (2. 184) of begging from oneтАЩs relations; because the former refers to the begging as part of the Upanayana ceremony, whereas the prohibition applies to the usual begging of food during the entire period of studentship.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The term тАШhaving collectedтАЩ shows that the food should be obtained from several ladies, and a large quantity should not be obtained from a single lady.

тАШItтАЩтАФrefers to that which has gone immediately before this, i.e., the food begged for ordinary eating, and not that which is done as part of the Initiation-rites, with which the context deals; specially as with regard to the latter all that the Gс╣Ыс╕еya-S┼лtra prescribes is that the food should be тАШcooked,тАЩ and nothing is said regarding тАШeating.тАЩ Further, the injunction that тАШthe boy should fast for the rest of the dayтАЩ shows that the boy undergoes the Initiatory rite after breakfast; so that the actual eating of the food cannot be part of that rite.

тАШAs much os way he neededтАЩ;тАФi.e., just as much food as may be necessary for the satisfaction of hunger; large quantities of food should not be begged.

тАШHaving offered it without guile to the Teacher;тАЩтАФi.e., he should not show the teacher only the inferior articles of food, hiding with these the superior ones, with the view that the Teacher would not take any thing out of the inferior articles. The тАШofferingтАЩ consists of presenting it to him, saying тАШthis is what I have obtained.тАЩ

What the teacher does not take, тАШhe should eat,тАЩ after having been permitted by the teacher to do so.

тАЬWhy should not the offering be regarded merely as an act producing in the food some transcendental effect (and not as a real offering meant to be accepted by the teacher)?тАЭ

That it is not so is proved by historical evidence: says the revered Vy─Бsa in the story of Hс╣Ыtak┼лpa, where it is distinctly stated that the teacher actually took what was offered.

That the boy should eat only after being permitted to do so, is laid down in several Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtras.

тАШWith his face to the east, after having sipped tenter.тАЩтАФSome people have asserted that the facing of the east is meant to be connected with the sipping of water,тАФthe two being in close proximity. But this is not right; as the rule regarding sippingтАФthat it should be done with the face towards the east or north,тАФwill come later on. Hence what is mentioned here is connected with the eating.

тАШPure.тАЩтАФThis means that after rinsing the mouth he should avoid, during meals, such tilings as looking at the C─Бс╣Зс╕Н─Бla going to unclean places, spitting and so forth.тАФ(51)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in Smс╣Ыtitattva (p. 936);тАФin Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 454), which latter adds that in the event of the Teacher not being near at hand, the food is to be offered to the TeacherтАЩs wife or son, or to his own companions,тАФin Apar─Бrka (p. 60);тАФin Saс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (p. 61), which explains тАШAm─Бyay─БтАЩ as that he should not conceal the better quality of food obtained - out of fear that the Teacher will take it for himself;тАФand in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 113).

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

Gautama-Dharmas┼лtra, 2.46-47.тАФтАШHaving offered it to the Teacher, he should eat it when permitted; in the absence of the Teacher, he should offer it to his wife or to his son or to his own fellow-students.тАЩ

Gautama-Dharmas┼лtra (Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava, p. 454).тАФтАШMorning and evening, he shall eat food which is respected, never decried.тАЩ

─Аpastamba-Dharmasutra, 1.3.31-35.тАФтАШHaving collected it, he should describe it to the Teacher; he should eat it on being permitted by him; during the TeacherтАЩs absence, he should offer it to the TeacherтАЩs family; during the absence of these also, to other Vedic scholars; he should never beg alms for himself alone.тАЩ

─Аpastamba-Dharmas┼лtra, 11.37.1.тАФтАШFood should be eaten, with face towards the East.тАЩ

Viс╣гс╣Зu-Smс╣Ыti, 27.9.тАФтАШAlms should be begged from qualified persons, never from the TeacherтАЩs family; the food obtained should be eaten only with his permission.тАЩ

Y─Бj├▒avalkya, 1.31.тАФтАШHaving done his duty to the Fires, he should eat his food silently, with the TeacherтАЩs permission, after having sipped water.тАЩ

─А┼Ыval─Бyana-Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtra, 1.22.9.тАФтАШhe should offer it to the Teacher and then rest during the rest of the day.тАЩ

P─Бraskara-Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtra, 2.5.8.тАФтАШHe offers the alms obtained to the Teacher; and then he should rest (luring the rest of the day, with speech controlled,тАФтАШso say some.тАЩ

  • рдпрддреН рддреБ рд╡рд┐рдзрд┐рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрд╛рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рджреН рдЕрд░реНрдерд╡рд╛рдж рдПрд╡рд╛рдпрдВ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╢реЗрд╖ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЪреЛрдХреНрддрдГ рдкрд░рд┐рд╣рд╛рд░рдГ рд╡рдЪрдирд╛рдирд┐ рддреНрд╡реН рдЕрдкреВрд░реНрд╡рддреНрд╡рд╛рджреН рдЗрддрд┐ ред рди рдЪ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реИрдХрд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрддрд╛рд╣реЗрддреБрд░реН рд╡рд┐рднрдЬреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╕рд╛рдХрд╛рдЩреНрдХреНрд╖рддреНрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рд░реН рдЕрд╕реНрддрд┐ ред рдпрджреНрдпреН рдЕрдкреНрдпреН рдЙрддреНрддрд░реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдЪреИрддрджреН рдЕрд╡рд░реЛрдзреАрддреНрдпреН рдЕрдиреЗрдирд╛рддрд┐рджреЗрд╢реЗрди рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдордЪрд╛рд░рд┐рдзрд░реНрдореЛ рд╜рдкрд┐ рдкреБрд░реБрд╖рдорд╛рддреНрд░рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН рдлрд▓рдВ рддреБ рди рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН ред рдЧреБрдгрдХрд╛рдордирд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рд╣рд┐ рдирд╛рддрд┐рджреЗрд╢рд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрддреНрддрд┐рдореН рдЕрдиреБрдордиреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ ред “рдЧреЛрджреЛрд╣рдиреЗрди рдкрд╢реБрдХрд╛рдорд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рдгрдпреЗрддреН” (рдЖрд╢реНрд╢реН рез.резрем.реи), “рдЦрд╛рджрд┐рд░рдВ рд╡реАрд░реНрдпрдХрд╛рдорд╕реНрдп” (рд╖рдбреНрдмреН рек.рек) рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рдХреГрддреЗрд╖реБ рдиреЗрд╖реНрдпрддреЗ рдХреИрд╢реНрдЪрд┐рддреН рее реи.релреи рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The preceding verse has laid down the general compulsory rule that the boy should eat with his face to the East, if he is not desirous of obtaining any peculiar results; the text is now laying down rules that are to he observed with a view to definite desired ends.

тАШ─Аyuс╣гyamтАЩтАФis that which is conducive to longevity; and тАШEating with face to the East, one does what is coducive to longevityтАЩ; when the act of eating brings about longevity, it becomes тАШwhat is conducive to longevity тАЩ; hence the meaning of the text comes to be that тАШif one desires longevity he should eat with face to the East.тАЩ Thus then, in regard to the East, there are two directionsтАФ(a) one should always face the East, and (b) one should do so when desiring the said result; so that if a man desires longevity, he should actually have the particular desire in view; while in the other case he should not have any result in view. Just as, though the Agnihotra is an obligatory act, yet if the man seeks heaven, he repeats its performance; and by so doing he fulfills, incidentally, the obligations of the obligatory act also.

Similarly, when one desires fame, he should face the South. All these rules are optional.

Desiring prosperityтАФthe form тАШShriyanтАЩ is formed by adding the present participial affix тАШ┼Ыatс╣ЫтАЩ to the nominal root formed by adding тАШkyachтАЩ to the noun тАШ┼Ъr─лтАЩ Or, we may read тАШShriyamтАЩ ending in m; the meaning being тАШwhat brings prosperityтАЩ; just as in the case of the other words тАШ─Бyuс╣гyamтАЩ and the rest.

The use of the root тАШbhuj,тАЩ тАШto eat,тАЩ in its literal sense becomes possible, if we regard тАШlongevityтАЩ and the rest as тАШparts of a living beingтАЩ; the same explanation applies also to the next clause тАШhe eats what leads to the true.тАЩ The meaning thus comes to be that byтАШeating with face to the west one obtains prosperity.тАЩ In this case we have the reading тАШshriyamтАЩ with the Accusative ending. Or, lastly we may read тАШshriyai,тАЩ with the Dative ending, which would signify тАШfor the sake of.тАЩ

тАШTrueтАЩ means the real, and also the sacrifice or Heaven as resulting from the sacrifice. The sense thus is that тАШif one seeks heaven he should eat with his face to the north.тАЩ

Even though we have no Injunctive affixes in the text, yet, since what is here laid down is something not already known, we take it in the sense of an Injunction, construing the Present Tense as denoting the fifth sense (Leс╣н, which is expressive of Injunction).

Thus then we have this rule of eating with face to various directions, with a view to various results.

Eating with face towards the subsidiary quarters, which one might be tempted to do undor special circumstances, becomes precluded by the obligatory injunction of facing the East, etc.

The optional rule here laid down does not apply only to the Religious Student, nor to the eating of the food obtained by begging only, but to all forms of eating by the Householder and others also. That this is so is indicated by the fact that though in the context we have all along had the Injunctive word тАШa┼Ыn─лy─Бt,тАЩ the present veise has used a different word тАШbhuс╣ЕkteтАЩ; if the author had definitely intended the present rule to be as restricted in its application as those that have gone before, then he would have used the same word. When however we find him making use of a different word, тАШbhuс╣Еkte,тАЩ we begin to doubt if what is meant is the particular eating that has been hitherto dealt with in the context, or a general rule applying to all forms of eating; and the conclusion we are led to is that since a different verb is used, it must stand for a different act, and it cannot be regarded as the same that has been dealt with in the context.

Some people have argued thatтАФтАЬin as much as there is no injunctive word in the present verse, it must be taken as merely laudatory of what has gone before.тАЭ But this has been answered in M─лm─Бms─Б S┼лtra 3.5.21 (where it is asserted that sentences laying down things not already known are to be regarded as injunctive). Nor do we find in the present verse any such signs as would indicate that it is meant to be subsidiary to the preceding verse,тАФsuch signs, for instance, as the fact of its being wanting in some integral part, if taken apart from the preceding verse, and so forth. It is possible to take the present verse as referring primarily to the Religious Student only, and then to extend its application to all men,тАФon the ground that what is laid down here is not incompatible with the duties of ordinary men, as the other duties of the Student are; but in that case the results mentioned in the verse would not accrue to the ordinary man. For authoritative writers 8.1.23, etc.) do not admit of activity by mere implied extension, in cases of special results following from the use of special accessory details. If such rules as тАШfor one desiring cattle, water should be fetched in the milking vessel,тАЩ тАШthe sacrificial post should be of khadira wood when the man desires vigour,тАЩ are never applied to the case of those sacrifices which are mere ectypes (of the Dar┼Ыap┼лrс╣З─Бm─Бsa); and to which the details of the Dar┼Ыap┼лrс╣Зam─Бsa become applicable by extended implication only.тАФ(52)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

тАШс╣ЪtamтАЩтАФтАШSacrifice,тАЩ an alternative explanation suggested by, Medh─Бtithi and N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa.

Medh─Бtithi (p. 97, L 20)тАФтАШGuс╣Зak─Бman─Бy─Бm hi, &c.тАЩ

This refers to M─лm─Бс╣Гs─Б S┼лtra 8.1.23 et. seq.

This verse is quoted in Smс╣Ыtitattva, (p. 431) which remarks that the verse refers to cases where a man makes it a rule to always face a certain quarter at meals;тАФin Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 34), which adс╕Нs the explanation that ┼Ыr─лyam and с╣Ыtam are objects to the present-participle тАШicchanтАЩ;тАФin Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 377) in support of the view that facing of the south is not interdicted when done with a special motive. Vidh─Бnap─Бrij─Бta (p. 324) also quotes the verse to show that what is here prescribed applies to that eating which is done with a special motive, the general law being that one should face the east or the north .тАФApar─Бrka (p. 61) quotes the verse, and adds the following explanation:тАФIf one eats facing the east, it brings longevity; one who eats facing the west, obtains prosperity; who eats facing the north attains the truth or the sacrifice.тАФThus eating with face towards the east is both compulsory (as laid down in the preceding verse) and optional, done with a special motive (as mentioned here).

It is quoted in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 115), which adds the following notesтАФтАШ─Бyuс╣гyamтАЩ means тАШconducive to longevityтАЩтАФone who eats facing the east obtains longevity; hence the meaning of the text is that тАШone who seeks for longevity should eat facing the east similarly тАШya┼ЫasyamтАЩ meaning conducive to fameтАЩ;тАФeating with face towards the south brings fameтАФand similarly one who seeks for wealth should eat facing the west, and he who seeks for тАШс╣Ыt─БтАЩ i. e., the truth, should eat facing the north.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

Viс╣гс╣Зu-Smс╣Ыti, 67. 40-41.тАФтАШHe should eat facing the East, or the South.тАЩ

Gobhila (Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava, p. 377).тАФтАШThe Br─Бhmaс╣Зa may sit facing the East, or the West; in connection with rites in honour of Pitс╣Ыs, even the North; but the South he must avoid.тАЩ

Mah─Бbh─Бrata (─А┼Ыvamedhika-Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava, p. 395).тАФтАШOne shall eat with wet feet, facing the East, with his two feet or even one touching the ground.тАЩ

Old Saying (Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava, p. 309).тАФтАШOne should eat seated, facing the east, with speech in check, not decrying the food, nor scattering it, with mind concentrated on it: and having eaten he shall sip water.тАЩ

052 (His meal will procure) long life, if he eats facing the east; fame, if he turns to the south; prosperity, if he turns to the west; truthfulness, if he faces the east.

The twice-b orn person should always take his food after having sipped water and with due care; and after having eaten, he should rinse his mouth in the proper manner and touch the cavities with water.тАФ(53).

  • рдЕрддреНрд░ рдХреЗрдЪрд┐рдиреН рдордиреНрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рд╢реБрджреНрдзреНрдпрд░реНрдердореН рдПрдХрдореН рдЖрдЪрдордирдореН, “рд╕реБрдкреНрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдХреНрд╖реБрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдЪ рднреБрдХреНрддреНрд╡рд╛ рдЪ” (рдореНрдзреН рел.резрекрел) рдЗрддрд┐ рдЕрдиреЗрдирд╛рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд░реНрдердВ рджреНрд╡рд┐рддреАрдпрдВ рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдореН ред рдПрд╡рдВ рдЪ рдкрдареНрдпрддреЗ " рдЖрдЪрд╛рдиреНрддрдГ рдкреБрдирд░реН рдЖрдЪрд╛рдореЗрддреН" (рдпреНрдзреН рез.резрепрем) рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдПрддрддреН рдкрдЮреНрдЪрдореЗ рд╕реНрдерд╛рдкрдпрд┐рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдордГ ред

  • рд╕рдореНрдпрдЧреН рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡реИрдзрддрд╛рдореН рдЖрдЪрдордирдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╕реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рджрддрд┐ ред “рдпрд╛рджреГрд╢реЛ рд╡рд┐рдзрд┐рд░реН рдЙрдХреНрддрд╕реН рддрдВ ред рддрд╕реНрдп рд╕рдВрдкреВрд░реНрдгрд╛рдЩреНрдЧрд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рдпреЛрдЧреЛ рд╡рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрддреЗ “рд╢реМрдЪреЗрдкреНрд╕реБрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджрд╛рдЪрд╛рдореЗрддреН” рдЗрддрд┐ (рдореНрдзреН реи.ремрез) ред рдпрджреН75 рд╡рд╛ рд╡рд┐рдзрд┐рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрднрд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рд░реНрдердВ рд╢рд╛рд╕реНрддреНрд░реАрдпрдореН рдПрддрджреН рдЖрдЪрдордирдВ рди рд▓реМрдХрд┐рдХрдореН рдЗрддрд┐ рд╕рдкрд░рд┐рдХрд░рд╕реНрдпреЗрддрд┐ рдпрджреН рдЙрдХреНрддрдВ рддрджреН рджрд░реНрд╢рд┐рддрдВ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рее реи.релрей рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The terms тАШ─БcamanaтАЩ and тАШspс╣Ы┼ЫaтАЩ are both synonymous, being found from the usage of cultured people, to signify a particular purificatory act. Though it is true that the root тАШsprahaтАЩ has been declared to have an entirely different meaning, and the root тАШchamuтАЩ (from which the word тАШ─БcamanaтАЩ is derived) also has been declared to signify the act of eating,тАФyet in actual usage we find that with the particular prefixes (upa and a) they are used in a much restricted sense and hence they are taken in that (restricted) sense. So that even though the root тАШspс╣Ы┼ЫaтАЩ has a very wide denotation, yet actual usage limits its significance. Just as though the root тАШgaс╕НiтАЩ denotes only part of the face in general, the term тАШgaс╣Зс╕НaтАЩ (derived from that root) is used in the sense of tho cheek only, and it is not applied to any other part of the face; similarly the root тАШpuс╣гyaтАЩ means to accomplish, and the term тАШpuс╣гyaтАЩ is laid down as denoting тАШlunar, asterismтАЩ in general, yet in actual usage this latter name is applied to one particular asterism only; similarly again the term тАШdh─Бyy─Б,тАЩ though laid down as denoting S─Бmidhen─л verses in general, is actually used in the sense of the ─Аv─Бpik─л verses only. Hence the term тАШupaspс╣Ы┼ЫyaтАЩ means exactly what is meant by the term тАШ─БcamyaтАЩ; the actual injunction of this act of тАШ─БcamanaтАЩ will come later on. Further, the text itself uses the two terms as synonymous. Having laid down that тАШone should always do the shana,тАЩ it goes on to say that тАШthis ─БcamanaтАЩ should be done three times; from which it is clear that the two are synonymous.

Though the тАШrinsing of the mouthтАЩ has been already laid down in verse 51, it is re-iterated again in order to show immediate sequence: the sense being that one should take his food immediately after rinsing the mouth, and no other act should be allowed to intervene. To this end we have the following declaration of the revered Vy─БsaтАФтАШOh Lord, I shall remain with such people as take their food with five limbs wetтАЩтАФthis being said by Lakс╣гm─л; the тАШfive limbsтАЩ being the two hands, two feet, and month; and these five limbs can remain wet only if one cats immediately after the rinsing, and not if he makes any delay. Manu himself (in 4. 76) is going to declare under the duties of the Sn─Бtaka that тАШone should eat with the feet still wetтАЩ; and there we shall show that there is no needless repetition involved in this.

тАШAlwaysтАЩтАФthis is added in order to guard against the notion that being laid down in the section dealing with the duties of the Student, what is here prescribed applies to him alone; and to show directly that it is applicable to every form of eating.

Some people have held that тАЬthe term тАШtwice-bornтАЩ is what is meant to make the rule applicable to every form of eating, and that the тАШalwaysтАЩ is merely an explanatory reiteration.тАЭ

This however is not right. This would have been the right explanation if the qualification тАШtwice-bomтАЩ were incompatible with the тАШstudentтАЩ; as a matter of fact however, the said qualification is quite applicable to the тАШstudentтАЩ; hence with the exception of the adverb тАШalwaysтАЩ there is nothing to indicate that what is here laid down is to be taken as going beyond the particular context.

тАШWith due careтАЩтАФThat is, with due consideration of the character of the food and his own (digestive) powers. If one happens to be absent-minded, he cannot avoid indigestible, unwholesome and hot food, nor can he eat only what is wholesome.

тАШAfter having eaten, he should rinse his mouth.тАЩтАФThat one should remove all traces of oil, etc., has been already prescribed under the section on the тАШpurification of substances.тАЩ The тАШrinsingтАЩ here laid down is that which one should do after he has eaten and removed all traces of oil, etc.

In this connection some people have held that one тАШrinsingтАЩ (after food) having been already laid down under 5. 145тАФwhere it is said that тАШone should rinse his mouth after sleep, sneezing and eating,тАЩтАФthe present verse must be taken as laying down a second тАШrinsing,тАЩ for the purposes of some transcendental result; there being such a general injunction as тАШhaving rinsed the mouth, one should rinse it again.тАЩ

This aspect of the question wo shall deal with under Discourse V.

In the proper manner.тАФThis only re-iterates the injunctive and obligatory character of the тАШrinsingтАЩ; the meaning being that тАШone should follow all the details of the Binning that have been enjoined.тАЩ

тАШShould touch with water the cavities.тАЩтАФтАШCavities,тАЩ i.e., holes in the head.

Objection.тАФтАЬIt is already laid down (under 60, below) that the cavities should be touched with water.тАЭ

To this some people reply that the repetition in the present verse is meant to exclude the тАШselfтАЩ and тАШheadтАЩ (which also are mentioned along with the тАШcavitiesтАЩ in 60),тАФand refers to that rinsing which one already clean, does, without reference to Eating. So that according to those who take the first тАШrinsingтАЩ after food as meant for cleanliness and a second тАШrinsingтАЩ as lending to some transcendental result,тАФthe тАШselfтАЩ and the тАШheadтАЩ are not тАШtouched with waterтАЩ for the purpose of bringing about a transcendental result; this being done for cleanliness alone. The actual process of this rinsing is going to he laid down in 61.тАФтАШOne desirous of cleanliness should always rinse his mouth, etc., etc..тАЩ

Another answer to the aforesaid objection is that what the present verse does is to emphasise the fact of the being recognised as something enjoined by the scriptures; the sense being that this Rinsing is the scriptural (prescribed in the ┼Ъ─Бstras), not the ordinary, rinsing. As a matter of fact, where a certain primary act has become known as equipped with particular accessories, wherever that same act is subsequently spoken of, it is at once recognised as being the same as the former one. So that when the text says тАШshould rinse his mouth,тАЩ it does not mean merely that a certain substance (water) should be sipped; what is meant is to indicate all that has been prescribed in connection with the scriptural purification, along with its appurtenent details.тАФ(53)

тАШNityamтАЩтАФThis, according to Govindar─Бja, Kull┼лka N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa and Nandana indicates that the rule refers to householders also. The first half of this verse has been quoted in Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 327).

рдЕрд╢реНрдпрдд рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрд╢рдирдВ рднрдХреНрддрд╕рдХреНрддреНрд╡рдкреВрдкрд╛рджреНрдпреН76 рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рддрджреН рдЕрд╢рдирд╛рд░реНрдердореН рдЖрдиреАрддрдВ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛рд░реВрдкреЗрдг рдкрд╢реНрдпреЗрддреН- “рдПрд╖рд╛ рд╡реИ рдкрд░рдорд╛ рджреЗрд╡рддрд╛ рдпрджреН рдЕрдиреНрдирдореН” ред рддрд╕реНрдп рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рднреВрддрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕реНрд░рд╖реНрдЯреГрддреНрд╡реЗрди рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрд┐рд╣реЗрддреБрддрдпрд╛ рдЪ рдпрджреНрджрд░реНрд╢рдирдВ рд╕рд╛рд╕реНрдп рдкреВрдЬрд╛ ред рдЕрде рд╡рд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рд░реНрдерддреНрд╡реЗрди рднрд╛рд╡рдирдВ рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпрдиреН-77 “рдпрдЬрдиреН рдордо рдпрджреН рдЕрд░реНрдерддреНрд╡рдВ рд╕рдВрдкреВрдЬрдпрддрд┐ рдорд╛рдВ рд╕рджрд╛” рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдирдорд╕реНрдХрд╛рд░рд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ рд╡рд╛ рдкреНрд░рдгрдореНрдп рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгрдВ рдкреВрдЬрд╛ ред

  • рдЕрджреНрдпрд╛рдЪреН рдЪреИрддрджреН рдЕрдХреБрддреНрд╕рдпрдиреН ред рдХрджрдиреНрдирддрдпрд╛ рджреБрдГрд╕рдВрд╕реНрдХрд╛рд░реЛрдкрдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгреЗрди рд╡рд╛ рдХреБрддреНрд╕рд╛рд╣реЗрддреБрд╕рдВрднрд╡реЗ рдирд╛рдиреНрдирдВ рдХреБрддреНрд╕рдпреЗрддреН ред “рдХрд┐рдореН рдЗрджрдореН рдЕрд╢реНрдпрддреЗ, рдЕрд░реБрдЪрд┐рдХрд░рдВ рдзрд╛рддреБрд╡реИрд╖рдореНрдпрдЬрдирдХрдореН” рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдПрд╡рдорд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛рднрд┐рдзрд╛рдиреЗрди рдирд╛рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреЗрддреН ред рдпрджрд┐ рддреБ рддрджреНрд░реВрдкрдВ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рддрджрд╛ рдирд╛рджреНрдпрд╛рдиреН рди рдХреБрддреНрд╕рдпрдиреНрдиреН рдЕрджреНрдпрд╛рддреН ред

рджреГрд╖реНрдЯреНрд╡реИрд╡ рд╣реГрд╖реНрдпреЗрддреН ред рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╕реНрддреНрд░реНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рд╕рдВрджрд░реНрд╢рдиреЗрди рдЪрд┐рд░рдкреНрд░рд╡рд╛рд╕рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдЧрдд рдЗрд╡реН рддреБрд╖реНрдпреЗрдд рдкреНрд░реАрдпреЗрдд ред рдкреНрд░рд╕реАрджреЗрдЪреН рдЪ ред рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддрд╛рдиреНрддрд░рдЬрдореН рдЕрдкрд┐ рдХрд╛рд▓реБрд╖реНрдпрдореН рдЕрдиреНрдирджрд░реНрд╢рдиреЗрди рд╣рд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ рдордирдГрдкреНрд░рд╕рд╛рджрдореН рдЖрд╢реНрд░рдпреЗрддреН ред рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдирдиреНрджреЗрдЪреН рдЪ ред рд╕рдореГрджреНрдзреНрдпрд╛ рд╢рдВрд╕рдирдВ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдирдиреНрджрдирдореН ред “рдирд┐рддреНрдпрдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛ рдПрддреЗрди рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдо” рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЖрджрд░реЛрдкрджрд░реНрд╢рдирдореН рдЕрднрд┐рдирдиреНрджрдирдореН ред рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╢рдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджрд╛ ред “рдЕрдиреНрдпрддрд░рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдореН” рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рд╕реНрдерд┐рддрд╡рд┐рднрд╛рд╖рд╛рд╡рд┐рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рддреН рд╕рдкреНрддрдореНрдпрд░реНрдереЗ рд╢рдореН рдХрд░реНрддрд╡реНрдпрдГ ред рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджреЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд╛ рдкрдард┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдореН рее реи.релрек рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШFood,тАЩ тАШa┼Ыana,тАЩ is that which in eaten (a┼Ыyate), i.e., rice and curry, etc. When the food is brought to him, he should look upon it as a тАШdeityтАЩ; i.e., he should have the notionтАФтАШthis food is my highest deity.тАЩ (a) The тАШworshippingтАЩ of the food may consist in regarding it as the source of the birth and sustenance of all living beings; or (b) in regarding it as the means of sustaining his life; as the food is declared to have saidтАФтАШhe worships me regarding me as sustaining lifeтАЩ; or (c) in receiving it with due obeisance, etc.

тАШHe should eat it without disparaging itтАЩ;тАФeven when there is any such source of disparagement as that the article of food is of bad quality, or it is badly cooked, he should not disparage the food; i.e., he should not make any such disparaging remarks asтАФтАШthis is most disagreeable,тАЩ or тАШit is likely to upset the constitution of the body,тАЩ and so forth. If the food happens to be really defective, he should simply not eat it; he should not eat it and yet find fault with it.

тАШWhen he sees it he should rejoiceтАЩтАФhe should rejoice just as he does when, on returning from a long journey, he sees his wife and children.

тАШHe should feel gratifiedтАЩ;тАФon seeing the food, he should remove from his mind even such displeasure as may have been produced by other causes.

тАШHe should welcome itтАЩ;тАФтАШwelcomingтАЩ consists in acclaiming it as a boon; i.e., receiving it with honour, with such words as тАШmay we have such food every day.тАЩ

тАШAlways,тАЩтАФat all times. The affix тАШshasтАЩ has the sense of the locative, according to the option involved in P─Бс╣ЗiniтАЩs S┼лtra 5. 4. 42. Or, wo may read тАШsarvad─БтАЩ (instead of тАШsarva┼Ыaс╕етАЩ).тАФ(54)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

P┼лjayetтАФтАШworshipтАЩ (Govindar─Бja and Nandana.);тАФMedh─Бtithi offers three explanations as to what is meant by the тАШworshippingтАЩ of the food;тАФN─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa takes it to mean that the mantra (с╣Ъgveda, 1. 187.1) should be addressed to it Kull┼лka explains it as тАШmeditate upon it as sustaining lifeтАЩ.

The first half of the verse is quoted in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 486), which explains the p┼лj─Б as standing for saс╣Гsk─Бra, due preparation.

It is quoted again in the ─Аhnika section of the same work (p. 382), where, on the strength of a statement attributed to ┼Ъ─Бt─Бtapa, it is said that in the case of food, тАШworshipтАЩ can only mean being regarded as a deity.

The verse is quoted in Smс╣Ыtitattva (p. 433);тАФand in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 114), which explains тАШakutsayanтАЩ as тАШnot decrying.тАЩ

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

**(Verses 54-55)

Y─Бj├▒avalkya, 1. 31,тАФтАШHe should eat the food, paying due regard to it, not disparaging it.тАЩ

Baudh─Бyana-Dharmas┼лtra, 7.2.6.тАФтАШSeatedтАФhe should eat the food, intent upon it, without disparaging the food,тАФnot dropping it on the ground; and after earing, he should touch Fire.тАЩ

Viс╣гс╣Зu-Smс╣Ыti, 67.42-43.тАФтАШWorshipping the food, with contented mind, wearing a garland and smeared with sandal-paste.тАЩ

Baudh─Бyana Dhaс╣Ыmas┼лtra, 2.3.17.тАФтАШ[Says the Food]тАФHe who eats me, without having made offerings to Pitс╣Ыs, Gods, dependents, guests, and to friends, eats, through foolishness, poison; and him I devour; for him I am death. He who eats me after having made the Agnihotra-ofFerings and the Vai┼Ыvadeva-offerings and after having honoured the guests and fed his dependents,тАФcontent, clean and reverential,тАФfor him I am nectar; he alone eats me.тАЩ

054 Let him always worship his food, and eat it without contempt; when he sees it, let him rejoice, show a pleased face, and pray that he may always obtain it.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдореВрд▓рд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The food, thus worshipped always, imparts strength and vigour. If eaten irreverently, it destroys them both.тАФ(55)

рдореЗрдзрд╛рддрд┐рдерд┐рдГ

рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╡рд┐рдзрд┐рд╢реЗрд╖реЛ рд╜рдпрдореН рдЕрд░реНрдерд╡рд╛рджрдГ, рди рддреБ рдлрд▓рд╡рд┐рдзрд┐рдГ ред рдлрд▓рд╡рд┐рдзреМ78 рд╣рд┐ рдХрд╛рдореНрдпреЛ рд╜рдпрдВ рд╡рд┐рдзрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рджреН рдКрд░реНрдЬрдХрд╛рдорд╕реНрдп рдмрд▓рдХрд╛рдорд╕реНрдп рдЪ ред рддрддрд╢реН рдЪ рдирд┐рддреНрдпрд╢рдмреНрджреЛ рдиреЛрдкрдкрджреНрдпреЗрдд рдкреВрдЬрд┐рддрдВ рд╣реНрдпреН рдЕрд╢рдирдВ рдирд┐рддреНрдпрдореН рдЗрддрд┐ ред рдЕрддреЛ рд╜рдпрдВ рдпрд╛рд╡рдЬреНрдЬреАрд╡рд┐рдХрдГ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЩреНрдореБрдЦрддрд╛ рдирд┐рдпрдордГ ред рдЕрдкреВрдЬрд┐рддрдВ рднреБрдХреНрддрдВ рд╣реНрдпреН рдЙрднрдпрдВ рдирд╛рд╢рдпреЗрджреН рдмрд▓рдореН рдКрд░реНрдЬрдВ рдЪ ред рдмрд▓рдВ рд╕рд╛рдорд░реНрдереНрдпрдореН рдЕрдирд╛рдпрд╛рд╕реЗрди рднрд╛рд░реЛрджреНрдпрдордирд╛рджрд┐рд╢рдХреНрддрддрд╛ ред рдХреГрд╢рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдпреН рдКрд░реНрдЬрдВ рдорд╣рд╛рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрддрд╛ ред рдЕрдЩреНрдЧреЛрдкрдЪрдпрдГ рдорд╣рд╛рдХрд╛рдпреЛ рдорд╣рд╛рдмрд▓рд╢реН рдЪ рднрд╡рддрд┐ рее реи.релрел рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

This verse is only a valedictory supplement to the rule prescribed above; it is not meant to be the statement of definite results following from the observance of that rule. If it were a statement of results, the rule would be an optional one, to be observed only by one who desires vigour and strength; and in that case the adverb тАШalwaysтАЩ would have no sense;тАФas we have in the expression, тАШthe food thus worshipped always, etc.тАЩ For these reasons the rule must be regarded as one to be observed throughout life, just like the rule regarding facing of the east (during meal).

тАШIf eaten irreverently, it destroys them both,тАЩтАФi.e., vigour and strength.

тАШStrength’ is power, the capacity to lift heavy loads without effort; while тАШvigourтАЩstands for energy and courage, which is found even in a man who is lean (and physically weak): while great strength is found only when the limbs of the body are well-developed and the body has attained huge proportions.тАФ(55)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

тАШ┼кrjamтАЩ.тАФBuhler wrongly attributes to Medh─Бtithi the explanation that this term means тАШbulkтАЩ. The term used by him is тАШmah─Бpr─Бс╣Зat─БтАЩ which means the same as тАШv─лryaтАЩ of Kull┼лka or тАШenergyтАЩ of N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa. Buhler has apparently been misled by a mis-reading of Medh─Бtithi.

This verse has been quoted in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 486) where тАШp┼лjitamтАЩ has been explained as, тАШsamskс╣ЫtamтАЩ, well prepared;тАФand in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 114).

He should not give the leavings to anyone; he should not eat in between; he should not do over-rating; and he should not go any-where with particles of food still on him.тАФ(56)

  • рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд╛рд╢рдмреНрджреЛ рдордзреНрдпрд╡рдЪрдирдГ ред рджреНрд╡реМ рднреЛрдЬрдирдХрд╛рд▓реМ рд╕рд╛рдпрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рддрд╢реН рдЪ ред рддрддреЛ рд╜рдиреНрдпрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рдХрд╛рд▓реЗ рди рднреБрдЮреНрдЬреАрдд ред рдЕрде рд╡рд╛ рд╡реНрдпрд╡рдзрд╛рдиреЗ рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд╛рд╢рдмреНрджрдГ ред рддреНрдпрдХреНрддрднреЛрдЬрдирд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрд╛рд░рдГ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдиреНрддрд░реЗрдг рд╡реНрдпрд╡рдзрд╛рдп рдкреБрдирд╕реН рддрджреН рдПрд╡ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдХреНрдкрд╛рддреНрд░рдЧреГрд╣реАрддрдВ рди рднреБрдЮреНрдЬреАрдд ред рд╕реНрдореГрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрд░реЗ рддреБ рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ рдкрдареНрдпрддреЗ- “рдЙрддреНрдерд╛рдирд╛рдЪрдордирд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреЗрддрдореН” рдЗрддрд┐ (рдЪреНреЬреНред рдЧреНрдзреН резрен.резреп) ред рдХреЗрдЪрд┐рддреН рддреБ рд╡рд┐рдЪреНрдЫреЗрджрдореН рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рдореН рдЖрдЪрдХреНрд╖рддреЗ ред “рд╕рд╡реНрдпреЗрди рдкрд╛рдгрд┐рдирд╛ рдкрд╛рддреНрд░рдореН рдЕрдиреНрд╡рд╛рд▓рднреНрдп рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгреЗрдирд╛рд╡рджрд╛рдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдпрд╛рд╕реНрдпреЗ рдЬреБрд╣реЛрддрд┐” рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реВрдпрддреЗ ред рддрддреНрд░ рдпрдГ рд╕рд╡реНрдпреЗрди рдкрд╛рддреНрд░рд╕реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрдЧреНрд░рд╣рд╕реН рддрджрдирдиреНрддрд░рдореН ред

  • рди рдЪреИрд╡рд╛рддреНрдпрд╢рдирдореН рдЕрддрд┐рдорд╛рддреНрд░рдореН рдЕрд╢рдирдВ рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рддреН ред рдПрддрдЪреН рдЪрд╛рдирд╛рд░реЛрдЧреНрдпрдХрд╛рд░рдгрдВ рдЧреБрд░реБрд╡рд┐рд░реБрджреНрдзрд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рджрд░реНрд╢рдирд╛рд░реНрдердореН ред рд╣реЗрддреВрдкрджреЗрд╢рд╛рдиреН рдорд╛рддреНрд░рд╛рд╢рд┐рддрд╛рдпрд╛рд╢реН рдЪрд╛рдпреБрд░реНрд╡реЗрджрд╛рджреН рдЕрддрд┐рдорд╛рддреНрд░рддрд╛ рдмреЛрджреНрдзрд╡реНрдпрд╛ ред рдпрд╛рд╡рджреН рдЕрд╢рд┐рддрдореН рдЕрдиреНрдирдореН рдЙрджрд░рдкреВрд░рдВ рди рдХрд░реЛрддрд┐ рд╕рдореНрдпрдЧреН рдЬреАрд░реНрдпрддрд┐ рддрд╛рд╡рджреН рдЕрд╢рд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдореН ред рддреНрд░рдпрдГ рдХреБрдХреНрд╖реЗрд░реН рднрд╛рдЧрд╛рдГ, рдЕрдзреНрдпрд░реНрдзрдореН рдЕрдиреНрдирд╕реНрдп рднрд╛рдЧрд╛рд░реНрдзрдВ рдкрд╛рдирд╕реНрдп рднрд╛рдЧреЛ рджреЛрд╖рд╕рдВрдЪрд╛рд░рд╛рдп ред рдЕрдиреНрдпрдерд╛рдирд╛рд░реЛрдЧреНрдпрдореН ред

  • рди рдЪреЛрдЪреНрдЫрд┐рддреНрд╖реНрдЯрдГ рдХреНрд╡рдЪрд┐рджреН рд╡реНрд░рдЬреЗрддреН ред рдЕрддрд╢реН рдЪреЛрдЪреНрдЫрд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдореН рдЕрдкрдиреАрдп рд╢реБрдЪрд┐рддреНрд╡рдореН рдЖрдкрд╛рджрд┐рддреЗ рддрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдиреН рдПрд╡ рджреЗрд╢ рдЖрдЪрд╛рдиреНрддрд╡реНрдпрдореН рее реи.релрем рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The food left in the dish, and become unclean by being touched with the mouth, is called, тАШleavings;тАЩтАФthis he should not give to anyone. The prohibition of the offering of the leavings to any person being already contained in this verse, the necessity of having another prohibition of the offering of the leavings to a ┼Ъ┼лdra,тАФwhich we find among the duties of the Sn─Бtak─БтАФwe shall explain in connection with the latter verse.

[In тАШKasyachitтАЩ ] though the dative would he the proper form, we have the genitive in the sense of тАШrelationship in general,тАЩ and what is meant is that it should not he given even to such living beings as do not understand that a certain thing has been given to them,тАФsuch for instance, as dogs and cats; in this latter case the act cannot he called тАШgivingтАЩ in its full sense; as it involves merely the cessation of the proprietary right of the giver, it does not involve the producing of the proprietary right in the recipient [that is why the Dative could not he rightly used: which could imply both giving and receiving ].

The phrase тАШantar─БтАЩ тАШin between,тАЩ means middle. There are two times for mealsтАФmorning and evening; and one should not eat between these meals. Or, тАШin betweenтАЩ may mean interruption; in which case the meaning is that тАШhaving once left off the act of eating, and having interrupted it by some other act, he should not eat the food left in the same dish.тАЩ Another Smс╣Ыti lays down the specific rule that тАШone should avoid eating interrupted by rising and washing.тАЩ Others again have explained the phrase тАШantar─Б,тАЩ as meaning disconnection. The ┼Ъruti having declared that тАШholding the dish with the left hand, ono should take up the morsel with the right hand and then offer it to the Life-breath in the mouth,тАЩтАФit is the omitting of the act of holding the dish with the left hand which is meant by the terms тАШantar─Б.тАЩ

тАШBe should not do over-eatingтАЩ;тАФone should not eat too much. This is with a view to health, and hence implies the avoidance of such food as may he either indigestible or unsuitable. Specially because the advice is based upon reason. What is тАШover-eatingтАЩ can he learnt from the ─Аyurveda. The sense is that one should eat only that quantity of food which does not quite fill the stomach, and which is properly digested. Of the three parts into which the stomach is divided, one part itself should bo filled with food, half a part with water, and one part should be left for the action of the bodily humours. If this is not done, health suffers.

тАШHe should not go anywhere teiс╣нh particles of food still on himтАЩ;тАФon the very spot where he has oaten, he should clean himself by removing all particles of food from the body and then wash his hands and mouth without rising from the place.тАФ(50)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

The second half of this verse is quoted in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 458); in Apar─Бrka (p. 61) in support of the view that by avoiding over-eating one acquires health;тАФand in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 115).

056 Let him not give to any man what he leaves, and beware of eating between (the two meal-times); let him not over-eat himself, nor go anywhere without having purified himself (after his meal).
