рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдореВрд▓рд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

Over-eating destroys health, cuts off life and bars heaven; it is unrighteous and detested by people; for these reasons one should avoid it.тАФ(57)

рдореЗрдзрд╛рддрд┐рдерд┐рдГ

рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрдореВрд▓рддрд╛рдореН рдЕрддреНрдпрд╢рдирдкреНрд░рддрд┐рд╖реЗрдзрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЪрд╖реНрдЯреЗ83 ред рдЕрдирд╛рд░реЛрдЧреНрдпрдВ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдзреНрдпреБрддреНрдкрддреНрддрд┐рд░реН рдЬреНрд╡рд░реЛрджрд░рд╛рджрд┐рдкреАрдбрд╛ ред рд╡рд┐рд╖реВрдЪрд┐рдХрд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ рдЬреАрд╡рд┐рддрдирд╛рд╢ рдЕрдирд╛рдпреБрд╖реНрдпрдореН ред “рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдд рдПрд╡рд╛рддреНрдорд╛рдирдВ рдЧреЛрдкрд╛рдпреЗрддреН” (рдЧреНрдзреН реп.рейрек) рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢рд░реАрд░рдкрд░рд┐рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛рджрд┐рд╡реНрдпрддрд┐рдХреНрд░рдорд╛рджреН рдЕрд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрдЧреНрдпрдореН ред рдирд░рдХрдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд┐рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реНрдЧрд╛рднрд╛рд╡реЗрди рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрджреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдЕрдкреБрдгреНрдпрдВ рджреМрд░реНрднрд╛рдЧреНрдпрдХрд░рдореН ред рд▓реЛрдХрд╡рд┐рджреНрд╡рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдВ рдмрд╣реБрднреЛрдЬрд┐рддрдпрд╛ рдирд┐рдиреНрджреНрдпрддреЗ ред рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рдХрд╛рд░рдгрд╛рджреН рдЕрддреНрдпрд╢рдирдВ рдкрд░рд┐рд╡рд░реНрдЬрдпреЗрддреН, рди рдХреБрд░реНрдпрд╛рддреН рее реи.релрен рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The present verse proceeds to show that the prohibition of over-eating is based upon ordinary worldly considerations.

тАШDestroys health,тАЩтАФis productive of such diseases as fever, pain in the stomach and so forth.

тАШCuts off life,тАЩтАФdestroys life, bringing on such diseases as cholera and the like.

тАШBars heaven,тАЩтАФbecause implying the neglect of oneтАЩs body, it involves the transgressing of such scriptural injunctions as тАШone should guard himself against all things.тАЩ The тАШbarring of heavenтАЩ means going to hell.

тАШUnrighteousтАЩтАФproductive of misfortune.

тАШDetested by peopleтАЩ;тАФthe man who eats too much is always looked down upon as a тАШglutton.тАЩ

For these reasons one тАШshould avoid,тАЩ тАФ i.e., not doтАФover-eating.тАФ(57)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 488); in Apar─Бrka (p. 156);тАФand in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 115).

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

**(Verse 56-57)
**

See Comparative notes for [Verse 2.56].

B├╝hler

057 Excessive eating is prejudicial to health, to fame, and to (bliss in) heaven; it prevents (the acquisition of) spiritual merit, and is odious among men; one ought, for these reasons, to avoid it carefully.

Every time, the Br─Бhmana should sip water, either though the receptacle dedicated to Brahm─Б, or through that dedicated to Praj─Бpati, or through that dedicated to the тАШThrice-tenтАЩ (Gods); but never through that dedicated to the Pitс╣Ыs.тАФ(58)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The term тАШt─лrtha,тАЩ тАШReceptacle,тАЩ means a clean vessel containing water; тАШt─лrthaтАЩ (literally) is that which exists for the purpose of saving people, i.e., freeing them from their sins. In some places тАШt─лrthaтАЩ is explained as тАШthat by which people descend into water.тАЩ In the present context however it stands for that part of the palm of the hand which contains water; and we must take the word тАШt─лrthaтАЩ as applied to the hand, with a view to eulogise it, only figuratively; for water does not remain in the hand always (and as such it cannot be called t─лrtha in its literal sense).

Through the said receptacle, he should sip water.

тАШDedicated to Brahm─БтАЩ;тАФthis also is a figurative eulogy. The term means тАШthat of which Brahm─Б is the deityтАЩ; and certainly the said тАШReceptacle,тАЩ not being of the nature of a тАШsacrifice,тАЩ or of a тАШMantra,тАЩ could not be said to be тАШdedicated to a deity.тАЩ The special nominal affix in the word тАШbr─Бhma,тАЩ which denotes тАШdedication to a deity,тАЩ may however be justified on the assumption that the said receptacle resembles a тАШsacrificeтАЩ in certain characteristics, such as being the means of sanctification and so forth.

тАШEvery timeтАЩтАФi.e., for the purposes of cleanliness, as also as part of religious performances.

тАШK─БyaтАЩтАФтАШKaтАЩ stands for Praj─Бpati: hence тАШk─БyaтАЩ is that which is dedicated to Praj─Бpati.

Similarly that which is dedicated to the тАШthrice-tenтАЩтАФi.e., the GodsтАФis called the тАШtraida┼Ыikam.тАЩ The word тАШtraida┼ЫikamтАЩ is derived from тАШtrida┼ЫaтАЩ with the deif├мc affix тАШaс╣З,тАЩ and then the reflexive тАШka.тАЩ And the deific character in this case also is of the same kind as before (in the term тАШbr─БhmaтАЩ).

Through these receptacles one should sip water. The mention of the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa (Vipra) is not meant to be significant here. For special rules for the Kс╣гatriya, etc., are going to be added later on (in verse 62, et seq.); and unless we had a general rule, there could he no room for specifications [and it is the present verse alone that could be taken as formulating that general rule, and hence it could not be taken as restricted to. the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa only.]

тАШNot through that dedicated to the Pitс╣ЫsтАЩтАФi.e., never through that of which the Pitс╣Ыs are the deity; even in cases where the aforesaid parts of the hand are disabled by the presence of boils and pimples.

Objection.тАФтАЬThe mere fact of what is sacred to Pitс╣Ыs not having been enjoined makes it impossible to be used (why should the negation be re-iterated)?тАЭ

Answer.тАФThere is one danger in that: The next verse supplies the description of тАШthe receptacle dedicated to Pitс╣ЫsтАЩ; while there is no use for it laid down in the present context; so that when one would proceed to seek for the use to which this particular receptacle could lie put, he might form the idea that it is to be used in connection with the act (of sipping water) that forms the subject-matter of the context. When, h owever, wc have the direct prohibition (of this receptacle, in connection with water-sipping), we gather the use for it from its very name, and conclude that the offering of water and such other rites for the Pitс╣Ыs are to be performed with тАШthe receptacle dedicated to Pitс╣Ыs.тАЩ In this manner the eulogy also becomes consistent. The тАШreceptaclesтАЩ dedicated to Brahm─Б and the rest being directly enjoined as those to be used, people might be led into the mistake that in the absence of these the other may be used; hence with a view to prevent this it was only right to mention the Pitrya-t─лrtha also (as that which should never be used).тАФ(58)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in V─лramitrodaya (─Аhnika, p. 76), where it is noted that according to Hem─Бdri, the term тАШvipraтАЩ stands for all the three twice-born castes, on the ground that Y─Бj├▒avalkyaтАЩs text bearing on the subject uses the generic term тАШdvijaтАФbut this view is controverted on the ground that it is more reasonable to take, on the strength of ManuтАЩs use of the particular term тАШvipra,тАЩ the term тАШdvijaтАЩ of Y─Бj├▒avalkyaтАЩs text as standing for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa only, rather than the other way about; as in this there is no stretching of the term тАШdvijaтАЩ which is often used for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa only; while in the other case the natural meaning of the term тАШvipraтАЩ is unduly extended to other than Br─Бhmaс╣Зas. The writer goes on to quote Medh─БtithiтАЩs words (p. 100, 11.20-21)тАФтАЬThe mention of the Vipra is not meant to be significant here. For special rules for the Kс╣гatriya etc., are going to be added later on (in verse 62, et seq), and unless we had a general rule there could be no room for specifications; [and it is the present verse alone that could be taken as formulating that general rule, and hence it could not be taken as restricted to the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa only.тАЭ] (Translation pp. 306-307);тАФand traverses this argument, on the ground that the present text is not injunctive of ─Аcamana, and hence the special rule that follows in verse 62 regarding ─Бcamana can have no bearing upon this verse; the real injunction of ─Аcamana is contained in verse 61. Verse 58, therefore, it is concluded, must be taken only as enjoining a particular тАШt─лrthaтАЩ for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa.

Proceeding with the explanation of the verse, V─лramitrodaya addsтАФтАШnityak─БlamтАЩ meaning always; so that whenever ─Бcamana has got to be done, it should be done by the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa by anyone of the thfee methods herein described; and it adds that such is the тАШsvarasa,тАЩ тАШinclination,тАЩ of Medh─Бtithi also, which clearly refers to Medh─Бtithi, p. 100, 1. 22. It goes on to point out, however, that the view of many Digests is that as far as possible the Br─Бhmat─лrtha should be used.,тАФsuch being the implication of the qualification тАШnityak─Бlam,тАЩ which is more nearly related to the first option; and the other alternatives are to be taken up only when the Brahma t─лrtha is disabled.тАФтАШK─БyaтАЩ means тАШdedicated to Praj─Бpati,тАЩ and тАШTraida┼Ыika,тАЩ тАШdedicated to the gods.тАЩ

It goes on to add that, though there was no possibility for the тАШPitrya t─лrthaтАЩ to be employed,тАФit not being mentioned among those sanctioned,тАФyet it has been specially interdicted with a view to indicate that the Pitryat─лrtha is never to be used, not even when every one of the three t─лrthas permitted is impossible, through pimples and sores: so that in such emergencies, the t─лrtha to be employed would be the ─Аgneya and others.

This verse is quoted in Nity─Бch─Бraprad─лpa (p. 64 and p. 253), which notes that тАШK─Бyatraida┼Ыikabhy─БmтАЩ is the secondary alternative mentioned in view of the contingency of there being a wound or some incapacity in the тАШBr─Бhmat─лrtha;тАФin ┼Ъuddhikaumud─л (p. 339), which has the following noteтАФтАШK─БyaтАЩ is Pr─Бj─Бpatya; тАШTraida┼ЫikaтАЩ is Daiva; тАШnityak─БlamтАЩ indicates that the second and third alternatives are to be resorted to only in the event of the using of the first being impossible;тАФin ─Аc─Бramay┼лkha (p. 20), which explains traida┼ЫikamтАЩ as daivam;тАФin Smс╣Ыtis─Бroddh─Бra (p. 311), which connects the negative particle тАШnaтАЩ with the whole of the second line, and explains тАШbr─БhmaтАЩ as the base of the aс╣Еguс╣гс╣нha, тАШk─БyaтАЩ as pr─Бj─Бpatya, the base of the little finger, тАШtraida┼ЫikaтАЩ as daiva, the tip of the fingers, and тАШpitryaтАЩ the base of the index finger;тАФand in V─лramitrodaya (Paribh─Бс╣г─Б. p. 77), which quotes тАШMedh─БtithisтАЩ explanation of the derivation of the term тАШtraida┼ЫikamтАЩ.

B├╝hler

058 Let a Brahmana always sip water out of the part of the hand (tirtha) sacred to Brahman, or out of that sacred to Ka (Pragapati), or out of (that) sacred to the gods, never out of that sacred to the manes.

The part of the palm at the root of the thumb they call тАШthe receptacle dedicated to Brahm─БтАЩ; that which is at the root of the finger тАШSacred to Praj─БpatiтАЩ; that on the finger-tops тАШdedicated to the GodsтАЩ; and that which is below these two тАШdedicated to the Pitс╣Ыs.тАЩтАФ(59)

рдореЗрдзрд╛рддрд┐рдерд┐рдГ

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The тАШrootтАЩ of the thumb is its lower part; and the part, of the hand just below that root is the тАШreceptacle dedicated to Brahm─Б.тАЩтАФThe term тАШtalaтАЩ stands for the inner part (the palm). That inner portion of the hand which extends up to the long palm-line and faces oneтАЩs own eyes is the part тАШdedicated to Brahm─Б.тАЩ

That at the root of the fingers, above the horizontal palmline is тАШdedicated to Praj─Бpati.тАЩ

тАШThat on the tip of the fingers is dedicated to the GodsтАЩтАФEven though the term тАШaс╣ЕguliтАЩ forms the subordinate factor in the compound (тАШaс╣Еguli-muleтАЩ), yet it is construed with the term тАШagre,тАЩ for the simple reason that this latter is a relative term (and hence stands in need of a correlative).

тАШThat below these two is dedicated to the Pitс╣Ыs.тАЩтАФThis also is to be construed with the terms тАШaс╣ЕguliтАЩ and тАШaс╣Еguс╣гс╣нha,тАЩ though both of these form subordinate factors in the two compounds. The тАШfingerтАЩ meant here is the index-finger. Hence it is the part below the thumb and the index-finger which is тАШdedicated to the Pitс╣Ыs.тАЩ

We interpret the text in this manner on the strength of what is prescribed in other Smс╣Ыtis, and also upon that of the practices of cultured people; specially as no sense could be got out of the words as they stand. Says ┼Ъaс╣ЕkhaтАФтАШBelow the thumb and behind the first palm-line is the receptacle dedicated to Brahm─Б; that between the thumb and the index-finger is dedicated to the Pitс╣Ыs; that below the little finger is dedicated to Praj─Бpati, that at the tip of the fingers is dedicated to the Gods.тАЩтАФ(59)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

тАШAс╣Еgulim┼лleтАЩтАФтАШat the base of the little fingerтАЩ (Kull┼лka, N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa and R─Бghav─Бnanda);тАФтАШat the base of the fingersтАЩ (Medh─Бtithi and Nandana)

Medh─Бtithi (p. 101,1. 8)тАФтАШTath─Б ca ┼Ъaс╣Еkhaс╕етАЩтАФThough Medh─Бtithi appears to be quoting the very words of ┼Ъaс╣Еkha, the actual passage from ┼Ъaс╣Еkha reads as follows:тАФ

k─Бyaс╣Г kaviс╣гс╣нak─Бm┼лle t─лrtham┼лktamman─лс╣гibhiс╕е
aс╣Еguс╣гс╣нham┼лle ca tath─Б pr─Бj─Бpatyaс╣Г vica?с╣Зai |
aс╣Еgus?yagre sthitaс╣Г daivaс╣Г pi┼Ы?yaс╣Г tarjanim┼лlake |

Here тАШK─БyaтАЩ is distinguished from тАШPr─Бj─БpatyaтАЩ V─лramitrodaya also cites Medh─Бtithi as quoting ┼Ъaс╣ЕkhaтАЩs text.

This verse is quoted in V─лramitrodaya (─Аhnika, p. 77), which offers the following explanationтАФтАШanguс╣гс╣нham┼лlaтАЩ means the lower part of the thumb; and on the palm-side of this is the тАШBr─Бhma-t─лrtha.тАЩ тАШTalaтАЩ is the palm; and that part of the palm which extends from the base of the thumb to the first long line in it constitutes the тАШBr─Бhma-t─лrthaтАЩ; and the part which lies between the base of the fingers and the long line parallel to them is the тАШK─Бya-t─лrthaтАЩ;тАФand at the tip of the fingers lies the тАШDaiva-t─лrtha.тАЩтАФThe term тАШagreтАЩ is to be construed with тАШaс╣Еguli,тАЩ which is the predominant factor in the compound тАШaс╣Еgulim┼лle.тАЩтАФтАШPitryam tayoradhaс╕е.тАЩтАФHere also тАШtayoс╕етАЩ stands for the two terms тАШaс╣ЕguliтАЩ and тАШaс╣Еguс╣гс╣нhaтАЩ; and the particular тАШaс╣ЕguliтАЩ or тАШfingerтАЩ meant here is the тАШfore-finger; so that the тАШPitrya-t─лrthaтАЩ would be тАШbelowтАЩ the thumb and the forefinger.тАФThe words of the text as they stand, if taken literally, do not yield any sense; that is why recourse has been taken to the more or less indirect construction, as explained above.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

Through any one of the aforesaid тАШreceptaclesтАЩ he should three times тАШsip water,тАЩтАФi.e., he should let water enter his stomach through the mouth.

тАШThenтАЩтАФi.e., after the sipping of water,тАФhe should тАШtwiceтАЩтАФi.e., by repeating the actтАФтАШwipe the mouth,тАЩтАФi.e., the two lips. This тАШwipingтАЩ consists of removing with a wet hand the drops of water attaching to the lips.

Question.тАФтАЬWhence do you get the idea that this wiping is to be done with the hand?тАЭ

Answer.тАФWe learn this from actual usage, and also deduce it from the fact of the context dealing with тАШreceptaclesтАЩ (which have been described as parts of the band);тАФthe terms тАШthrough the receptacleтАЩ and тАШwith vrater,тАЩ though occurring elsewhere, being brought in here also.

Further, inasmuch as the wiping is meant only to serve a visible purpose, the term тАШmouthтАЩ is taken to stand for a part of the mouth (i.e., the lips).

тАШCavitiesтАЩтАФholes;тАФтАШhe should touch with waterтАЩтАФhold in the hand. тАШUpaspar┼ЫanaтАЩ (of the text) is the same as тАШspar┼Ыana.тАЩ Since the text has been speaking of the тАШmouth,тАЩ the тАШcavitiesтАЩ meant to be touched are those pertaining to the mouth (i.e., located in the bead). Says Gautama (1.36)тАФтАШHe should touch the cavities in the head.тАЩ

тАШThe SoulтАЩтАФstands for the Heart and the Navel. In the Upaniс╣гads we read that тАШone should And the Soul in the heart.тАЩ Hence the тАШtouching of the heartтАЩ becomes the тАШtouching of the Soul,тАЩ the all-pervading entity ensouling the body. (We have to take it in this sense, because) there can be no touching of the Soul itself, which is something incorporeal. In some law-books it is laid down that тАШone should touch the navelтАЩ; hence we have included тАШnavelтАЩ also (as indicated by the term тАШSoulтАЩ of the text).

тАШHeadтАЩтАФthis is well known.

Since all Smс╣Ыtis arc meant to serve the same purpose, тАШthe washing of hands up to the wristsтАЩ and such other acts (as are laid down in Gauс╣нama 1.36, for instance) also hare to be done along with those mentioned in the text; such acts, for instance, as not making noise, keeping silent, sprinkling of water on the feet,тАФor even washing the feet, as laid down in the Mah─Бbh─Бrata.тАФ(60)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

Medh─Бtithi (p. 101, l, 21)тАФтАШKvachit smaryateтАЩтАФHopkins refers in this connection to Mah─Бbh─Бrata 13.104.39.

This verse is quoted in Smс╣Ыtitattva (p. 178);тАФand in Hem─Бdri (┼Ъr─Бddha, p. 992), which adds the following notes:тАФтАШMukham,тАЩ the two lips,тАФthe whole for the part,тАФthe тАШholesтАЩ to be touched also are those connected with the face, mukha;тАФтАШ─Бtm─Бnam,тАЩ heart or navel,тАФthe Upaniс╣гads describing the тАШ─БtmanтАЩ as тАШto be seen within the heart,тАЩтАФhence the тАШtouchingтАЩ is to be of the heart, as the тАШSoul,тАЩ being all-pervading, cannot be touched;тАФthe touching of the navel also is laid down in other textsтАФ[Hence тАШ─Бtm─Бnam may stand for either the heart or the navel. ]

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

Bodh─Бyava-Dharmas┼лtra, 1.5.15-10.тАФтАШThrice he should sip water, reaching to the heart,тАФnot laughing, not talking, not standing, not looking this way and that, not stooping, not bowing down, not having his ┼Ыikh─Б untied, with throat not covered, nor with head covered, not in a hurry, not without the sacred thread, not spreading out his feet, with the end of his lower garment not tucked into the waist-band, with arms not outside the knees, without making any sound; and he should wash thrice; twice, according to some.тАЩ

Baudh─Бyana-Dharmas┼лtra, 1.5.21.тАФтАШTouching the holes with water, he should touch the feet, navel, head, and lastly, the left hand.тАЩ

Gautama-Dharmas┼лtra, l.38-42.тАФтАШSeated on a clean spot, placing his right arm between his knees, wearing the sacred thread, washing his hands up to the wrist, with speech in check, he should sip water, touching the heart, thrice or four times; he should wash twice; the feet also; should touch the holes in the head; should sprinkle water on the heart also.тАЩ

─Аpastamba-Dharmas┼лtra, 1.5.10. 2-9.тАФтАШSeated, he should sip water twice, reaching his heart; should wash the lips thriceтАФtwice, say some; once he should rinse his mouth,тАФtwice, say some; washing the left hand with the right, he should touch with water, the feet, the head, the sense-organs, the eyes, the nostrils and the ears; then he should touch water; when going to take food, he should, even though clean, sip water twice, twice wash his lips and once rinse the mouth; he should sip water alter having washed the lips to the ends.тАЩ

Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нha-Smс╣Ыti, 3.29-30.тАФтАШWith the Brahma-t─лrtha, he should thrice sip water and twice wash the lips with water; should touch the holes with water; should sprinkle water on the head.тАЩ

Viс╣гс╣Зu-Smс╣Ыti, 62,6-8.тАФтАШWith the Brahma-t─лrtha, he should sip water thrice; twice wash; touch with water the holes, the head and the chest.тАЩ

Gobhila-Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtra, 2.5-8.тАФтАШGoing to the north of the Fire, washing his hands, seated, he should sip water thrice, and wash twice; having sprinkled water over the feet, he should sprinkle it over the head; touch the organs with water; the eyes, the nostrils and the ears.тАЩ

Y─Бj├▒avalkya, 1-20.тАФтАШHaving sipped water thrice and washed twice, he should touch the holes with water in its natural condition.тАЩ

060 Let him first sip water thrice; next twice wipe his mouth; and, lastly, touch with water the cavities (of the head), (the seat of) the soul and the head.

One who knows his duties, when desiring cleanliness, should always sip, through the proper receptacle, water which is neither hot nor frothy,тАФin solitude, with his face towards the North or the East.тАФ(61)

рдЗрддрд┐ (рдЧреНрдзреН рез.рейрел) ред рдпрдерд╛ “рдмреГрд╣рджреНрд░рдердиреНрддрд░рд╕рд╛рдо рд╖рдбрд╣реЗ” рдЗрддрд┐ рдХреЗрд╖реБрдЪрд┐рджреН рдЕрд╣рдГрд╕реБ92 рдмреГрд╣рддреН рдХреЗрд╖реБрдЪрд┐рджреН рд░рдердиреНрддрд░рдореН, рди рддреНрд╡реН рдПрдХрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдиреН рдЕрд╣рдирд┐ рд╕рдорд╕реНрддреЛрднрдпрд╕рд╛рдорддреНрд╡рдореН ред реи.ремрез рее

рдЙрдХреНрддрдореН рдЖрдЪрдордирдВ рддреАрд░реНрдереЗрдирд╛рдкрд╛рдВ рднрдХреНрд╖рдгрдореН ред рдкрд░рд┐рдорд╛рдгрдВ рддреБ рдиреЛрдХреНрддрдореН ред рдЕрддрд╕реН рддрджреН рдЕрд╡рдзрд╛рд░рдгрд╛рд░реНрдердореН рдЖрд╣ ред

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШHotтАЩ hero stands for boiled; elsewhere we read that the sipping should be done тАШwith unboiled water.тАЩ So that the prohibition docs not apply to such water as is naturally hot, or has imbibed the beat of the hot atmosphere.

тАШFrothтАЩ is meant to include тАШbubblesтАЩ also, as elsewhere we read that тАШthe water should be free from froth and bubbles.тАЩ

The terms тАШthrough the proper receptacleтАЩ and тАШone who knows his dutiesтАЩ have been added only for the purpose of filling up the metre.

тАШDesiring cleanlinessтАЩтАФseeking to attain cleanliness, i.e., purity. The sense is that without the sipping of water he can never be clean.

тАШAlwaysтАЩтАФi.e., not only at the timo of eating, as would seem implied by the fact of the rule occurring in the section on тАШeating,тАЩтАФbut also at other times, when, for instance, one seeks cleanliness after passing urine or stool, etc.

Though тАШwaterтАЩ is the object of the act of sipping, yet it is put in the Instrumental Case, with a view to indicate that what is prescribed is meant to be applicable not only to the water that is sipped but also to that which forms the instrument in such acts as the washing of the feet and the like. What we hold is that in the act of sipping also the water is only the тАШinstrumentтАЩ; specially as the sipping does not constitute the sanctification of the water (in which case alone the water could be the тАШobjectтАЩ).

тАШIn solitudeтАЩтАФi.e., in a clean place; a solitary place, being uncrowded by people, is generally clean.

тАШWith his face towards the North or the EastтАЩ;тАФthe term тАШfaceтАЩ is to be construed along with each of the two terms (тАШEastтАЩ and тАШNorthтАЩ); as Gauс╣нama (1.35) says that тАШthe man should face either the North or the East.тАЩ The compound should be expounded as тАШhe who has his face towards the North, EastтАЩ; the compound being a pure Bahuvr─лhi, not a Bahuvr─лhi containing another copulative compound [i.e., we cannot expound the compound as тАШNorth and East,тАЩ and then compound this with the term тАШmukha,тАЩ the sense in this case being тАШone having his face towards the North and the EastтАЩ]. If wo made tho Bahuvr─лhi contain a copulative compound, then if the compound тАШpr─Бс╣ЕudakтАЩ were taken as an aggregative copulative, it should have an additional тАШaтАЩ at the end; nor could it be taken as a segregative copulative. Further, it is not possible for the man to face both the North and the East at one and the same time; for in that case, the rule would mean that one part of the sipping should be done with face towards the North, and another part of it with face towards the East; and this would mean that the sipping is not done at one place. Then again, the directions mentioned do not form the principal factor in the predicate of the sentence, which alone could justify their being taken reciprocally; nor does the term тАШpr─Бс╣ЕudakтАЩ from a well-known name of the North-East quarter, in the manner in which тАШdakс╣гina- p┼лrvaтАЩ does of the South-East quarter; hence there can be no justification for the compound being taken as a containing another compound name of a particular quarter, [i.e., we cannot take тАШpr─Бс╣ЕudakтАЩ as the name of the North-East quarter and then compound it with тАШmukhaтАЩ]. For these reasons the. compound cannot be taken as a тАШBahuvr─лhiтАЩ containing within itself another compound. From all this it follows that option, is meant; as is clearly laid down in another Smс╣ЫtiтАФтАШActs of cleanliness should be begun with

face towards the North or the EastтАЩ (Gauс╣нama 1.35). This option is just like the option that we have in the case of the S─Бman to be sung at the с╣вaс╕Нoha sacrifice, where the injunction being in the form that тАШthe Bс╣Ыhadrathantara S─Бman should be sung,тАЩ what is actually done is that on some days of the sacrifice (which lasts for six days) they sing the тАШBс╣ЫhatтАЩ while on other the тАШRathantaraтАЩ S─Бman; and never on any one day do they ever sing both the S─Бmans.тАФ(61)

The тАШsipping,тАЩ as consisting of the drinking of water, has been prescribed; but the exact quantity of the water to be sipped has not yet been laid down. Hence the Text now proceeds to define the precise measure (of the water to be sipped):тАФ

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in V─лramitrodaya (─Аhnika, p. 66), where it is explained that what the epithet тАШanuс╣гс╣Зabhiс╕етАЩ means is that the water should not be heated by fire, as is distinctly stated by Viс╣гс╣Зu;тАФagain on page 77, where it is stated to be the injunction of ─Бcamana in general, for all the three castes;тАФalso on page 79, where it is added that тАШek─БnteтАЩ means not crowded,тАФwhere alone the mind can be calm and collected,тАФas is laid down by Viс╣гс╣Зu.

On the tern тАШpr─Бgudaс╣Еmukhaс╕е,тАЩ this work has the following note, criticising Medh─БtithiтАЩs explanation:тАФтАЬThe term pr─Бgudaс╣Еmukhaс╕е must mean the north-east quarter, on the strength of the declaration of H─Бr─лta; and in the ┼Ъruti also we see the term used in the sense of the north-eastтАФe. g. in the passage referring to the branch of the Pal─Б┼Ыa treeтАФ

тАШPr─Бch─лm─Бharati, ud─лch─лm─Бharati, pr─Бgud─лch─лm─БharatiтАЩ and also in K─Бty─Бyanas┼лtra, where it is saidтАФтАШpr─Бgudakpravaс╣Зam devayajanam,тАЩ where the term тАШpr─БgudakтАЩ stands for the north-east. For these reasons the assertion of Medh─БtithiтАФthat тАШthe term pr─Бgudak being never found used in the sense of north-east, it should not be explained as such,тАЩтАФmust be disregarded. Medh─Бtithi has explained the compound pr─Бguduс╣Еmukhaс╕е as a Bahuvr─лhi compound composed of three terms, whereby the meaning comes to be that the man must face the East or the North.тАЭ

The writer has conveniently ignored Medh─БtithiтАЩs reference to Gautama 1.35, in support of his interpretation.

The second half of the verse is quoted in ┼Ъuddhi-kaumud─л (p. 339);тАФand in Hem─Бdri (┼Ъr─Бddha, p. 983), which notes that тАШanuс╣гс╣З─Бbhiс╕етАЩ is meant to prohibit the water heated by fire.

Bodh─Бyan─Б-Dharmas┼лtra, 1. 5. 14.тАФтАШWater-sipping should never be done with the lingers, nor with such water as has hubbies or foam, is brackish or saltish, or muddy, or discoloured, or foul-smelling.тАЩ

Baudh─Бyana (V─лra-─Аhnika, p. 71).тАФтАШSipping should not be done with water left over after washing the feet; or if this has to be done, it should be done after pouring out some of the water on the ground.тАЩ

─Аpastamba-Dharmas┼лtra, 5. 15. 4-7.тАФтАШWater should not bo sipped out of rain-showers; nor out of cavities in the Earth; nor with warm water, without reason.тАЩ [тАШReasonтАЩ such as sickness.] [Hut according to Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нha, if the cavity contained water enough for satisfying the cow, which is not unclean, then, it may be used.]

Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нha-Smс╣Ыti, 3. 36.тАФтАШSipping should not be done with water with bad colour, bad smell or bad taste, or that proceeding from an unclean source.тАЩ

Viс╣гс╣Зu-Smс╣Ыti, 62. 5.тАФтАШSeated in a clean place, with arms between the knees, facing the East or the North, with happy and concentrated mind, he should sip water, which is not fire-heated, which is free from foam, which has not been brought by the ┼Ъ┼лdra, and which is not brackish.тАЩ

Y─Бj├▒avalkya, 1.20.тАФтАШWith water in its natural condition, free from bubbles and foam.тАЩ

Gobhila-Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtra, 1.2.22-23.тАФтАШWith water, not hot, nor with bubbles.тАЩ

┼Ъaс╣Еkha (V─лra-─Аhnika, p. 66).тАФтАШWith water pulled out, which is free from bubbles and foam, not heated by fire, nor brackish.тАЩ

Gautama and ┼Ъaс╣Еkha-Likhita (Do., p. 67).тАФтАШNot with water fetched by a ┼Ъ┼лdra or an unclean person or by one hand.тАЩ K┼лrmapur─Бс╣Зa (Do.).тАФтАШWith water which is not brackish and which has not been fetched by a ┼Ъ┼лdra or by an unclean person; nor with water brought with one hand.тАЩ

Saс╣Гvarta (Do.).тАФтАШNever with water offered by a ┼Ъ┼лdra or an unclean person, or with one hand.тАЩ

061 He who knows the sacred law and seeks purity shall always perform the rite of sipping with water neither hot nor frothy, with the (prescribed) tirtha, in a lonely place, and turning to the east or to the north.

рдПрд╡рдорд░реНрдердореН рдПрд╡ рдЪрд╛рд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреНрдиреН рдЕрд╡рдзрд╛рд╡реН рдЗрджрдореН рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ рее реи.ремреи рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШReaching the heartтАЩтАФthat which reaches down to the regions of the heart; the word being derived from the root тАШgamтАЩ with the тАШс╕НaтАЩ affix, according to P─Бс╣Зini, 6. 2.101; the term тАШhс╣ЫdayaтАЩ being changed into тАШhс╣ЫdтАЩ according to P─Бс╣ЗiniтАЩs S┼лtra, 6.3.50.

тАШIs purifiedтАЩтАФReaches sanctity; that is, gets rid of impurity. The water (reaching the heart) would, in quantity, be just a little less than a handful.

тАШThe Kс╣гatriya by that reaching the throatтАЩтАФi.e., by that which reaches only down to the throat. The term тАШbh┼лmipaс╕етАЩ in the text stands for the Kс╣гatriya; as the тАШlordship of landтАЩ is laid down for the Kс╣гatriya only; and hence this well-known function (of ruling the land) indicates here the Kс╣гatriya caste. If actual тАШlordshipтАЩ of the land were meant, then what is laid down here would have been prescribed among the тАШduties of tho king.тАЩ

тАШThe Vai┼Ыya by the water that is just sipped,тАЩтАФi.e., which is just taken into the mouth; even without reaching the throat, the water thus sipped serves to purify the Vai┼Ыya.

тАШThe ┼Ъ┼лdra by what is touched with the end;тАЩтАФтАШanс╣нataс╕етАЩ stands for тАШantenaтАЩ; the тАШtasilтАЩ affix having the force of the instrumental, according to the V─Бrtika on P─Бс╣Зini, 5. 4. 44. The term тАШendтАЩ (anta) means proximity; e.g., the phrase тАШudak─БntaтАЩ means тАШnear waterтАЩ. It also means a part; e.g., in such expressions as тАШvastr─Бnta,тАЩ тАШvasan─БntaтАЩ and the like. With both these significations the term тАШendтАЩ (being a relative term) stands in need of a correlative; whenever it is used, one always wants to knowтАФтАШnear what тАЩ or тАШpart of what.тАЩ Now in the present case, the water-sipping has been laid down for the other castes as to he done with certain parts of the hand and the lips and the tongue; and it is the тАШendтАЩ of these that is meant. It cannot mean mere тАШproxi mityтАЩ; because the тАШwater-sippingтАЩ prescribed cannot he accomplished by mere proximity. Then again, the тАШtouchтАЩ (of the water with the tongue and lips) would involve sipping (which has been laid down for the Vai┼Ыya); for one is sure to feel the taste of that which is touched with the tongue and lips. Hence the conclusion appears to he that the quantity of water sufficient for the ┼Ъ┼лdra is just a little less in quantity than that for the Vai┼Ыya; e.g., while for the Vai┼Ыya the water should touch the root of the tongue, for the ┼Ъ┼лdra it should touch only its tip.

Water being a fluid substance, its going beyond the limits prescribed would be unavoidable; hence all that is meant is that if the water sipped fails to reach the prescribed limits, it fails to purify the man.

The description of the тАШreceptaclesтАЩ (parts of the hand) refers to the right hand; as it is this hand that should be used in all washings; specially as it has been laid down that men should perform (religious) acts with the right hand. It is for this reason that we reiterate this fact in the present connection.тАФ(62)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 221);тАФin Smс╣Ыtitattva (p. 335), which points out that for the ┼Ъ┼лdra, there is no ─Бcamana, as the verse stops short at the Vai┼Ыya; so in the place of ─Бcamana, the ┼Ъ┼лdra should wash his hands and feet;тАФthis is clear from a text of the Brahmapur─Бс╣Зa;тАФand in V─лramitrodaya (─Аhnika, p. 74), where it is explained that тАШantataс╕етАЩ means inside of the mouth; and hence what is meant is that there should be no drinking of the water, which should only touch the inner part of the mouth;тАФsuch being the opinion of Kalpataru. It is curious that Kalpataru, as quoted in V─лramitrodaya, has quoted Manu 5.13 9, where тАШantataс╕етАЩ does not occur at all, and missed the present verse, which, as V─лramitrodaya rightly remarks, is the text that really supports the explanation provided by Kalpataru. V─лramitrodaya notes Medh─БtithiтАЩs explanation with approval on p. 75.

This verse is quoted in Kс╣Ыtyas─Бrasamuccaya (p. 46);тАФin Hem─Бdri (┼Ъr─Бddha, p. 985), which adds the following notes:тАФтАШHс╣Ыdg─Бbhiс╕е,тАЩ reaching the regions of the heart,тАФтАШP┼лyateтАЩ acquires purity;тАФтАШKaс╣Зthay─Бbhiс╕е,тАЩ just touching the throat only,тАФтАШbh┼лmipoс╕е,тАЩ the Kс╣гatriya;тАФтАШpr─Б┼Ыit─Бс╕еhiс╕етАЩ, just taken into the mouth, and not reaching the throat,тАФтАШantataс╕е,тАЩ the affix тАШtasiтАЩ has the force of the Instrumental,тАФthe term тАШantaтАЩ meaning near requires a correlative, that to which nearness is meant,тАФso that the meaning is that the ┼Ъ┼лdra is purified by water reaching that point which is in close proximity to that which the water should reach for purifying the Vai┼Ыya;тАФand as the tongue is the point for the Vai┼Ыya, for the ┼Ъ┼лdra it must be the teeth; though the water that reaches the teeth must touch the tongue also, yet all that is meant is that the quantity for the ┼Ъ┼лdra should be just a little less than that for the Vai┼Ыya.

It is quoted also in Saс╣Гsk─Бraratnam─Бl─Б (p. 221).

Viс╣гс╣Зu-Smс╣Ыti, 62. 9.тАФтАШThe three twice-born castes become pure by water reaching the heart, the throat and the palate respectively, the woman and the ┼Ъ┼лdra by touching it once.тАЩ

Gautama Dharmas┼лtra, 1.37.тАФтАШHe should thrice or four times sip water reaching the heart.тАЩ

Va┼Ыiс╣гс╣нha-Smс╣Ыti, 3.33-34.тАФтАШThe Br─Бhmaс╣Зa is purified by bubble-free and foamless water reaching his heart; the Kс╣гatriya by it reaching the throat, the Vai┼Ыya by water actually drunk; the woman and the ┼Ъ┼лdra by merely touching it.тАЩ

  • рдХрдердВ рдкреБрдирдГ рдХреЗрд╡рд▓рд╕реНрдпреЛрдкрд╡реАрддрд╕реНрдпреИрд╡рд╛рдЪрдордирд╛рдЩреНрдЧрддрд╛ рдпрд╛рд╡рддрд╛рдиреНрдпрджреН рдЕрдкреНрдпреН рдЕрддреНрд░ рдирд┐рд░реНрджрд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЪреАрдирд╛рд╡реАрддрд┐ рдЪ ред рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЪреАрдирд╛рд╡реАрддрдВ рд╕реНрд╡рд╢рдмреНрджреЗрдиреИрд╡ рдкрд┐рддреНрд░реНрдпреЗ рдХрд░реНрдордгрд┐ рд╡рд┐рд╣рд┐рддрдореН, рддрддреНрд░рд╛рд░реНрдерд╡рддреНрддрд╛рдпрд╛рдореН рдЙрдкрдпрд╛рддрд╛рдпрд╛рдВ рдирд╛рдХреГрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрдиреЛрдкрд╡реАрддреЗрди рд╡рд┐рдХрд▓реНрдкрд┐рддреБрдореН рдЕрд░реНрд╣рддрд┐ ред рдирд┐рд╡реАрддрдореН рдЕрдкреНрдпреН рдЕрднрд┐рдЪрд╛рд░реЗ рд╜рд░реНрдерд╡рддреН ред рдпрджреНрдпреН рдЕрдкреНрдпреН рдЕрддреНрд░ рдирд┐рд╡реАрддрд╕реНрдп рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧреЛ рдирд╛рд╕реНрддрд┐, рддрдерд╛рдкрд┐ рд╕реНрдореГрддреАрдирд╛рдВ рдЪреИрдХрд╛рд░реНрдереНрдпрд╛рджреН рдЕрдиреНрдпрддреНрд░ рдпреЛ рд╡рд┐рдирд┐рдпреЛрдЧрд╕реН рддреЗрдиреЗрд╣рд╛рдкреНрдпреН рдЕрд░реНрдерд╡рддреНрддрд╛ рднрд╡рддреНрдпреН рдПрд╡ ред рдкрд╛рдгрд┐рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгрдВ рдмрд╛рд╣реВрдкрд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрд╛рд░реНрдердореН рдЙрджреНрдзреГрддрдмрд╛рд╣реБрд░реН рдпрддреЛ рд▓реЛрдХ рдЙрдкрд╡реАрддреАрддреНрдпреН рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рд╕рд╛рд░реНрд╡рдХрд╛рд▓рд┐рдХрдВ рдЪреЛрдкрд╡реАрддрдВ рд╡рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрд╛рдордГ ред рди рдЪ рдХреЗрд╡рд▓рдкрд╛рдгрд╛рд╡реН рдЙрджреНрдзреГрдд рдЙрдкрд╡реАрддреА ред рд╕рд╡реНрдпреЗ рдЙрджреНрдзреГрддреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЪреАрдирд╛рд╡реАрддреА ред рд╕рдорд╛рд╕рдкрджрд╛рдиреН рдирд╛рдордзреЗрдпрдореН ред рдЕрд╕рдорд╛рд╕рд╕реН рддреБ рд╡реГрддреНрддрд╛рдиреБрд░реЛрдзрд┐рддрдпрд╛ ред рдХрдгреНрдард╕рдЬреНрдЬрдиреЗ ред рдХрдгреНрдареЗ рд╕рдЬреНрдЬрдирдВ рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрдГ95 рд╕реНрдерд╛рдкрдирдореН ред рдпрджрд╛ рд╡рд╕реНрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╕реВрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдп рд╡рд╛рдиреНрдпрддрд░реЛ рд╜рдкрд┐ рдмрд╛рд╣реБрд░реН рдЙрджреНрдзреНрд░рд┐рдпрддреЗ рддрджрд╛ рдирд┐рд╡реАрддреА рднрд╡рддрд┐ рее реи.ремрей рее
рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

An objection is raisedтАФтАЬAs a matter of fact, in treatises dealing with Dharma, the meanings of words are accepted to be exactly as they are known in ordinary usage; and the works of Manu and others should not make it their business to explain the meanings of words, in the way in which it is done by grammatical and lexicographical works.тАЭ

─Аnswer.тАФWe have already answered this before; if treatises on Dharma should be found to supply the explanation of such words as are not ordinarily known, are they to be blamed for doing so? Then again, in the present instance, there is another purpose also in view. The term тАШupav─лtinтАЩ is explained in the course of the explanation of the act of тАШwater-sipping,тАЩ with a view to indicate that the method (of wearing the sacred thread, etc.) is auxiliary to that act. Though it is true that the wearing of the sacred thread,тАФeither as part of a religious observance, or as accomplishing certain desirable results for man,тАФis known as to be done at all times, yet if the тАШwater-sippingтАЩ were done without it, it would remain incomplete. So that, if we did not have the present text (as indicating the necessity of wearing the sacred thread during water-sipping), there would be some deficiency in the religious act, as also some defect in the agent. If the sipping were done without the sacred thread, it would be as good as not done, and there would be the additional wrong done, in the shape of sipping the water while unclean.

Question.тАФтАЬHow is it that the Upav─лta-method alone is regarded as auxiliary to the тАШwater-sipping,тАЩ when as a matter of fact, the present text has spoken of another method, the тАШPr─Бch─лn─Бv─лta,тАЩ also?тАЭ

Our answer is as follows:тАФAs for the тАШPr─Бch─лn─Бv─лtaтАЩ method, this has been directly prescribed, in so many words, as pertaining to acts of offering to the Pitс╣Ыs; so that when its use has been found in connection with these, it could not be taken as an alternative to the тАШUpav─лtaтАЩ method, whose use has not yet been found. Similarly the тАШNiv─лс╣нaтАЩ method also has its use in connection with acts of sorcery. Though the use of the тАШNiv─лс╣нaтАЩ has not been laid down in the itself, yet since all Smс╣Ыtis have the same end in view, the use prescribed in other Smс╣Ыtis could be regarded as accepted in the present context also.

The term тАШhandтАЩ stands here for the arm; it is only when the man raises his arm that he is called тАШUpav─лс╣нiтАЩ; further, we are going to point out later on that the тАШUpav─лс╣нaтАЩ is the method (of wearing the thread) to be employed at all times (not during religious acts only); and no one is called тАШUpav─лс╣нinтАЩ by merely lifting his hand.

тАШWhen the left hand is held above,тАЩ he is called тАШPr─Бch─лn─Бv─лс╣н─лтАЩ; it is the compounded form (тАШpr─Бch─лn─Бv─лс╣н─лтАЩ) that constitutes the name; the text puts it iu the uncompounded form on account of the exigencies of metre.

тАШOn its hanging by the neckтАЩ;тАФтАШSajjana,тАЩ тАШhangingтАЩ means being worn, when the sacred thread, or the piece of cloth, is worn over the neck, and neither arm is held over it, then the man becomes тАШniv─лt─л.тАЩтАФ(63)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in Saс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (p. 39), which notes that the non-compounding (in тАШpr─Бch─лna-─Бv─лtiтАЩ is a Vedic anomaly;тАФand in Saс╣Гsk─Бraratnam─Бl─Б (p. 188).

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

Baudh─Бyana-Dharmas┼лtra, 5.1.5-8.тАФтАШThe Sacred Thread worn at sacrifices to gods (upav─лta) consists of the silk or the cotton thread folded three times three: it should reach down to the navel; the right arm being held above;тАФthe reverse (pr─Бch─лn─Бvita) at offerings to Pitс╣Ыs; hanging by the neck, it is niv─лta; hanging downwards it is adhov─лta.тАЩ

─Аpastamba-Dharmas┼лtra, 1.6.18-19.тАФтАШHe who is wearing the Sacred Thread in the upav─лta form is to be regarded as wearing two pieces of cloth;тАФwhile he who is wearing it in the Adhov─лta form, is to be regarded as wearing only one piece of cloth.тАЩ

Gobhila-Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtra, 1.2.2-3.тАФтАШHolding aloft the right arm, passing over the head, resting the thread on the left shoulder, hanging down the right arm-pit,тАФthus does he become the wearer of the Yaj├▒opav─лta; lifting the left arm, passing over the head, resting the thread on the right shoulder, hanging down the left arm-pit,тАФthus does he become the wearer of the Pr─Бch─лn─Бv─лta.тАЩ

063 A twice-born man is called upavitin when his right arm is raised (and the sacrificial string or the dress, passed under it, rests on the left shoulder); (when his) left (arm) is raised (and the string, or the dress, passed under it, rests on the right shoulder, he is called) prakinavitin; and nivitin when it hangs down (straight) from the neck.

When the girdle, the skin, the staff, the sacred thread or the water-pot becomes damaged, he should throw it into the water and take up another with the proper formulas.тАФ(64)

рдХрдордгреНрдбрд▓реБрдиреЛрдкрдирдпрдиреЛрддреНрддрд░рдХрд╛рд▓рд╛рдиреБрд╡рд░реНрддрд┐рдирд╛ рддреБрд▓реНрдпрд╡рдиреН рдирд┐рд░реНрджреЗрд╢рд╛рддреН рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдореН рдЕрдкреНрдпреН рдпрджрд╛ рдХрдордгреНрдбрд▓реБрд╕реН рддрджреЗрдпрдВ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрддреНрддрд┐рд░реН рдЗрддрд┐ рдкрд╛рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдХрддреНрд╡рдВ рд╕реНрдпрд╛рддреН ред

  • рддрддреНрд░ рджрдгреНрдбрдзрд╛рд░рдгрдВ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдЧреГрд╣реНрдп рджрдгреНрдбрдВ рднрд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдВ рдЪрд░реЗрджреН рдЗрддрд┐ рдХреНрд░рдорд╛рджреН рднреИрдХреНрд╖реНрдпрдЪрд░реНрдпрд╛рдЩреНрдЧрддреНрд╡рдореН рдПрд╡ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрдВ рд╕рдорд╛рдЪрд╛рд░рд╛рджреН рдЕрднреИрдХреНрд╖реЗ рд╜рд░реНрдереЗ рд╜рдкрд┐ рднреНрд░рдордгреЗ рднрд╡рддреНрдпреН рдПрд╡ ред рди рддреБ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджреИрд╡ рдХрд░рддрд▓рдзреГрддрджрдгреНрдбрд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрдерд╛рдирд╛рд╕рдирд╢рдпрдирднреЛрдЬрдирд╛рджреАрдирд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЪ рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдзреНрдпрд╛рдпреЗ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдорд╛рдЮреНрдЬрд▓рд┐рдВ рд╡рдХреНрд╖реНрдпрддрд┐ ред

  • рдордиреНрддреНрд░рд╡рджреН рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЙрдкрдирдпрдирд╡рд┐рдзрд┐рдирд╛ рдЧреНрд░рд╣рдгрдореН рдЕрдиреБрд╡рджрддрд┐ ред рддрддреНрд░ рдЪ рдореЗрдЦрд▓рд╛рдпрд╛ рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдГ, рди рджрдгреНрдбрд╕реНрдп рее реи.ремрек рее

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The present verse enjoins that when these things are damaged, they should be thrown into water and others should be taken up; and the sequence of the тАШthrowingтАЩ and the тАШtaking upтАЩ is to be just as it is found in the text. In as much as one has got to take up these things again, they cannot be regarded as forming part of the Initiatory Ceremony itself; if it were part of this ceremony, then all their purpose would have been fulfilled by the completion of the ceremony. The right view therefore is that these should continue to be taken up throughout the тАШstudent-stage.тАЩ

тАЬBut is it not possible to regard the throwing into water here laid down as the disposal of the things mentioned, if they happen, during the Initiatory CeremonyтАФand before its completion,тАФto be damaged by divine or human adverse forces? The taking up of fresh ones, would, in this case, be necessary for the completion of the ceremony; just as there is of the begging-bowl. Is it absolutely impossible for the text to be taken in this manner, that the mere fact of the re-taking being laid down should be made the basis of assuming that the things should continue to be held throughout the student-stage?тАЭ

Our answer to the above is as follows:тАФAs for mere тАШholding,тАЩ this has been laid down in connection with the staff only (during the Initiatory Rite); as for the girdle what is to be done during the ceremony is only its tying (round the waist); so that what should be done as part of the Initiatory Ceremony is the peculiar arrangement of strings (which constitutes the act of tying); this being done, the purpose of the Injunction will have been fulfilled; so that if, at some future time, any thing becomes damaged or not, what effect could that have upon the ceremony (which will have been long completed)? As for the particular form of тАШdisposal,тАЩ this helps the Rite only when what has become damaged forms an integral part of the Rite itself. Nor again have the scriptures laid down any purpose for which the girdle, etc., are worn, for the fulfilment of which purpose, the re-taking of them (during the ceremony) would be enjoined (in the present text); it is only when the purpose of a certain object has not been fulfilled, that we take it for granted that that object should be taken up again. For these reasons, because the text lays down (a) a particular form of Disposal, and (b) the re-taking of the things, we conclude that, even though the holding of these may form an integral part of the Initiatory Ceremony, the necessity of this holding does not end with the completion of the ceremony. Then again, the girdle, etc., are mentioned in the same category as the тАШwater-pot,тАЩ which continues to be held after the ceremony also; and this shows that the other articles also are to continue to be held, and all this тАШholdingтАЩ forms part of the observances (of the Religious Student). From all this it follows that the girdle and other things are subservient to both: by the force of тАШcontext,тАЩ they form part of the Initiatory Ceremony, and since they are found to be held after the completion of that ceremony, they are to continue as long as the тАШstudent-stageтАЩ lasts. That the тАШwater-potтАЩ has to be carried (always) for the purpose of carrying water is also implied by (the binding and universal character of) the injunction of the тАШDisposalтАЩ; otherwise (if the pot were not meant to be carried always), the meaning of the injunction would be that the disposal is to be carried out only when the water-pot may be held; and this would make the Injunction partial and limited in its application.

As regards the тАШholding of the staff,тАЩ this comes to be regarded as part of the тАШbegging of food,тАЩ on the basis of sequence enjoined in the rule тАШone should beg for food after taking up the staffтАЩ, but on the basis of actual practice, it comes to be done in connection with such ordinary talking also as is not done for the purpose of тАШfood-begging.тАЩ But it does not mean that the staff should be held always; for the boy who may be holding the stick would be unable to do such acts as standing, sitting, sleeping, eating and so forth; similarly in Verse 2.70 it is laid down that the boy, when proceeding to read the Veda, should sit with joined palms (and this would not be possible if he held the staff in his hand).

тАШWith the proper formulasтАЩтАФthis means that the retaking of the articles should be in the same manner in which they are taken up during the Initiatory Ceremony; and in that connection formulas are laid down in regard to the wearing of the Girdle, and not in regard to the holding of the staff.тАФ(64)

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in Par─Б┼Ыaram─Бdhava (─Аc─Бra, p. 451), which says that it lays down the method of disposing of the sacred thread and other things whenever they happen to break;тАФalso in Nirс╣Зayasindhu (p. 190).

It is quoted in Smс╣Ыtitattva (p. 934) which says that, as the use of mantras is essential, if a certain Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtra does not mention the mantra, it has to be borrowed from another Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtra;тАФand in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 423), where also the verse is explained as laying down the тАШdisposalтАЩ of the tilings mentioned. The latter quotes the verse again on p. 887, where it is explained that in a case where an injunction lays down a certain act as to be done тАШwith the proper mantrasтАЩтАФas is done in the present verseтАФand no particular mantra is prescribed? one has to use the mantra that may be found mentioned in a particular Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtra. This is what тАШmantravatтАЩ has beeif explained to mean, in Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 37 also.)

It is quoted in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra,, p. 85) as laying down the disposal of the sacred thread that has been worn out;тАФin Saс╣Гsk─Бramay┼лkha (p. 39), which notes that the meaning of the term тАШmantravatтАЩ is that they have to be worn with those same mantras that were used for wearing them at the Upanayana;тАФand in V─лramitrodaya (Paribh─Бс╣г─Б, p. 72) as an example of the principle that where the text laying down a certain act as to be done тАШwith mantrasтАЩ does not specify the particular mantras to be used, these have to be taken as laid down in other Gс╣Ыhyas┼лtras.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

Viс╣гс╣Зu-Smс╣Ыti, 27.29.тАФ[Reproduces the exact words of Manu.]

Baudh─Бyana-Dharmas┼лtra, 4.5-7.тАФтАШWhen these articles become spoilt by urine, excreta, blood or semen, they should be thrown away; when the water-pot breaks, one should offer a hundred libations with the Vy─Бhrti mantras; the pieces he should throw into the water, and repeating the S─Бvitr─л ten times, he should take up another pot.тАЩ

Bhс╣Ыgu (V─лra-Samsk─Бra, p. 423).тАФтАШWhen the sacred thread is torn or broken, the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa should bathe and then wear a new one.тАЩ

064 His girdle, the skin (which serves as his upper garment), his staff, his sacrificial thread, (and) his water-pot he must throw into water, when they have been damaged, and take others, reciting sacred formulas.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдореВрд▓рд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The sacrament of Ke┼Ы─Бnta is ordained for the Br─Бhmaс╣Зa in his sixteenth year; for the Kс╣гatriya in his twenty-second year, and for the Vai┼Ыya two years later.тАФ(65)

рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реЗрдгрд╛рд╡реГрджреНрд╡рдЪрдиреЗрди рдЬрд╛рддрдХрд░реНрдорд╛рджрд┐рд╡рджреН рдЙрдкрдирдпрдиреЗ рд╜рдкреНрдпреН рдЕрдордиреНрддреНрд░рдХреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддреЗ100_ рддрдиреНрдирд┐рд╡реГрддреНрддреНрдпрд░реНрддреНрдпрдореН рдЖрд░рднреНрдпрддреЗ ред_

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

тАШThis whole seriesтАЩ should be done for females, without the recitation of Vedic formulas.тАФтАШSeriesтАЩ stands for the entire body of sacraments, beginning with the тАШBirth-rites,тАЩ along with all the acts that constitute their procedure.

тАШFor the purpose of sanctifyingтАЩтАФi.e., purifying This means that the purpose of the sacraments in the case of females that is the same as that in that of males.

тАШAt the proper time,тАЩтАФi.e., without letting that time pass which has been prescribed for the several sacraments. The term тАШyath─БтАЩ here signifies non-transgression, and hence, not signifying тАШsimilarity,тАЩ it is compounded according to P─Бс╣Зini 2.1.7.

The same explanation applies to the compound тАШyath─Б-kramamтАЩ also.

In as much as the text has distinctly asserted that it is only the reciting of Vedic formulas that may be omitted, there could be no idea of the sacraments (for females) being performed at a time, or in an order, other than the prescribed ones; so that the prohibition of other times and another order should be taken as merely describing what is already known, and as added only for the purpose of filling up the metre. All that is really meant by the text is that for females the sacraments should be performed without the Vedic formulas.

The тАШseriesтАЩ spoken of above would imply that like the тАШBirth-riteтАЩ and the other ceremonies, the тАШInitiatory ceremonyтАЩ also should be performed for females; with a view to preclude this idea, the Text addsтАФ

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

This verse is quoted in Smс╣Ыtitattva (p. 926);тАФin Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 362), where ─Бvс╣Ыt is explained as j─Бtakarm─Бdikriy─Б; and yath─Бkramam is to taken to mean that there should ho no deviation from the exact order of sequenceтАФsuch deviation necessitating expiation;тАФin Nirс╣Зayasindhu (p. 188);тАФand in Apar─Бrka (p. 30), which explains ─Бvс╣Ыt as тАШkriy─БтАЩ, act, rite;тАФтАШa┼Ыeс╣гtaс╕етАЩ as along with all detailsтАЩ, and тАШyath─БkramamтАЩ as meaning that the order of the sacraments should not be disturbed or else the Sarvapr─Бya┼Ыcitta has to be performed.тАЩ

It is quoted in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, at several places, on pages 194, 255, 278, 317 and 403). On p. 194, тАШ─Бvс╣ЫtтАЩ is explained as j─Бtakarm─Бdikriy─Б; and on the term тАШamantrik─БтАЩ it is added that what this interdicts is the use of only those mantras that pertain to the primary acts of eating butter, honey and the rest, and not the use of the subsidiary mantras; and this conclusion is in accordance with the principle enunciated in M─лm─Бс╣Гs─Б Sutra 3.8. 34-35, where it is declared that the qualification of up─Бс╣Г┼Ыutva (silence) pertains to only the primary rite of the тАШ─Аtharvaс╣Зa Iс╣гс╣нisтАЩ and not to the subsidiary ones.тАФOn p. 255 the verse is quoted in support of the view that the rite of Niс╣гkramaс╣Зa, is to be performed in the case of the female baby also.тАФSimilarly on p. 278, it is quoted to show that the rite of тАШAnnpr─Б┼ЫanaтАЩ should be performed for the female baby.тАФOn p. 317, it is made to justify performance of the rite of тАШTonsureтАЩ for girls.тАФOn page 403, it is quoted as laying down the performance of all the sacramentsтАФbeginning from the J─Бtakarma and ending with the Ke┼Ы─Бnta; whereby it is concluded that the Upanayaс╣Зa also, for girls is to be done тАШwithout mantrasтАЩ; another view is noted, whereby the pronoun тАШthis тАШiyam in ManuтАЩs text is taken as standing only for the first five sacraments, ending with Tonsure, so that Upanayaс╣Зa and Ke┼Ы─Бnta become excluded from the category. But this view is rejected; and in answer to the argument that тАЬin view of the declaration in the following verse that for women Marriage constitutes Upanayaс╣Зa, the pronoun тАШiyamтАЩ in the present verse must exclude Upanayaс╣ЗaтАФit is pointed out that all that the next verse means is that in the case of a person following the opinion of another Smс╣Ыti and not performing the Upanayana for his girl,тАФMarriage should be regarded as constituting her Upanayana; and not that in all cases Marriage should take the place of Upanayana. The conclusion is stated thus:тАФThere are two kinds of girlsтАФтАШBrahmav─Бdin─лтАЩ and тАШSodyovodh┼лтАЩ;тАФfor the former there is Upanayana, in the eighth year, vedic study, and тАШreturnтАЩ (completion of Vedic study) before puberty,тАФand marriage also before puberty; while for the Sodyovodh┼л, there is Upanayana at the time of marriage, followed by immediate тАШcompletion of study,тАЩ which is followed immediately by Marriage. But from the assertion in certain Smс╣Ыtis that there used to be Upanayana for women in a тАШprevious cycle,тАЩ it seems that in the present cycle, it is not to be performed. (Bee note on the next verse).

The above note regarding the two kinds of women is based on a passage in H─Бr─лta Smс╣Ыti (quoted in Madanap─Бrij─Бt─Б, p. 37), which adds that all this refers to another cycle. The exact words of H─Бr─лta mean as follows:тАФтАЬThere are two kinds of womenтАФBrahmav─Бdin─л and Sadyovadh┼л; for the former, there are Upanayana, fire-laying, vedic study in the house itself and also alms-begging; while for the latter, when the time of marriage arrives, Upanayana should be performed somehow and then marriage.тАЭ

This verse is quoted in Nс╣Ыsiс╣Гhapras─Бda (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 400);тАФand in Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 00) which explains тАШ─Бvс╣ЫtтАЩ as meaning the J─Бtakarma and other rites, and adds that this implies that none of the rites is to be omitted for the women.

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрд╛рдиреБрд╡рд╛рджрдГ

The ceremony called тАШUpanaya,тАЩ тАШInitiation,тАЩ has been called тАШVedic,тАЩ because it is gone through for the purpose of studying the Veda. This ceremony, in the case of females, consists of the тАШRites of marriage,тАЩтАФi.e., those rites that are accomplished by means of marriage. Thus, since тАШmarriageтАЩ has been prescribed for them in place of the тАШInitiation,тАЩ the former has been described here as becoming the latter; and this can preclude the necessity of тАШInitiationтАЩ only if the purposes of this latter were taken as served by the тАШmarriage.тАЩ

Objection.тАФтАЬWell, the Initiation may be excluded from women, but the study of the Veda and the keeping of the observances have still got to be performed.тАЭ

With a view to preclude these two also, the Text addsтАФ

тАШThe serving of husband is their residence with the Teacher.тАЩ When the woman servesтАФattends upon and reveres her husband, she does what is meant to bo accomplished by тАШResidence with the Teacher.тАЩ The study of the Veda could be done by the woman only if she resided with the Teacher; and as there is no тАШResidence with the TeacherтАЩ in her case, how can there be any studying of the Veda? тАШHousehold dutiesтАЩ;тАФall that she does in the course of her household work,тАФe.g., cooking, getting together of articles for household use, general supervision, and so forth, which are going to be described in discourse IX, тАШthe husband should employ her in saving wealth &c., &c.тАЩ (9.11). These household duties are for the woman what the тАШbringing of fuelтАЩ in the morning and evening is for the Religious Student (male). The term тАШtending of fireтАЩ stands for all the observances and vows that the student keeps.

By reason of the тАШMarriageтАЩ having taken the place of the тАШInitiatory CeremonyтАЩ (for women), it follows that, just as in the case of men, all the ordinances of ┼Ъruti and Smс╣Ыti and custom become binding upon him after the Initiatory Ceremony, before which they are free to do what they like, and are unfit for any religious duties,тАФso for women, there is freedom of action before Marriage, after which they become subject to the ordinances of ┼Ъrutis and Smс╣Ыtis.

Or, we may interpret the text as follows:тАФMarriage constitutes the Vedic SacramentтАФi.e., TJpanayanaтАФfor females; even though marriage is not really the Upanayana, yet it is spoken of as such attributively. The question arising as to whence lies the similarity by virtue of which Marriage is spoken of as Upanayana, the text addsтАФтАШthe serving of the husband &c., &c.тАЩтАФ(67)

The next verse sums up the contents of the sectionтАФ

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреНрдпрдГ

тАШVaiv─Бhikovidhiс╕етАЩтАФтАШSacrament performed with Vedic textsтАЩ (Nandana and R─Бghav─Бnanda);тАФтАШSacrament for the purpose of learning the VedaтАЩ (Medh─Бtithi and N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa).

This verse has been quot├зd in Gad─Бdharapaddhati (K─Бlas─Бra, p. 220) to the effect that for women Marriage itself is Upanayana;тАФin Smс╣Ыticandrik─Б (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 61), which notes that for women, тАШattendingтАЩ on husband takes the place of тАШservice of the teacher,тАЩ and тАШhousehold dutiesтАЩ take the place of тАШtending the fire,тАЩ and that for girls also, before marriage, there are no restrictions regarding food and other tilings;тАФand in V─лramitrodaya (Saс╣Гsk─Бra, pp. 403-4), where it is discussed along with the preceding verse (see note on 66). This verse has been taken as excluding women from Upanayana, entirely. But the author points out that this is not right; and he sets forth his well-considered opinion at the end (see note on 66); and the present verse he takes only as laying down a substitute for the Upanayana in the case of those women who are not Brahmav─Бdin─лs.

V─лramitrodaya proceeds to explain the verse to mean that тАШvaidikaс╕е saс╣Гsk─Бraс╕етАЩтАФтАШthe sacrament which is gone through for the purpose of studying the Veda,тАЩтАФi. e., UpanayanaтАФconsists, in the case of women, in the тАШrites of marriageтАЩ; i. e., consecration brought about by the marriage-rites, as has been тАЬdeclaredтАЩ by the ancients. It points out that such is the meaning of the verse with the words тАШSaс╣Гsk─Бro vaidikaс╕е smс╣Ыtaс╕етАЩ as read by Medh─Бtithi; but Mit─Бkс╣гar─Б and other works adopt the reading тАШaupan─Бyanikaс╕е smс╣Ыtaс╕етАЩ instead of тАШsaс╣Гsk─Бro vaidikaс╕е smс╣Ыtaс╕етАЩ, which means that marriage rites serve the purpose of Upanayana rite; so that marriage would be for women what Upanayana is for men.

This verse is quoted also in Madanap─Бrij─Бta (p. 37), which also adopts the reading тАШaupan─Бyanikaс╕е smс╣Ыtaс╕е.тАЩ

рдЧрдЩреНрдЧрд╛рдирде-рддреБрд▓реНрдп-рд╡рд╛рдХреНрдпрд╛рдирд┐

Viс╣гс╣Зu-Smс╣Ыti, 22.32.тАФтАШFor women Marriage is the sacrament.тАЩ

V├мsmt-Smс╣Ыti, 27-15.тАФтАШThe Marriage of women is with mantras.тАЩ

Y─Бj├▒avalkya, 1.13.тАФтАШFor women, Marriage is with mantras.тАЩ

Yama (V─лramitrodaya-Saс╣Гsk─Бra, p. 402).тАФтАШIn former times, for girls also there was Upanayana, also the teaching of the Veda and the pronouncing of the S─Бvitr─л. But she should be taught by her father, uncle or brother, none else. For the girl, alms-begging is to be done in her own home; and she should avoid the skin, the rags and also matted locks.тАЩ

B├╝hler

067 The nuptial ceremony is stated to be the Vedic sacrament for women (and to be equal to the initiation), serving the husband (equivalent to) the residence in (the house of the) teacher, and the household duties (the same) as the (daily) worship of the sacred fire.
